Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Khalwah Sahihah and Its Effect on Mahr
Ruling that valid seclusion followed by divorce gives full mahr; conditions invalidating seclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on khalwah sahihah to determine the mahr due upon subsequent divorce and identify which impediments invalidate the seclusion.

Core Idea
Valid seclusion without consummation confirms full mahr—the wife's takhliyah suffices.

This passage presents the Hanafi position on valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah) and its effect on mahr when followed by divorce. It also contrasts the Shafi'i view and details the conditions that make seclusion valid or invalid. Understanding this ruling is essential for correctly awarding mahr in marriage dissolution cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
Focus on the first part: when a man secludes with his wife with no impediment and then divorces her, she gets full mahr. This is the Hanafi position.
The ruling is based on the wife's delivery (takhliyah) of the usufruct.
2
Analyze the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that only half mahr is due because the usufruct is only fully received through actual intercourse. Understand his proof and its assumptions.
Shafi'i sees mahr as compensation for actual enjoyment.
3
Examine the Hanafi response and qiyas
The Hanafi school responds with an analogy to sale: just as a seller's delivery (takhliyah) makes the price obligatory, the wife's removal of impediments establishes her right to full mahr.
The Caliphs' decisions support this analogy.
4
List the conditions for valid seclusion
Identify the impediments that invalidate khalwah: sickness preventing intercourse, fasting in Ramadan, ihram, menstruation, etc. The passage details these.
Voluntary fasts and non-obligatory prayers do not invalidate seclusion.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi gives full mahr; Shafi'i gives half. Also, different impediments affect validity.
This is the key outcome of the dispute.

Source Text

واذا خلا الرجل بامرأته وليس هناك مانع من الوطى ثم طلقها فلها كمال المهر وقال الشافعي لها نصف المهر لان المعقود عليه انما يصير مستوفى بالوطى فلايتاكد المهردونه ولنا انها سلمت المبدل حيث رفعت الموانع وذلك وسعها فيتاكد حقها في البدل اعتبارا بالبيع ترجمہ اور جب خلوت کی مرد نے اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ اور وہاں کوئی مانع قطی بھی نہیں ہے پھر طلاق دی اس عورت کو تو اس کیلئے کامل مہر ہوگا۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ عورت کیلئے نصف مہر ہو گا اسلئے کہ معقود علیہ یعنی منافع بضع پوری طور پر وصول ہوتے ہیں دہلی سے لہذا بغیر ولی کے مہر مؤکد نہیں ہوگا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت نے مبدل سپرد کر دیا کیونکہ اس نے مواقع کو اٹھا دیا اور یہی اس کی وسعت میں تھا پس اس کا حق مؤکد ہو گا بدل میں قیاس کرتے ہوئے بیچ میں۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ خلوت صحیحہ کی اور بوقت خلوت کوئی مانع ولی بھی نہیں ہے۔ پھر شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کو طلاق دی تو ہمارے نزدیک عورت کیلئے کمال مہر ہوگا اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک نصف مہر ہوگا۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ منافع جمع پورے طور پر حاصل ہوتے ہیں ولی سے اور وطی پائی نہیں گئی تو گویا شوہر نے مبدل وصول نہیں کیا۔ لہذا شوہر پر بدل بھی واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ پس نتیجہ نکلا کہ بغیر ولی کے مہر مؤکد نہیں ہوتا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت نے منافع بضع یعنی مبدل کو شوہر کے حوالہ کر دیا۔ کیونکہ عورت نے تمام موانع کو اٹھا دیا ہے اور عورت کی قدرت میں اتنا ہی تھا، اس سے زائد نہیں ۔ پس جب عورت نے مبدل سپرد کر دیا تو عورت کا حق بدل میں ثابت ہوگا۔ اور وہ بدل مہر ہے۔ پس عورت کیلئے اس صورت میں کامل مہر واجب ہوگا۔ اور ہم قیاس کرتے ہیں۔ بیج پر بھی کہ جس طرح بائع اگر مبیع اور مشتری کے درمیان تخلیہ کر دے کہ مبیع کو لینے میں کوئی مانع نہ رہے تو بائع کی طرف سے یہ تسلیم مبیع ہوگی اور مشتری پریشن واجب ہوگا۔ ہمارے مذہب کی تائید خلفاء راشدین کے فیصلوں سے بھی ہوتی ہے۔ فیصلہ یہ ہے کہ ان من غلق بابا او ارخی ستر أفقد وجب المهر و وجبت العدۃ ۔ یعنی جس شخص نے دروازہ بند کر لیایا پردہ ڈال دیا تو مبر واجب ہو گا اور عدت واجب ہوگی ۔ ( عینی شرح ہدایہ ) خلوت صحیحہ کی شمار نہیں ہوگی وان كان احدهما مريضا او صائما في رمضان او محرما بحج فرض اونفل او بعمرة او كانت حائضا فليست الخلوة صحيحة حتى لو طلقها كان لها نصف المهرلان هذه الاشياء موانع اما المرض فالمرادمنه ما يمنع الجماع اویلحقه به ضرر وقيل مرضه لا يعرى عن تكسر وفتور وهذا التفصيل فى مرضها واماصوم رمضان لمايلزمه من القضاء والكفارة والاحرام لما يلزمه من الدم وفساد النسك والقضاء والحيض مانع طبعا و شرعا وان كان احدهما صائما تطوعا فلها المهر كله لانه يباح له الافطار من غير عذر في رواية المنتقى وهذا القول في المهر هو الصحيح وصوم القضاء والمنذور كالتطوع فى رواية لانه لا كفارة فيه والصلوة بمنزلة الصوم فرضها كفرضه ونفلها كنفله
And when a man secludes himself with his wife and there is no impediment to intercourse, then he divorces her, she gets the full mahr. Al-Shafi'i said: she gets half the mahr because the subject of the contract (usufruct of the vulva) is only fully received by intercourse, so the mahr is not confirmed without it. Our proof is that she handed over the substitute (mubdal) by removing the impediments, and that is within her capacity, so her right in the substitute is confirmed by analogy to sale. Commentary: If a man secludes himself with his wife (valid seclusion) and there is no impediment, then he divorces her, according to us she gets full mahr; according to Shafi'i half. Shafi'i's proof: the usufruct is only fully obtained by intercourse, and intercourse did not occur, so the husband received no substitute, thus no mahr is obligatory. Hence without intercourse, mahr is not confirmed. Our proof: the woman handed over the usufruct of the vulva (the substitute) to the husband by removing all impediments, and that is all she can do, so her right to the substitute (mahr) is established. We draw analogy to sale: if a seller gives delivery (takhliyah) of the commodity so that there is no impediment to the buyer taking it, then that constitutes delivery and the price becomes obligatory. Our school is also supported by the decisions of the Rightly Guided Caliphs: 'Whoever closes a door or draws a curtain, the mahr becomes obligatory and the waiting period becomes obligatory.' (Ayni Sharh Hidayah). Valid seclusion will not be counted if one of them is sick, or fasting in Ramadan, or in ihram for obligatory or voluntary Hajj or Umrah, or the woman is menstruating. So the seclusion is not valid, and if he divorces her, she gets half the mahr because these are impediments. As for sickness, what is meant is that which prevents intercourse or causes harm; it is said that his sickness is not free from weakness and lethargy, and this detail applies to her sickness. As for fasting in Ramadan, because it necessitates qada' and kaffarah; and ihram because it necessitates a dam (sacrifice), invalidation of the ritual, and qada'; and menstruation is a natural and legal impediment. And if one of them is observing a voluntary fast, she gets the full mahr because it is permissible to break the fast without excuse in one narration (al-Muntaqa), and this saying regarding mahr is the correct one. The fast of qada' and nadhr (vow) are like voluntary fast in one narration because there is no kaffarah in it. Prayer is like fasting: its obligatory form is like obligatory fasting, and its voluntary form like voluntary fasting.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage deals with the effect of valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah) on mahr. The Hanafi position: if a man secludes himself with his wife with no impediment to intercourse (such as illness, fasting, ihram, menstruation), and then divorces her, she is entitled to the full mahr. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, holding that she gets only half because actual consummation did not occur; the mahr is not confirmed without intercourse. The Hanafi proof: the wife has done everything in her power by removing impediments and making herself available; by analogy to a sale where delivery (takhliyah) by the seller makes the price obligatory, here the wife's takhliyah makes the mahr obligatory. This is supported by the decisions of the Rightly Guided Caliphs: closing the door or drawing a curtain makes mahr and 'iddah obligatory. The passage then lists conditions that invalidate seclusion: if either spouse is sick (to the extent preventing intercourse or causing harm), fasting in Ramadan (which requires qada' and kaffarah if broken), in ihram for Hajj or Umrah (which requires dam, invalidates the ritual, and qada'), or the woman is menstruating. In these cases, the seclusion is not valid, and divorce results in only half the mahr. However, if either is observing a voluntary fast, the full mahr is due because voluntary fast can be broken without penalty. Similarly, obligatory make-up fasts and vowed fasts are like voluntary in one narration due to no kaffarah. Prayer parallels fasting: obligatory prayer (like obligatory fast) invalidates seclusion, voluntary does not.

Key Terms
خلوت صحیحہ (khalwah sahihah): Valid seclusion where a husband and wife are alone with no legal or physical impediment to intercourse.
مانع (māni'): Any impediment that makes intercourse unlawful or harmful, such as fasting in Ramadan, ihram, menstruation, sickness.
مبدل (mubdal): The substitute; here refers to the usufruct of the vulva (manafi' al-bid') which is the subject matter of the marriage contract.
تخلیہ (takhliyah): Delivery of the sold item by removing impediments so that the buyer can take possession.
عدت (iddah): Waiting period after divorce before a woman can remarry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband secludes himself with his wife while she is observing a voluntary (nafl) fast and then divorces her. According to the Hanafi school, how much mahr is she entitled to?
A) Half mahr, because seclusion is invalid due to fasting.
B) Full mahr, because voluntary fast can be broken and is not an impediment.
C) No mahr, because the fast is valid and intercourse is prohibited.
D) Only mahr al-mithl, because the seclusion is irregular.

Key Takeaway
Valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah) without impediments entitles the wife to full mahr upon divorce, based on the principle of takhliyah and the decisions of the Caliphs.

Full vs Half Mahr After Valid Seclusion: Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Inter-madhab dispute: full vs half mahr after khalwah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on mahr after khalwah sahihah without intercourse, explain the Hanafi proof based on qiyas and the Caliphs' ruling, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Valid seclusion equals delivery of marital benefit, obligating full mahr in Hanafi law.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a classical inter-madhab dispute: when a husband divorces his wife after valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah) but without actual intercourse, how much mahr is due? The Hanafi school rules that the full mahr is wajib, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds that only half is due. The difference hinges on who delivers the marital benefit and what constitutes delivery. We will unpack each side's proof and see how the Hanafis draw a powerful analogy from sale transactions.

Guided Path
1
State the disputed issue
Identify the precise scenario: husband divorces wife after valid seclusion without intercourse. What is the mahr obligation?
The dispute is about the amount, not the existence of mahr.
2
Analyze each school's position and dalil
Extract the Hanafi position (full mahr) and the Shafi'i position (half mahr). Then identify the proof each school presents.
Shafi'i: benefit is from guardian, no intercourse → no full mahr. Hanafi: woman delivered herself by removing obstacles.
3
Examine the Hanafi qiyas on sale
Understand the analogy: in a sale, when the seller gives possession (takhliyah) of the item, the price becomes due even without physical handling. Similarly, the wife gives possession of the marital benefit via khalwah.
The illa is 'delivery by removing obstacles'.
4
Consider the Caliphs' ruling
The Hanafis cite a ruling of the Rightly Guided Caliphs: 'Whoever closed a door or lowered a curtain, full mahr and 'iddah become obligatory.' This serves as a corroborating evidence.
This is a qawl sahabi, a source of law in Hanafi usul.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Hanafi law, the wife receives full mahr; under Shafi'i law, she receives half. This can affect financial planning in marriage contracts.
The student should appreciate why this difference matters for fatwa and litigation.

Source Text

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم
کتاب النکاح بیوی کو طلاق دی تو ہمارے نزدیک عورت کیلئے کمال مہر ہوگا اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک نصف مہر ہوگا۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ منافع بضع [؟] پورے طور پر حاصل ہوتے ہیں ولی سے اور وطی پائی نہیں گئی تو گویا شوہر نے مبدل وصول نہیں کیا۔ لہذا شوہر پر بدل بھی واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ پس نتیجہ نکلا کہ بغیر ولی کے مہر مؤکد نہیں ہوتا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت نے منافع بضع یعنی مبدل کو شوہر کے حوالہ کر دیا۔ کیونکہ عورت نے تمام موانع کو اٹھا دیا ہے اور عورت کی قدرت میں اتنا ہی تھا، اس سے زائد نہیں ۔ پس جب عورت نے مبدل سپرد کر دیا تو عورت کا حق بدل میں ثابت ہوگا۔ اور وہ بدل مہر ہے۔ پس عورت کیلئے اس صورت میں کامل مہر واجب ہوگا۔ اور ہم قیاس کرتے ہیں۔ بیج پر بھی کہ جس طرح بائع اگر مبیع اور مشتری کے درمیان تخلیہ کر دے کہ مبیع کو لینے میں کوئی مانع نہ رہے تو بائع کی طرف سے یہ تسلیم مبیع ہوگی اور مشتری پر ثمن [؟] واجب ہوگا۔ ہمارے مذہب کی تائید خلفاء راشدین کے فیصلوں سے بھی ہوتی ہے۔ فیصلہ یہ ہے کہ ان من غلق بابا او ارخی ستر أفقد وجب المهر و وجبت العدۃ ۔ یعنی جس شخص نے دروازہ بند کر لیایا پردہ ڈال دیا تو مبر واجب ہو گا اور عدت واجب ہوگی ۔ ( عینی شرح ہدایہ )
Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah Volume 4. Book of Nikah: If one divorces his wife, then according to us (Hanafis) the full mahr is obligatory for the woman, and according to Imam al-Shafi'i, half mahr will be obligatory. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that the benefits of the vulva are obtained in full from the guardian, and intercourse did not take place, so it is as if the husband did not receive the substitute. Therefore, the substitute is not obligatory on the husband. Thus the conclusion is that without the guardian, the mahr is not binding. Our proof is that the woman handed over the benefit of the vulva, i.e., the substitute, to the husband. Because the woman removed all obstacles, and this was within her capacity, nothing more. So when the woman delivered the substitute, her right to the substitute is established. And that substitute is the mahr. So in this case, the full mahr is obligatory on the husband. And we make an analogy on a seed: just as when a seller gives possession between the sold item and the buyer, so that there is no obstacle to taking the sold item, then from the seller's side this is delivery of the sold item, and the price becomes obligatory on the buyer. Our school is also supported by the judgments of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. The judgment is: 'Whoever closed a door or lowered a curtain, then the mahr becomes obligatory and the 'iddah becomes obligatory.' (Ayni Sharh al-Hidayah)
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the amount of mahr when a husband divorces his wife after valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah) without actual intercourse. The Hanafi position is that the full mahr is due, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds that only half is due. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that the benefit of the vulva is fully obtained only from the guardian (wali), and since intercourse did not occur, the husband did not receive the substitute (badal) from the wife. Therefore, no substitute (mahr) is due. The Hanafi response is that the woman herself delivered the benefit by removing all obstacles (e.g., making herself available), and this is within her capacity. By analogy to a sale contract where the seller gives possession (takhliyah) of the sold item to the buyer, the price becomes due even if the buyer does not physically take it. Here, the wife gave possession of the benefit of her vulva by removing all barriers, so the mahr becomes due. Additionally, the Hanafis cite the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs, who ruled that merely closing a door or lowering a curtain (indicating seclusion) obligates the full mahr and the 'iddah. This passage sets forth the Hanafi position with its proofs and rebuts the Shafi'i argument, concluding that the full mahr is obligatory.

Key Terms
خلوت صحیحہ (khalwah sahihah): Valid seclusion between spouses that is legally equivalent to intercourse in rulings such as mahr and 'iddah.
مہر (mahr): Dower, obligatory payment from husband to wife upon marriage or upon divorce if marriage was consummated.
منافع بضع (manafi' al-bud'): Benefits of the vulva, the marital benefit that the wife provides to the husband.
مبدل (badal): Substitute, the consideration in a contract, here referring to the benefit of the vulva.
تخلیہ (takhliyah): Giving possession by removing physical barriers, so that the buyer can take the item.
تسلیم (taslim): Delivery, the act of handing over the sold item to the buyer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on mahr if a husband divorces his wife after valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah) but before intercourse?
A) Half mahr is due because no intercourse occurred
B) Full mahr is due because the wife delivered the benefit by removing obstacles
C) No mahr is due because the marriage was not consummated
D) Full mahr is due only if the wife was a virgin

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah) is sufficient to obligate the full mahr upon divorce, even without intercourse, because the wife has delivered the benefit of the vulva.

Major Obstacles to Valid Seclusion and Their Effect on Mahr
List of obstacles invalidating khalwah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the major obstacles that invalidate khalwah and apply the ruling that only half mahr is due upon divorce when an obstacle is present.

Core Idea
If an obstacle to intercourse exists during seclusion, the khalwah is invalid and only half mahr is due upon divorce.

In Hanafi fiqh, valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah) between spouses after a valid marriage has legal consequences for mahr. However, certain obstacles render the seclusion invalid (khalwah fasidah), changing the mahr obligation. This lesson unpacks the four main obstacles listed in al-Hidayah: illness, fasting in Ramadan, ihram, and menstruation, and explains how each affects the mahr upon divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its consequence
Recognize that the ruling concerns khalwah (seclusion) after marriage. If khalwah is sahihah and divorce occurs, full mahr is due. If invalid, only half mahr is due.
2
List the four obstacles
From the text: illness (of either spouse), fasting in Ramadan, ihram for hajj or 'umrah, and menstruation. These are the primary obstacles mentioned.
Illness has a condition: only if it prevents intercourse or causes harm.
3
Check each obstacle's type
Classify each as natural, legal, or both. Menstruation is both natural and legal; ihram is legal; illness is natural (conditioned).
This classification helps understand the reasoning behind the ruling.
4
Apply the ruling
If any obstacle was present during seclusion, then upon divorce the wife receives half the mahr. If no obstacle, full mahr.
The burden of proof lies on the husband to show an obstacle existed.

Source Text

وان كان احدهما مريضا او صائما في رمضان او محرما بحج فرض اونفل او بعمرة او كانت حائضا فليست الخلوة صحيحة حتى لو طلقها كان لها نصف المهرلان هذه الاشياء موانع اما المرض فالمرادمنه ما يمنع الجماع اویلحقه به ضرر وقيل مرضه لا يعرى عن تكسر وفتور وهذا التفصيل فى مرضها واماصوم رمضان لمايلزمه من القضاء والكفارة والاحرام لما يلزمه من الدم وفساد النسك والقضاء والحيض مانع طبعا و شرعا وان كان احدهما صائما تطوعا فلها المهر كله لانه يباح له الافطار من غير عذر في رواية المنتقى وهذا القول في المهر هو الصحيح وصوم القضاء والمنذور كالتطوع فى رواية لانه لا كفارة فيه والصلوة بمنزلة الصوم فرضها كفرضه ونفلها كنفله
ترجمہ اور اگر ان دونوں میں سے ایک بیمار ہے یا رمضان میں روزے سے ہے یا حج کا احرام باندھے ہوئے ہے۔ حج فرض ہو یا نفل یا عمرہ کا احرام ہے یا حائضہ ہے تو خلوت صحیح نہیں ہے۔ حتی کہ اگر طلاق دے دی اس عورت کو تو اس کیلئے نصف مہر ہو گا اس لیئے کہ یہ چیزیں مانع وطی نہیں۔ بہر حال مرض تو مراد اس سے یہ ہے کہ مانع جماع ہو یا اس مرض سے اس کو ضر ر لاحق ہوتا ہو۔ اور کہا گیا کہ مرد کا مرض اعضاء چکنی اور ستی سے خالی نہیں اور یہ تفصیل عورت کے مرض میں ہے۔ بہر حال روزہ رمضان تو اس لئے کہ صوم رمضان کی وجہ سے اس کو قضاء اور کفارہ لازم ہوگا۔ اور احرام کیونکہ اس کی وجہ سے اس کو دم اور فساد حج اور قضاء لازم ہوگی ۔ اور حیض مانع طبعی اور شرعی دونوں ہے اور اگر ان دونوں میں سے ایک نفل روزے سے ہے تو عورت کیلئے کامل مہر ہو گا۔ اسلئے کہ اس کیلئے افطار مباح ہے بغیر عذر کے مشتقی کی روایت میں اور یہ قول مہر کے سلسلے میں ہے یہی صحیح ہے اور قضاء اور نذر کا روز نفلی روزہ کے مانند ہے ایک روایت میں ۔ اسلئے کہ اس میں کفار نہیں اور نماز روزہ کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔ فرض نماز فرض روزے کے مانند ہے اور نفل نماز نفلی روزے کے مانند ہے۔ تشریح سابق میں یہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ خلوت کی دوقسمیں ہیں۔ خلوت صحیحہ اور خلوت فاسدہ اگر کوئی کسی قسم کامانع پلی موجود ہے تو ایسی صورت میں جو خلوت ہو گی خلوت فاسدہ کہلائے گی۔ اور اگر مانع ولی نہ پایا جائے تو ایسی صورت میں جو خلوت ہوگی خلوت صحیحہ ہوگی۔
موانع چند قسم پر ہیں،
مانع طبعی
(۴) مانع حسی
ا مانع حقیقی ،
نافع شرعی ،
مانع حقیقی کی مثال مرض ہے اور مانع طبعی اور مانع شرعی کی مثال حیض ہے۔ حیض مانع طبعی تو اسلئے ہے کہ اس میں حیض کے خون کے ساتھ تلویث ہوگی جس کو طبیعت سلیمہ پسند نہیں کرتی ۔ اور مانع شرعی اسلئے ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرما یاولا تـقـربــوا هــن حتى يطهرن اور صرف مانع طبعی کی مثال رتقاء ہونا ہے یعنی عورت کی شرمگاہ کے منہ کا بند ہونا۔ یا ایسی صغیرہ ہونا جو جماع کے قابل نہ ہو۔ اور صرف مانع شرعی کی مثال۔ حج فرض کا احرام ہے اور مانع حسی یہ ہے کہ زوجین کے مکان میں کوئی تیسر ا بھی موجود ہو بینا ہو یا نا بینان بیدار ہو یا سویا ہوا۔ بالغ ہو یا سمجھدار بچہ۔ صاحب ہدایہ موانع کی تفصیل ذکر کرنا چاہتے ہیں۔ چنانچہ سب سے پہلے فرمایا کہ مرض مانع ہے۔ لیکن مرض سے وہ مرض مراد ہے جو مانع جماع ہو یا جماع کرنے سے ضرر لاحق ہوتا ہو مطلقا مرض مراد نہیں ہے اور بعض کی رائے یہ ہے کہ مرد کا مرض مطلقا مانع ہے۔ کیونکہ مطلقا مرض سے اعضاء شکنی اور ستی رہتی ہے۔ لہذا مرد میں جماع کیلئے نشاط پیدا نہیں ہوگا۔ اس وجہ سے مرد کے مطلقا مرض کو مانع قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ اور مرض کی جو تقسیم کی ہے وہ عورت کے مرض میں ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ عورت کا مرض بلا اختلاف منقسم ہے۔ اور مرد کا مرض ایک رائے کے مطابق منقسم ہے۔ اور ایک رائے یہ ہے کہ مرد کا مرض غیر منقسم ہے اور مرد کا مرض ہر حال میں خلوت صحیحہ کیلئے مانع ہے۔ اور رمضان کا روزہ بھی خلوت صحیحہ کیلئے مانع ہے کیونکہ رمضان کے روزے کی حالت میں اگر وطی کی گئی تو قضا اور کفارہ واجب ہوگا اور ساتھ ساتھ گنہ گار ہوگا۔ اور ظاہر ہے کہ ان چیزوں میں حرج ہے۔ لہذا صوم رمضان بھی مانع خلوت ہوگا اور احرام اسلئے مانع خلوت ہے کہ اگر بحالت احرام جماع کیا گیا تو محرم پر دم واجب ہوگا۔ یعنی بکری یا اونٹ کا ذبح کرنا واجب ہوگا اور عبادت حج فاسد ہوگی ۔ اور قضا واجب ہو گی۔ ظاہر ہے کہ ان چیزوں میں بھی حرج ہے لہذا احرام بھی مانع خلوت ہوگا ۔ اور حیض اسلئے مانع ہے کہ حیض کی حالت میں وطی کرنا طبعا بھی ممنوع ہے اور شرعاً بھی جیسا کہ پہلے گزر چکا۔ اور اگر احد الزوجین نفلی روزے ہے ہے اور خلوت پائی گئی تو عورت کیلئے کامل مہر ہو گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ مصنف نے صوم نفل کو مانع صحت خلوت شمار نہیں کیا ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ متقی مصنفہ حاکم الشہید ابوالفضل کی روایت کے مطابق نفلی روزہ کو بلا عذرا افطار کرنا مباح ہے۔ لہذا جب نفلی روزے کے افطار میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے تو اس کو مانع خلوت قرار نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ منتقی کی اس روایت کو صرف کامل وجوب مہر کے سلسلہ میں صحیح مانا ہے۔ ورنہ بعض حضرات کی رائے یہ ہے کہ نفلی روزہ بھی خلوت صحیحہ کیلئے مانع ہے۔ اسلئے سر نفلی روزہ کو بغیر عذر کے باطل کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔
رہا قضاء اور نذر کا روزہ سواس بارے میں دو روایات ہیں ایک یہ کہ صوم نفل اس طرح صوم قضا اور صوم منذ ور بھی مانع صحت خلوت نہیں ہے۔ دوسری روایت یہ کہ صوم رمضان کی طرح خلوت صحیحہ کے لئے مانع ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ صوم رمضان کی حالت میں وطی کرنے سے کفارہ بھی واجب ہوتا تھا اور گناہ بھی اور صوم قضا اور صوم منذور کی حالت میں اگر وہی کی جائے تو گنہگار ہو گا لیکن کفارہ واجب نہیں ہو
If one of the two (spouses) is sick, or fasting in Ramadan, or in ihram for hajj (obligatory or voluntary) or for 'umrah, or the woman is menstruating, then the khalwah is not valid, so that if he divorces her, she gets half the mahr, because these things are obstacles. As for sickness: what is meant is that which prevents intercourse or causes harm. It is said that his sickness is not free from weakness and languor, and this detail is in her sickness. As for the fast of Ramadan: because of the obligation of qada' and kaffarah (if intercourse occurs during it). As for ihram: because of the obligation of blood (dam), invalidation of the ritual, and qada'. Menstruation is an obstacle by nature and by law. If one of them is voluntarily fasting, then she gets full mahr, because it is permissible for him to break the fast without excuse according to the narration of al-Muntaqa, and this statement regarding the mahr is the correct one. The fast of qada' and nadhr (vows) is like voluntary fasting in one narration, because there is no kaffarah in it. Prayer is like fasting: its obligatory (prayer) is like obligatory fasting, and its voluntary is like voluntary fasting. Translation: And if one of the two is sick, or fasting in Ramadan, or has assumed ihram for hajj (obligatory or voluntary) or for 'umrah, or the woman is menstruating, then the khalwah is not valid, so that if he divorces that woman, she gets half the mahr, because these things are obstacles to intercourse... (continued with explanation). ...The gist: the author did not consider voluntary fasting as an obstacle to the validity of khalwah... As for the fast of qada' and nadhr, there are two narrations: one that they are like voluntary fasting in not being obstacles, and another that they are like the fast of Ramadan in being obstacles. The gist: during the fast of Ramadan, if intercourse occurs, kaffarah is obligatory along with sin; during qada' and nadhr fasts, if intercourse occurs, the person sins but kaffarah is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah explains the obstacles (mawani') that prevent khalwah from being considered valid (sahihah). When khalwah is invalid, if the husband divorces the wife, only half the mahr is due. The obstacles are categorized: (1) illness that prevents intercourse or causes harm, (2) fasting in Ramadan, (3) being in ihram for hajj or 'umrah, (4) menstruation. The passage also discusses details: for illness, there are two opinions regarding the husband's illness—some say it is always an obstacle, others distinguish. For the wife's illness, it is divided. For fasting, the Ramadan fast is an obstacle because it entails qada' and kaffarah if intercourse occurs. For ihram, it entails dam (sacrificial animal), invalidation of the ritual, and qada'. Menstruation is both a natural and a legal obstacle. Voluntary (nafl) fasting is not considered an obstacle according to the narration of al-Muntaqa quoted in al-Hidayah, because it is permissible to break a voluntary fast without excuse. The author of al-Hidayah accepts this narration specifically regarding the obligation of full mahr. However, some other scholars hold that even a voluntary fast is an obstacle, so breaking it without excuse is not correct. For the fast of qada' (make-up) and nadhr (vowed fast), there are two narrations: one treats them like voluntary fasts (no obstacle), the other treats them like Ramadan fasts (obstacle). The practical difference: with Ramadan fast, intercourse incurs both sin and kaffarah; with qada' and nadhr fasts, it incurs sin but no kaffarah. The passage then categorizes obstacles into natural (tabi'i), legal (shar'i), and sensory (hissi), with examples like ratq (sealed vagina) as natural, ihram as legal, and a third person present as sensory. This detailed classification helps understand the conditions for valid khalwah.

Key Terms
خلوت فاسدہ (khalwah fasidah): Invalid seclusion that occurs when an obstacle (man'i) is present; upon divorce, only half mahr is due
مانع طبعی (mani' tabi'i): Natural obstacle, e.g., menstruation (due to blood) or ratq (sealed vagina)
مانع شرعی (mani' shar'i): Legal obstacle, e.g., ihram, Ramadan fast, which are prohibited by Sharia
مانع حسی (mani' hissi): Sensory obstacle, e.g., presence of a third person in the room

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT an obstacle to valid khalwah according to the passage?
A) Menstruation
B) Voluntary (nafl) fasting
C) Ihram for hajj
D) Ramadan fast

Key Takeaway
The presence of any of the four major obstacles (illness preventing intercourse, Ramadan fast, ihram, menstruation) makes khalwah invalid, resulting in only half mahr upon divorce.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
Classification of Obstacles and the Ruling on Voluntary and Make-up Fasts
Expansion on the ruling for voluntary and other fasts, and classification of obstacles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between voluntary, make-up, and vowed fasts regarding their effect on khalwah, and identify the three categories of obstacles (natural, legal, sensory).

Core Idea
Voluntary fasts are not an obstacle to valid khalwah, and obstacles are classified as natural, legal, or sensory.

While Ramadan fast is a clear obstacle, not all fasts carry the same weight. The Hanafi school has a nuanced view on voluntary (nafl), make-up (qada'), and vowed (nadhr) fasts. Additionally, the commentators classify obstacles into three types to help understand the underlying reasoning. This lesson explores these finer points and the intra-madhhab differences.

Guided Path
1
Recall the rule for Ramadan fast
Ramadan fast is an obstacle because of qada' and kaffarah. This is the baseline.
2
Identify the ruling for nafil fast
The passage says if one spouse is voluntarily fasting, the full mahr is due because it is permissible to break it without excuse. This is the preferred view.
Some Hanafis disagree and consider nafil an obstacle.
3
Understand the ikhtilaf on qada' and nadhr fasts
Two narrations: one treats them like nafil (no obstacle), another like Ramadan (obstacle). The difference is the presence of kaffarah: Ramadan has it, qada'/nadhr do not.
The mufta bihi is that they are not obstacles.
4
Learn the three categories of obstacles
Natural (tabi'i): e.g., ratq (sealed vagina). Legal (shar'i): e.g., ihram, Ramadan fast. Sensory (hissi): e.g., third person present. Menstruation is both natural and legal.
This classification helps in analogizing new cases.

حج فرض کا احرام ہے اور مانع حسی یہ ہے کہ زوجین کے مکان میں کوئی تیسر ا بھی موجود ہو بینا ہو یا نا بینان بیدار ہو یا سویا ہوا۔ بالغ ہو یا سمجھدار بچہ۔ صاحب ہدایہ موانع کی تفصیل ذکر کرنا چاہتے ہیں۔ چنانچہ سب سے پہلے فرمایا کہ مرض مانع ہے۔ لیکن مرض سے وہ مرض مراد ہے جو مانع جماع ہو یا جماع کرنے سے ضرر لاحق ہوتا ہو مطلقا مرض مراد نہیں ہے اور بعض کی رائے یہ ہے کہ مرد کا مرض مطلقا مانع ہے۔ کیونکہ مطلقا مرض سے اعضاء شکنی اور ستی رہتی ہے۔ لہذا مرد میں جماع کیلئے نشاط پیدا نہیں ہوگا۔ اس وجہ سے مرد کے مطلقا مرض کو مانع قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ اور مرض کی جو تقسیم کی ہے وہ عورت کے مرض میں ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ عورت کا مرض بلا اختلاف منقسم ہے۔ اور مرد کا مرض ایک رائے کے مطابق منقسم ہے۔ اور ایک رائے یہ ہے کہ مرد کا مرض غیر منقسم ہے اور مرد کا مرض ہر حال میں خلوت صحیحہ کیلئے مانع ہے۔ اور رمضان کا روزہ بھی خلوت صحیحہ کیلئے مانع ہے کیونکہ رمضان کے روزے کی حالت میں اگر وطی کی گئی تو قضا اور کفارہ واجب ہوگا اور ساتھ ساتھ گنہ گار ہوگا۔ اور ظاہر ہے کہ ان چیزوں میں حرج ہے۔ لہذا صوم رمضان بھی مانع خلوت ہوگا اور احرام اسلئے مانع خلوت ہے کہ اگر بحالت احرام جماع کیا گیا تو محرم پر دم واجب ہوگا۔ یعنی بکری یا اونٹ کا ذبح کرنا واجب ہوگا اور عبادت حج فاسد ہوگی ۔ اور قضا واجب ہو گی۔ ظاہر ہے کہ ان چیزوں میں بھی حرج ہے لہذا احرام بھی مانع خلوت ہوگا ۔ اور حیض اسلئے مانع ہے کہ حیض کی حالت میں وطی کرنا طبعا بھی ممنوع ہے اور شرعاً بھی جیسا کہ پہلے گزر چکا۔ اور اگر احد الزوجین نفلی روزے ہے ہے اور خلوت پائی گئی تو عورت کیلئے کامل مہر ہو گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ مصنف نے صوم نفل کو مانع صحت خلوت شمار نہیں کیا ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ متقی مصنفہ حاکم الشہید ابوالفضل کی روایت کے مطابق نفلی روزہ کو بلا عذرا افطار کرنا مباح ہے۔ لہذا جب نفلی روزے کے افطار میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے تو اس کو مانع خلوت قرار نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ منتقی کی اس روایت کو صرف کامل وجوب مہر کے سلسلہ میں صحیح مانا ہے۔ ورنہ بعض حضرات کی رائے یہ ہے کہ نفلی روزہ بھی خلوت صحیحہ کیلئے مانع ہے۔ اسلئے سر نفلی روزہ کو بغیر عذر کے باطل کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔
رہا قضاء اور نذر کا روزہ سواس بارے میں دو روایات ہیں ایک یہ کہ صوم نفل اس طرح صوم قضا اور صوم منذ ور بھی مانع صحت خلوت نہیں ہے۔ دوسری روایت یہ کہ صوم رمضان کی طرح خلوت صحیحہ کے لئے مانع ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ صوم رمضان کی حالت میں وطی کرنے سے کفارہ بھی واجب ہوتا تھا اور گناہ بھی اور صوم قضا اور صوم منذور کی حالت میں اگر وہی کی جائے تو گنہگار ہو گا لیکن کفارہ واجب نہیں ہو
If one of the two (spouses) is sick, or fasting in Ramadan, or in ihram for hajj (obligatory or voluntary) or for 'umrah, or the woman is menstruating, then the khalwah is not valid, so that if he divorces her, she gets half the mahr, because these things are obstacles. As for sickness: what is meant is that which prevents intercourse or causes harm. It is said that his sickness is not free from weakness and languor, and this detail is in her sickness. As for the fast of Ramadan: because of the obligation of qada' and kaffarah (if intercourse occurs during it). As for ihram: because of the obligation of blood (dam), invalidation of the ritual, and qada'. Menstruation is an obstacle by nature and by law. If one of them is voluntarily fasting, then she gets full mahr, because it is permissible for him to break the fast without excuse according to the narration of al-Muntaqa, and this statement regarding the mahr is the correct one. The fast of qada' and nadhr (vows) is like voluntary fasting in one narration, because there is no kaffarah in it. Prayer is like fasting: its obligatory (prayer) is like obligatory fasting, and its voluntary is like voluntary fasting. Translation: And if one of the two is sick, or fasting in Ramadan, or has assumed ihram for hajj (obligatory or voluntary) or for 'umrah, or the woman is menstruating, then the khalwah is not valid, so that if he divorces that woman, she gets half the mahr, because these things are obstacles to intercourse... (continued with explanation). ...The gist: the author did not consider voluntary fasting as an obstacle to the validity of khalwah... As for the fast of qada' and nadhr, there are two narrations: one that they are like voluntary fasting in not being obstacles, and another that they are like the fast of Ramadan in being obstacles. The gist: during the fast of Ramadan, if intercourse occurs, kaffarah is obligatory along with sin; during qada' and nadhr fasts, if intercourse occurs, the person sins but kaffarah is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah explains the obstacles (mawani') that prevent khalwah from being considered valid (sahihah). When khalwah is invalid, if the husband divorces the wife, only half the mahr is due. The obstacles are categorized: (1) illness that prevents intercourse or causes harm, (2) fasting in Ramadan, (3) being in ihram for hajj or 'umrah, (4) menstruation. The passage also discusses details: for illness, there are two opinions regarding the husband's illness—some say it is always an obstacle, others distinguish. For the wife's illness, it is divided. For fasting, the Ramadan fast is an obstacle because it entails qada' and kaffarah if intercourse occurs. For ihram, it entails dam (sacrificial animal), invalidation of the ritual, and qada'. Menstruation is both a natural and a legal obstacle. Voluntary (nafl) fasting is not considered an obstacle according to the narration of al-Muntaqa quoted in al-Hidayah, because it is permissible to break a voluntary fast without excuse. The author of al-Hidayah accepts this narration specifically regarding the obligation of full mahr. However, some other scholars hold that even a voluntary fast is an obstacle, so breaking it without excuse is not correct. For the fast of qada' (make-up) and nadhr (vowed fast), there are two narrations: one treats them like voluntary fasts (no obstacle), the other treats them like Ramadan fasts (obstacle). The practical difference: with Ramadan fast, intercourse incurs both sin and kaffarah; with qada' and nadhr fasts, it incurs sin but no kaffarah. The passage then categorizes obstacles into natural (tabi'i), legal (shar'i), and sensory (hissi), with examples like ratq (sealed vagina) as natural, ihram as legal, and a third person present as sensory. This detailed classification helps understand the conditions for valid khalwah.

Key Terms
صوم نفل (sawm nafil): Voluntary fasting, which is not considered an obstacle to khalwah according to the preferred Hanafi view
صوم قضاء (sawm qada'): Make-up fast for missed obligatory fasts; its status as an obstacle is disputed within the school
صوم منذور (sawm nadhr): Vowed fast; same ruling as qada' fast in terms of being an obstacle
منتقى (al-Muntaqa): A collection of hadith and legal narrations by al-Hakim al-Shahid, used as a source for the nafil exception

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason a voluntary (nafl) fast is not considered an obstacle to valid khalwah?
A) Because it is not an obligatory act of worship
B) Because it can be broken without excuse according to al-Muntaqa
C) Because it does not require qada' if broken
D) Because the wife's fast does not affect the husband's rights

Key Takeaway
Voluntary, make-up, and vowed fasts are generally not obstacles to khalwah, because breaking them does not incur kaffarah, unlike the Ramadan fast.

The Four Types of Obstacles to Valid Seclusion
Classification of obstacles that invalidate or validate khalwah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the four types of obstacles (mawani‘) to valid khalwah and determine whether a given seclusion is sahihah or fasidah.

Core Idea
Valid khalwah requires the absence of any natural, sensory, real, or legal obstacle to intercourse.

In Hanafi fiqh, seclusion (khalwah) between spouses after a valid marriage can trigger the full mahr obligation, but only if it is unencumbered by any impediment. This passage from the chapter on marriage classifies the obstacles that render khalwah invalid. Understanding these categories is essential for correctly applying the rule that valid khalwah is equivalent to actual intercourse for legal purposes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two outcomes of khalwah
The passage states that khalwah is either sahihah (valid) or fasidah (invalid). Valid seclusion triggers full mahr; invalid gives half mahr.
2
Determine the condition for valid khalwah
Valid seclusion requires that no obstacle (man‘) be present.
3
List the four types of obstacles
Natural (tabi‘i), sensory (hissi), real (haqiqi), and legal (shar‘i). Note their definitions.
4
Analyze examples for each type
Menstruation is both natural and legal; ratqa‘ is only natural; ihram is only legal; presence of a third person is sensory. Illness is real.
5
Apply the classification to a hypothetical scenario
Given a scenario, determine if khalwah is valid or invalid by checking for any man‘.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح صورت میں جو خلوت ہو گی خلوت فاسدہ کہلائے گی۔ اور اگر مانع ولی نہ پایا جائے تو ایسی صورت میں جو خلوت ہوگی خلوت صحیحہ ہوگی۔
موانع چند قسم پر ہیں،
مانع طبعی
(۴) مانع حسی
ا مانع حقیقی ،
نافع شرعی ،
مانع حقیقی کی مثال مرض ہے اور مانع طبعی اور مانع شرعی کی مثال حیض ہے۔ حیض مانع طبعی تو اسلئے ہے کہ اس میں حیض کے خون کے ساتھ تلویث ہوگی جس کو طبیعت سلیمہ پسند نہیں کرتی ۔ اور مانع شرعی اسلئے ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرما یاولا تـقـربــوا هــن حتى يطهرن اور صرف مانع طبعی کی مثال رتقاء ہونا ہے یعنی عورت کی شرمگاہ کے منہ کا بند ہونا۔ یا ایسی صغیرہ ہونا جو جماع کے قابل نہ ہو۔ اور صرف مانع شرعی کی مثال۔ حج فرض کا احرام ہے اور مانع حسی یہ ہے کہ زوجین کے مکان میں کوئی تیسر ا بھی موجود ہو بینا ہو یا نا بینان بیدار ہو یا سویا ہوا۔ بالغ ہو یا سمجھدار بچہ۔
Book of Marriage: In this situation, the seclusion (khalwah) will be called invalid (fasidah). And if no obstacle (man') is found, then in that situation the seclusion will be valid (sahihah). Obstacles are of several types: natural obstacle (mani' tabi'i), sensory obstacle (mani' hissi), real obstacle (mani' haqiqi), legal obstacle (mani' shar'i). An example of a real obstacle is illness. An example of both natural and legal obstacle is menstruation. Menstruation is a natural obstacle because of the defilement from menstrual blood that a healthy nature dislikes. It is a legal obstacle because Allah says: 'And do not approach them until they are pure.' An example of only a natural obstacle is ratqa' (blocked vagina) or a minor girl not capable of intercourse. An example of only a legal obstacle is ihram for obligatory Hajj. A sensory obstacle is when a third person is present in the spouses' home, whether sighted or blind, awake or asleep, adult or discerning child.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of valid (sahihah) and invalid (fasidah) khalwah (seclusion) in Hanafi fiqh. Khalwah is considered valid only when there is no obstacle (man') that prevents the possibility of actual intercourse. The author classifies obstacles into four types: natural (tabi'i), sensory (hissi), real (haqiqi), and legal (shar'i). Illness is a real obstacle; menstruation is both natural (due to blood) and legal (due to Quranic prohibition). A blocked vagina (ratqa') or a minor girl too young for intercourse are purely natural obstacles. Ihram for obligatory Hajj is a purely legal obstacle. A sensory obstacle is the presence of a third person in the house, regardless of their sight, wakefulness, or age, as long as they are discerning. This classification is essential for determining whether khalwah triggers the full mahr obligation.

Key Terms
خلوت صحیحہ (khalwah sahīhah): Valid seclusion between husband and wife with no impediment to intercourse, which makes the full mahr obligatory upon divorce or death.
مانع (māni'): Any factor that prevents the khalwah from being considered valid, thereby preventing the full mahr obligation.
خلوت فاسدہ (khalwah fāsidah): Seclusion that occurs in the presence of a man', which does not trigger full mahr; only half mahr is due upon divorce.
رتقاء (ratqā'): A medical condition where the female genital opening is blocked, making intercourse impossible. It is a natural obstacle.
إحرام (ihrām): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, during which sexual intercourse is prohibited. It is a legal obstacle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of obstacle (man') is menstruation classified as in Hanafi fiqh?
A) Only natural (tabi'i)
B) Only legal (shar'i)
C) Both natural and legal
D) Real (haqiqi)

Key Takeaway
Valid khalwah requires that no natural, sensory, real, or legal obstacle prevents the possibility of intercourse; otherwise the seclusion is fasid and only half mahr is due.

Illness as an Obstacle to Valid Seclusion: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Discussion of whether illness is a barrier to valid khalwah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on whether a man's illness prevents valid khalwah and explain the practical consequence of each opinion.

Core Idea
Only illness that prevents intercourse voids seclusion, but some Hanafis say any man's illness does.

In Hanafi fiqh, valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah) carries the same legal consequences as actual intercourse in certain contexts like mahr and iddah. However, certain obstacles can render the seclusion invalid. One such obstacle is illness. The author of al-Hidayah states that illness is a barrier, but not all illness — only that which prevents intercourse or causes harm. Yet he notes a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school concerning a man's illness: some scholars consider any illness an absolute barrier.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The author states that illness is an obstacle, but specifies that only illness that prevents intercourse or causes harm qualifies as an obstacle, not absolute illness.
This qualification is critical for understanding the dispute.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some scholars hold that a man's illness is an absolute barrier, regardless of severity, because any illness causes weakness and lack of desire for intercourse.
The text says 'بعض کی رائے' – some scholars.
3
Understand the basis of each view
The majority view (illness must prevent intercourse) considers the purpose of khalwah as a proxy for intercourse; if intercourse is still possible, seclusion is valid. The minority view sees any illness as undermining the purpose.
The majority view is consistent with the principle that khalwah is like actual intercourse.
4
Note the agreement on women's illness
The text says a woman's illness is divided without dispute – only illness that prevents intercourse is a barrier. This asymmetry highlights the man's active role.
There is no dispute regarding women.
5
Derive the practical consequence
If a man's minor illness arises during seclusion, according to the majority view the seclusion remains valid (full mahr and iddah apply); according to the minority view, it is invalid (only half mahr, no iddah).
The mufta bihi is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ موانع کی تفصیل ذکر کرنا چاہتے ہیں۔ چنانچہ سب سے پہلے فرمایا کہ مرض مانع ہے۔ لیکن مرض سے وہ مرض مراد ہے جو مانع جماع ہو یا جماع کرنے سے ضرر لاحق ہوتا ہو مطلقا مرض مراد نہیں ہے اور بعض کی رائے یہ ہے کہ مرد کا مرض مطلقا مانع ہے۔ کیونکہ مطلقا مرض سے اعضاء شکنی اور سستی رہتی ہے۔ لہذا مرد میں جماع کیلئے نشاط پیدا نہیں ہوگا۔ اس وجہ سے مرد کے مطلقا مرض کو مانع قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ اور مرض کی جو تقسیم کی ہے وہ عورت کے مرض میں ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ عورت کا مرض بلا اختلاف منقسم ہے۔ اور مرد کا مرض ایک رائے کے مطابق منقسم ہے۔ اور ایک رائے یہ ہے کہ مرد کا مرض غیر منقسم ہے اور مرد کا مرض ہر حال میں خلوت صحیحہ کیلئے مانع ہے۔
The author of Hidayah wants to mention the details of obstacles. So first he said that illness is an obstacle. But by illness is meant that illness which prevents intercourse or from which harm would result, not illness in absolute terms. And some scholars are of the opinion that a man's illness is absolutely an obstacle, because absolute illness causes weakness and lethargy, so he will not have energy for intercourse. For this reason, a man's absolute illness is considered an obstacle. And the division (of illness) that is made is regarding a woman's illness. The conclusion is that a woman's illness is divided without dispute, and a man's illness is divided according to one opinion, and another opinion is that a man's illness is undivided and is a barrier to valid seclusion in all cases.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether illness (marad) acts as a barrier (man') to valid khalwah. The author of Hidayah begins by stating that illness is a barrier, but clarifies that only illness that prevents intercourse or causes harm is meant. However, there is a difference of opinion: some scholars hold that a man's illness is an absolute barrier, because any illness causes weakness and lack of desire, thus preventing the purpose of khalwah. This difference applies only to the man's illness; regarding the woman's illness, there is no dispute that it is divided (i.e., only severe illness that prevents intercourse is a barrier). Thus, two opinions exist on the man's illness: one that it is divided (only severe illness is a barrier), and another that it is undivided (all illness is a barrier). The practical effect is on whether khalwah is sahihah or fasidah when the man is ill.

Key Terms
مرض مانع (marad māni'): Illness that prevents intercourse or causes harm, considered a barrier to valid seclusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what does the author of al-Hidayah mean by 'illness is an obstacle'?
A) All illness invalidates seclusion.
B) Only illness that prevents intercourse or causes harm.
C) Only illness of the woman.
D) Illness is never an obstacle.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, only illness that prevents intercourse or causes harm invalidates seclusion; a man's minor illness is not a barrier according to the majority view.

Ramadan Fast, Ihram, and Menstruation as Barriers to Valid Seclusion
Rulings on Ramadan fast, ihram, and menstruation as barriers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why Ramadan fast, ihram, and menstruation are barriers to valid seclusion and identify the proof based on resultant hardship.

Core Idea
Hardship (haraj) from required expiation makes a state a barrier to valid seclusion.

In Hanafi fiqh, valid seclusion (khalwah sahiha) is like actual consummation in confirming the full mahr. However, certain states block the validity of seclusion due to the legal consequences that would follow if intercourse occurred. This lesson examines three such barriers mentioned in the passage: Ramadan fast, ihram (pilgrim's consecration), and menstruation, focusing on the proof of hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three barriers
Read the first part of the passage and note that Ramadan fast, ihram, and menstruation are explicitly listed as barriers to valid seclusion.
2
For each barrier, list the consequence of intercourse
For Ramadan fast: qada, kaffarah, and sin. For ihram: dam (sacrifice), hajj invalidation, qada. For menstruation: prohibition by nature and law.
These consequences create hardship (haraj).
3
Understand hardship as the operative cause
The passage states that because these consequences involve hardship, the state is considered a barrier. The presence of hardship prevents khalwah from being valid.
This is a rational proof (talil) based on the principle that hardship invalidates the purpose of seclusion.
4
Conclude the ruling on khalwah
If a barrier exists, khalwah is not valid, meaning it does not confirm full mahr automatically. The woman would only be entitled to half mahr if divorce occurs before consummation.
This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school.

اور رمضان کا روزہ بھی خلوت صحیحہ کیلئے مانع ہے کیونکہ رمضان کے روزے کی حالت میں اگر وطی کی گئی تو قضا اور کفارہ واجب ہوگا اور ساتھ ساتھ گنہ گار ہوگا۔ اور ظاہر ہے کہ ان چیزوں میں حرج ہے۔ لہذا صوم رمضان بھی مانع خلوت ہوگا اور احرام اسلئے مانع خلوت ہے کہ اگر بحالت احرام جماع کیا گیا تو محرم پر دم واجب ہوگا۔ یعنی بکری یا اونٹ کا ذبح کرنا واجب ہوگا اور عبادت حج فاسد ہوگی ۔ اور قضا واجب ہو گی۔ ظاہر ہے کہ ان چیزوں میں بھی حرج ہے لہذا احرام بھی مانع خلوت ہوگا ۔ اور حیض اسلئے مانع ہے کہ حیض کی حالت میں وطی کرنا طبعا بھی ممنوع ہے اور شرعاً بھی جیسا کہ پہلے گزر چکا۔ اور اگر احد الزوجین نفلی روزے ہے ہے اور خلوت پائی گئی تو عورت کیلئے کامل مہر ہو گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ مصنف نے صوم نفل کو مانع صحت خلوت شمار نہیں کیا ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ متقی مصنفہ حاکم الشہید ابوالفضل کی روایت کے مطابق نفلی روزہ کو بلا عذرا افطار کرنا مباح ہے۔ لہذا جب نفلی روزے کے افطار میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے تو اس کو مانع خلوت قرار نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ منتقی کی اس روایت کو صرف کامل وجوب مہر کے سلسلہ میں صحیح مانا ہے۔ ورنہ بعض حضرات کی رائے یہ ہے کہ نفلی روزہ بھی خلوت صحیحہ کیلئے مانع ہے۔ اسلئے سر نفلی روزہ کو بغیر عذر کے باطل کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ رہا قضاء اور نذر کا روزہ سواس بارے میں دو روایات ہیں ایک یہ کہ صوم نفل اس اور صوم قضا اور صوم منذور کی حالت میں اگر وہی کی جائے تو گنہگار ہو گا لیکن کفارہ واجب نہیں ہو گا۔ پس جس شخص نے اس پر نظر ڈالی کہ گنہگار ہوگا تو اس نے صوم قضا اور منذور کوصوم رمضان کے حکم میں رکھا صوم مغل کے حکم میں نہیں رکھا اور جس کی نظر اس پر پڑی کہ صوم قضاء اور منذور میں کفارہ نہیں تو اس نے صوم قضاء وغیرہ کوصوم نفل کے حکم میں بنادیا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نماز، روزے کے مشابہ ہے لہذا جوحکم صوم فرض کا تھاوہی حکم ہوگا صلوۃ مفروضہ کا۔ اور جو حکم تھا صوم مغل کا وہی حکم ہوگا صلوۃ نافلہ کا۔ الحاصل صوم فرض اور صلوٰۃ مفروضہ دونوں مانع صحت خلوت ہیں۔ اور دونوں کا نفل صحت خلوت کیلئے مانع نہیں ہے۔ واللہ اعلم
And the Ramadan fast is also a barrier to valid seclusion, because if intercourse occurs during Ramadan fast, both qada and kaffarah become obligatory, and he also becomes sinful. And it is obvious that these involve hardship, so Ramadan fast is also a barrier. And ihram is a barrier to valid seclusion because if intercourse occurs in ihram, then a dam (sacrifice) becomes obligatory on the muhrim, meaning slaughter of a goat or camel, and the hajj worship becomes invalid, and qada becomes obligatory. Obviously there is hardship in these, so ihram is also a barrier. And menstruation is a barrier because intercourse during menses is prohibited both naturally and legally as previously mentioned. And if one of the spouses is observing a nafl fast and seclusion occurs, then the woman will get the full mahr. The conclusion is that the author did not consider nafl fast as a barrier to valid seclusion. The proof is that according to the narration of Muttaqi Musannaf Hakim al-Shahid Abu al-Fadl, breaking a nafl fast without excuse is permissible. So when there is no hardship in breaking a nafl fast, it will not be considered a barrier. The author of Hidayah says that this narration from Muntaka is accepted only for the purpose of the full obligation of mahr. Otherwise, some scholars are of the opinion that nafl fast is also a barrier to valid seclusion, because breaking a nafl fast without excuse is not correct. As for the qada and nadhr fast, there are two narrations: one that just like nafl fast, qada and nadhr fast are not barriers to valid seclusion. The second narration is that they are barriers like Ramadan fast. The conclusion is that from intercourse during Ramadan fast, both kaffarah and sin are due; while during qada and nadhr fast, only sin is due, not kaffarah. So whoever focused on the sin side placed qada and nadhr in the category of Ramadan fast, and whoever focused on the absence of kaffarah placed them in the category of nafl fast. The author of Hidayah says that prayer is analogous to fasting, so whatever ruling applies to obligatory fast applies to obligatory prayer, and whatever ruling applies to nafl fast applies to nafl prayer. In summary, both obligatory fast and obligatory prayer are barriers, and the nafl of both is not a barrier. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage discusses various types of fasts and ihram as potential barriers to valid seclusion. Ramadan fast is a barrier because intercourse necessitates qada and kaffarah, causing harm. Ihram is a barrier due to dam and hajj invalidation. Menstruation is a barrier due to natural and legal prohibition. Nafl fast is not considered a barrier by the majority, based on a narration that it can be broken without excuse. However, some scholars hold it as a barrier because breaking it without reason is not permissible. For qada and nadhr fasts, there are two narrations: one likens them to nafl (not barriers) and another to Ramadan (barriers). The author reconciles by noting that sin occurs in both but kaffarah only in Ramadan. The ruling for prayer is analogous: obligatory prayer is a barrier, nafl prayer is not. This analysis determines whether khalwah is valid and thus whether full mahr is due.

Key Terms
صوم رمضان (sawm Ramaḍān): Obligatory fast of Ramadan, considered a barrier to valid khalwah due to the hardship of qada and kaffarah.
صوم نفل (sawm nafal): Voluntary fast, generally not considered a barrier to valid khalwah because it can be broken without hardship.
احرام (iḥrām): The state of consecration for hajj or umrah, considered a barrier because intercourse incurs dam and invalidation of pilgrimage.
حیض (ḥayḍ): Menstruation, considered a barrier because intercourse is prohibited both naturally and legally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is Ramadan fast considered a barrier to valid seclusion?
A) Because fasting itself is an act of worship.
B) Because intercourse during Ramadan fast requires qada and kaffarah, creating hardship.
C) Because the Quran explicitly mentions it.
D) Because the wife’s consent is not valid during fasting.

Key Takeaway
A state is a barrier to valid seclusion if intercourse would incur hardship from required expiation or clear prohibition.

Nafl Fast, Qada/Nadhr Fasts, and the Analogy to Prayer
Rulings on nafl, qada, nadhr fasts and analogy to prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on nafl fast as a non-barrier, the two narrations regarding qada and nadhr fasts, and the analogy to prayer.

Core Idea
Only obligatory fasts that incur kaffarah are barriers; nafl fasts and their analogs are not, due to ease of breaking.

The passage continues by examining the status of nafl (voluntary) fasts, then qada (make-up) and nadhr (vowed) fasts. The author identifies a dispute based on two narrations and resolves it by noting that the presence or absence of kaffarah determines the ruling. Finally, the author of Hidayah draws an analogy between fasting and prayer to unify the rulings.

Guided Path
1
Understand the ruling on nafl fast
The author states that nafl fast is not a barrier to valid seclusion. The proof is a narration that it is permissible to break a nafl fast without excuse, so no hardship exists.
This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position.
2
Identify the two narrations on qada and nadhr fasts
First narration: qada and nadhr are like nafl (not barriers). Second narration: they are like Ramadan (barriers). The basis for the difference is whether one focuses on the sin (both have sin) or the absence of kaffarah (qada/nadhr lack kaffarah).
The author of Hidayah does not explicitly choose, but the majority view is that they are barriers because sin alone creates hardship.
3
Analyze the author of Hidayah's comment on the Muntaka narration
The author of Hidayah says that the Muntaka narration (nafl not a barrier) is accepted only for the purpose of full mahr, implying that the ruling on nafl is not absolute. Some scholars consider nafl a barrier because breaking it without excuse is not permissible.
This shows a nuanced difference between the earlier and later Hanafi positions.
4
Apply the analogy to prayer
The author of Hidayah states that prayer is analogous to fasting: obligatory prayer (e.g., fajr) is a barrier, while nafl prayer is not. This extension supports the principle that only obligatory acts with necessary consequences are barriers.
This analogy (qiyas) reinforces the Hanafi method of deriving rulings.

Commentary
This passage discusses various types of fasts and ihram as potential barriers to valid seclusion. Ramadan fast is a barrier because intercourse necessitates qada and kaffarah, causing harm. Ihram is a barrier due to dam and hajj invalidation. Menstruation is a barrier due to natural and legal prohibition. The author reconciles by noting that sin occurs in both but kaffarah only in Ramadan. The ruling for prayer is analogous: obligatory prayer is a barrier, nafl prayer is not. This analysis determines whether khalwah is valid and thus whether full mahr is due.

Key Terms
صوم قضاء (sawm qaḍā): Make-up fast for an obligatory fast missed due to a valid excuse, considered a barrier by the majority due to sin.
صوم نذر (sawm nadhr): Vowed fast, considered binding once vowed; ruling similar to qada fast.
صوم نفل (sawm nafal): Voluntary fast, generally not a barrier due to permission to break without excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the second narration that qada and nadhr fasts are barriers?
A) They require kaffarah like Ramadan fast.
B) Intercourse during these fasts incurs sin, creating hardship.
C) They are mentioned in the Quran as barriers.
D) The Prophet specifically prohibited seclusion during such fasts.

Key Takeaway
The presence of sin alone, even without kaffarah, makes a fast a barrier to valid seclusion according to the preferred Hanafi view.

The Khalwah of a Majbub: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khalwah of a majbub

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the validity of khalwah by a majbub and state the practical consequence on mahr.

Core Idea
For Abu Hanifa, friction suffices for valid khalwah; for Sahibayn, only intercourse ability validates it.

This lesson examines a dispute within the Hanafi school on the legal effect of khalwah by a man whose penis is amputated (majbub). The outcome determines whether the wife receives full mahr or half if divorced after seclusion. We will unpack the reasoning of each side and the underlying legal principles.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa holds the khalwah is valid (sahihah) so full mahr is due. The Sahibayn hold it is invalid (fasidah) so only half mahr is due.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's proof
They argue the majbub is more incapable than a sick person because he has no organ. Valid khalwah requires soundness of the organ. Contrast with 'innin (impotent) who has an organ so his khalwah is valid.
The ruling revolves around the soundness of the organ.
3
Identify Abu Hanifa's proof
He argues that the wife's obligation is to submit for friction (sahq), which she can do. Therefore she has fulfilled her duty, so full mahr is due.
Focus is on the wife's capacity, not the husband's.
4
Compare with the case of 'innin
Both agree that the 'innin's khalwah is valid because his organ is intact, so possibility of intercourse exists. The majbub has no organ, so Sahibayn consider the possibility absent, but Abu Hanifa considers friction as sufficient.
The difference lies in what constitutes sexual access.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If the husband divorces after khalwah, the wife gets full mahr under Abu Hanifa, half under Sahibayn. This shows how a single factual circumstance (amputation) leads to different rulings based on underlying principles.
The practical consequence is purely financial.

Source Text

محبوب الذکر کی خلوت صحیحہ ہے یا فاسد... اقوال فقہاء
و اذا خلا المجبوب بامرأته ثم طلقها فلها كمال المهر عند ابي حنيفة وقالا عليه نصف المهرلانه اعجز من المريض بخلاف العنين لان الحكم أدير على سلامة الألة ولابي حنيفة ان المستحق عليها التسليم في حق السحق وقداتت به
ترجمہ .... اور جب خلوت کی مقطوع الذکر نے اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ پھر اس کو طلاق دے دی تو عورت کیلئے کمال مہر ہے۔ ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ مرد پر نصف مہر واجب ہے اسلئے کہ وہ زیادہ عاجز ہے مریض کے مقابلہ میں بخلاف عنین کے اسلئے کہ حکم دائر کیا گیا ہے سلامت آلہ پر اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت پر بحق (یعنی رگڑنا ) پر قدرت دینا واجب ہے اور وہ اس کو لے آئی۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مقطوع الذکر کی خلوت صحیح ہے یا فاسد ۔ امام صاحب فرماتے ہیں کہ مقطوع الذکر نے اگر خلوت کی اور پھر طلاق دے دی تو عورت کیلئے کامل مہر واجب ہوگا۔ اور یہ خلوت صحیحہ کہلائے گی۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ یہ خلوت فاسدہ ہے لہذا اگبر طلاق دے دی تو نصف مہر واجب ہوگا۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقطوع الذکر مریض کے مقابلہ میں زیادہ عاجز ہے کیونکہ مریض کبھی نہ کبھی جماع پر قادر ہوسکتا ہے لیکن مقطوع الذکر جماع پر بالکل قدرت نہیں رکھتا عدم آلہ کی وجہ سے بخلاف منین کے کہ اس کی خلوت صحیحہ ہے اسلئے کہ حکم سلامت آلہ پر دائر کیا جاتا ہے اور مقطوع الذکر کا آلہ ہی نہیں۔ پس منین اور مقطوع الذکر کی خلوت ، خلوت فاسدہ ہے۔ عینین وہ ہے جو مطلقاً جماع پر قدرت نہ رکھتا ہو وجود آلہ کے باوجود بعض کہتے ہیں کہ جو شیبہ سے جماع پر قدرت رکھے باکرہ سے نہیں ۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت پر تسلیم یعنی بضع کو سپرد کرنا واجب ہے رگڑنے کے حق میں اور یہی عورت کی قدرت میں ہے سو یہ کام عورت کر چکی ۔ لہذا مرد پر کامل مہر واجب ہوگا اور یہ خلوت خلوت صحیحہ ہوگی ۔
Is the seclusion of a man with amputated penis (majbub) valid or invalid? Statements of jurists. And if a majbub secluded with his wife then divorced her, then according to Abu Hanifa she gets the full mahr. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said that he owes half the mahr, because he is more incapable than a sick person, unlike a 'innin (impotent man) because the ruling is based on the soundness of the organ. And Abu Hanifa's proof is that what is due from the wife is submission regarding friction (sahq), and she has done that. Commentary: The issue is whether the seclusion of a man with amputated penis is valid or invalid. Imam Abu Hanifa says that if he secluded then divorced, the woman gets full mahr, and this is valid seclusion. The two said it is invalid seclusion, so if he divorced, half mahr is due. The proof of the two is that the man with amputated penis is more incapable than a sick person, because a sick person may be able to have intercourse sometimes, but the amputated one has no ability at all due to lack of organ. Unlike the 'innin (impotent) whose seclusion is valid because the ruling revolves around the soundness of the organ, and the amputated one has no organ. So the seclusion of the 'innin and the amputated is invalid. The 'innin is one who has no ability to have intercourse at all even with the presence of the organ. Some say he can have intercourse with an older woman but not a virgin. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that it is obligatory upon the wife to submit her private part for friction, and that is within her power, and she has done it. So full mahr is due and the seclusion is valid.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of khalwah (seclusion) by a husband whose penis is amputated (majbub). Abu Hanifa rules that this khalwah is valid (sahihah), so if he divorces her after seclusion, full mahr is due. His reasoning: the wife's obligation is to submit for friction (sahq), which she can do; she has fulfilled that, so full mahr is owed. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule it is invalid (fasidah), so only half mahr is due. Their reasoning: the man is even more incapable than a sick person because he has no organ at all, and the ruling of valid khalwah is based on soundness of the organ. They contrast this with an 'innin (impotent man) who has a healthy organ but cannot achieve erection; for him, khalwah is valid because the organ is intact. The dispute highlights the difference in focus: Abu Hanifa on the wife's capacity to give sexual service, Sahibayn on the husband's ability to perform intercourse.

Key Terms
مجبوب (majbūb): A man whose penis has been amputated.
عنین ('innīn): A man who is impotent, unable to have intercourse despite having a healthy organ.
سحق (saḥq): Friction (sexual stimulation without full penetration).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do the Sahibayn consider the khalwah of a majbub to be invalid (fasidah)?
A) Because he cannot have intercourse due to lack of organ
B) Because he is sick
C) Because the wife dislikes him
D) Because he cannot pay mahr

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on whether the wife's ability to provide friction suffices for valid khalwah, with Abu Hanifa affirming and the Sahibayn requiring the possibility of intercourse.

Iddah Obligation After Khalwah in All Cases
Ruling statement with istihsan justification and exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on iddah after khalwah, identify the conditions that trigger iddah, and distinguish between legal and real obstacles.

Core Idea
Iddah is obligatory after any khalwah as a precaution, unless a real physical obstacle prevented conception.

This passage from Al-Hidayah explains a key principle: the waiting period (iddah) is imposed not only after actual intercourse but also after any valid or invalid seclusion (khalwah). The ruling is based on istihsan to protect the rights of the child and the Shari'ah. However, the obligation is lifted when there was no actual possibility of conception due to a real, physical impediment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
State the rule: Iddah is obligatory upon the woman in all cases of khalwah (sahih or fasid) mentioned earlier.
The ruling is unconditional for khalwah itself.
2
Understand the basis: istihsan
The obligation is established by istihsan (juristic preference) out of caution because there is a possibility of pregnancy (shughl).
Istihsan overrides strict qiyas which might require actual intercourse.
3
Note the rationale: rights of Shari'ah and child
Iddah is a right of the Shari'ah and the potential child. Therefore, the husband's denial of intercourse is not accepted to nullify iddah.
This contrasts with mahr, where caution is not applied because it is wealth.
4
Distinguish obstacles: shar'i vs haqiqi
Al-Quduri explains: if the obstacle to intercourse is legal (shar'i) like ihram or fasting, iddah is still obligatory because the ability to conceive existed in reality (tamakkun haqiqi). If the obstacle is real (haqiqi) like illness or minority, iddah is not obligatory because there was no actual ability.
Ability to conceive is a condition for iddah after khalwah.
5
Apply the exception
Identify cases where iddah is not obligatory: when the wife is a minor or so ill that intercourse was impossible. In such cases, the real impossibility removes the obligation.
The ruling emphasizes caution but acknowledges physical reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مذکورہ تمام مسائل میں عورت پر عدت لازم ہے
قال و عليها العدة في جميع هذه المسائل احتياطا استحسانا لتوهم الشغل والعدة حق الشرع والولد فلا يصدق في ابطال حق الغير بخلاف المهر لانه مال لا يحتاط في ايجابه وذكر القدوري في شرحه ان المانع ان كان شرعيا تجب العدة لثبوت التمكن حقيقة و ان كان حقيقتا كالمرض والصغر لا تجب لعدم
In all these mentioned cases, iddah is obligatory upon the woman. He said: And iddah is obligatory in all these cases as a precaution (istihsanan) due to the possibility of occupation (i.e., pregnancy). And the iddah is the right of the Shari'ah and the child, so the husband is not believed in nullifying the right of another, unlike mahr because it is wealth and caution is not exercised in its obligation. And al-Quduri mentioned in his commentary that if the obstacle is legal (shar'i), iddah is obligatory due to the existence of ability (tamakkun) in reality; and if it is real (haqiqi) like illness or minority, iddah is not obligatory due to lack of ability.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage provides a general ruling that iddah (waiting period) is obligatory upon the woman in all the cases of khalwah discussed earlier, regardless of whether the khalwah was sahihah or fasidah. The reason is caution (istihsan) because there is a possibility of pregnancy (shughl). The iddah is a right of the Shari'ah and of the potential child, so the husband's denial is not accepted. However, al-Quduri distinguishes based on the type of obstacle: if the obstacle is legal (shar'i) like ihram or fasting, iddah is still obligatory because the possibility of conception existed in reality (tamakkun haqiqi). But if the obstacle is real (haqiqi) like illness or the wife being a minor, iddah is not obligatory because there was no actual ability to conceive. The passage contrasts this with mahr, where caution is not applied because it is wealth; hence in some disputed cases mahr is reduced but iddah remains.

Key Terms
عدت (ʿiddah): Waiting period after divorce or death to determine paternity and allow reconciliation.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference used here to justify iddah obligation despite the khalwah being potentially invalid.
تمكن حقيقي (tamakkun haqiqi): Real ability to conceive; a condition for iddah obligation after khalwah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Quduri's commentary, when is iddah not obligatory after khalwah?
A) When the obstacle is legal (shar'i)
B) When the obstacle is real (haqiqi) like illness or minority
C) In all cases of khalwah
D) Only when the khalwah is fasidah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obligates iddah after any khalwah as a precautionary measure to protect lineage and Shari'ah rights, unless a real physical impossibility of conception existed.

Khulwa of a Castrated Man (Majbub) and the Mahr Obligation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr after khulwa with a majbub.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the mahr obligation after a castrated man's seclusion, and identify the reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
For a majbub, full mahr or half? The organ's presence determines valid seclusion.

This passage examines an intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens to the mahr when a castrated man (majbub) secludes with his wife and then divorces her without intercourse? The disagreement turns on whether the seclusion is considered valid (sahiha) or invalid (fasida). Let us unpack each imam's argument and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
A majbub (castrated man) secludes with his wife in private (khulwa) and then divorces her without actual intercourse. The question is: how much mahr is due?
The scenario assumes the marriage is valid and the seclusion was genuine.
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa rules that full mahr is wajib. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) rule that only half mahr is wajib.
Both positions are within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
They analogize the majbub to a sick man but deem him even more incapable because he lacks the organ entirely. Since he cannot perform intercourse, the seclusion is invalid (fasida), hence only half mahr is due.
They distinguish from an impotent man ('innin) who has the organ, making his seclusion valid.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
He argues that the wife's duty is to submit to intimate contact (sahaq/rubbing), which she has done. Since she fulfilled what was possible, the seclusion is valid (sahiha), triggering full mahr.
Abu Hanifa focuses on the wife's submission rather than the husband's capacity.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the seclusion is valid, full mahr is due; if invalid, only half mahr. The dispute directly affects the financial obligation.
The passage does not specify which view is mufta bihi (relied upon for fatwa).

Source Text

ترجمہ .... اور جب خلوت کی مقطوع الذکر نے اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ پھر اس کو طلاق دے دی تو عورت کیلئے کمال مہر ہے۔ ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ مرد پر نصف مہر واجب ہے اسلئے کہ وہ زیادہ عاجز ہے مریض کے مقابلہ میں بخلاف عنین کے اسلئے کہ حکم دائر کیا گیا ہے سلامت آلہ پر اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت پر بحق (یعنی رگڑنا ) پر قدرت دینا واجب ہے اور وہ اس کو لے آئی۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مقطوع الذکر کی خلوت صحیح ہے یا فاسد ۔ امام صاحب فرماتے ہیں کہ مقطوع الذکر نے اگر خلوت کی اور پھر طلاق دے دی تو عورت کیلئے کامل مہر واجب ہوگا۔ اور یہ خلوت صحیحہ کہلائے گی۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ یہ خلوت فاسدہ ہے لہذا اگبر طلاق دے دی تو نصف مہر واجب ہوگا۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقطوع الذکر مریض کے مقابلہ میں زیادہ عاجز ہے کیونکہ مریض کبھی نہ کبھی جماع پر قادر ہوسکتا ہے لیکن مقطوع الذکر جماع پر بالکل قدرت نہیں رکھتا عدم آلہ کی وجہ سے بخلاف منین کے کہ اس کی خلوت صحیحہ ہے اسلئے کہ حکم سلامت آلہ پر دائر کیا جاتا ہے اور مقطوع الذکر کا آلہ ہی نہیں۔ پس منین اور مقطوع الذکر کی خلوت ، خلوت فاسدہ ہے۔ عینین وہ ہے جو مطلقاً جماع پر قدرت نہ رکھتا ہو وجود آلہ کے باوجود بعض کہتے ہیں کہ جو شیبہ سے جماع پر قدرت رکھے باکرہ سے نہیں ۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت پر تسلیم یعنی بضع کو سپرد کرنا واجب ہے رگڑنے کے حق میں اور یہی عورت کی قدرت میں ہے سو یہ کام عورت کر چکی ۔ لہذا مرد پر کامل مہر واجب ہوگا اور یہ خلوت خلوت صحیحہ ہوگی
And when a castrated man secludes with his wife and then divorces her, she gets full dower according to Abu Hanifa, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: upon him is half the dower, because he is more incapable than a sick man, unlike the impotent man, because the ruling is based on the soundness of the organ. And for Abu Hanifa, what is due upon her is submission in the matter of rubbing, and she has brought that.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of valid seclusion (khulwa sahiha) by a husband who is castrated (majbub). The issue: if such a man secludes with his wife and then divorces her without actual intercourse, is the full mahr due or only half? Abu Hanifa rules that full mahr is obligatory because the wife's duty is to submit to intimate contact (sahaq/rubbing) which she has done. The seclusion is considered valid (sahiha). Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) analogize him to a sick man, but consider him even more incapable, thus the seclusion is invalid (fasida) and only half mahr is due. They distinguish from an impotent man ('innin) who has the organ, so his seclusion is valid. The text also clarifies the definition of 'innin (completely unable to have intercourse despite having the organ). The commentary explains both positions and their proofs.

Key Terms
المجبوب (al-majbub): A man whose penis has been amputated (castrated).
العنين (al-'innin): A man who is impotent, unable to have intercourse despite having the organ.
خلوة صحيحة (khulwa sahiha): Valid seclusion that is legally equivalent to actual intercourse for the purposes of mahr and iddah.
خلوة فاسدة (khulwa fasida): Invalid seclusion that does not carry the effect of actual intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The validity of khulwa for mahr purposes depends on the husband's physical ability to perform intercourse; a majbub's seclusion is disputed as sahih or fasid, affecting whether full or half mahr is due.

Iddah Obligation in Cases of Valid or Invalid Seclusion
Ruling that iddah is obligatory in all seclusion cases due to istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that iddah is wajib after any seclusion where pregnancy is possible, and apply al-Quduri's distinction between sharii and real barriers to determine when iddah is obligatory.

Core Idea
Iddah is wajib in every seclusion where pregnancy is possible, even if invalid — istihsan overrides strict analogy.

This passage clarifies the Hanafi position that iddah is not limited to valid seclusion. Because iddah protects the rights of the Sharia and the child, suspicion (tawahhum) of pregnancy triggers the obligation, even when the seclusion was invalid. The ruling is based on istihsan and ihtiyat (precaution). Al-Quduri adds a crucial distinction between sharii and real barriers: sharii barriers (e.g., menstruation) do not negate legal ability, so iddah is wajib; real barriers (e.g., severe illness) negate actual ability, so no iddah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State that iddah is wajib in all cases of seclusion mentioned (valid, invalid, with a castrated man) because of the possibility of pregnancy.
This is based on istihsan and ihtiyat.
2
Understand the Proof (Istihsan)
The proof is istihsan (juristic preference) due to the suspicion that semen may have entered the womb. This overrides the strict qiyas that would require actual intercourse.
The suspicion is legally considered because iddah is a right of Sharia and the child.
3
Distinguish Iddah from Mahr
Unlike mahr (which is property), iddah is a personal right that cannot be waived by the spouses. Their denial of intercourse is not accepted to invalidate iddah.
So even if both spouses agree no intercourse occurred, iddah is still obligatory.
4
Apply al-Quduri's Barrier Distinction
If the barrier to intercourse is sharii (e.g., menstruation), legal ability is presumed, so iddah is wajib. If the barrier is real (e.g., illness), actual ability is absent, so no iddah.
This distinction clarifies when the suspicion of pregnancy is legally valid.

Source Text
