مذکورہ تمام مسائل میں عورت پر عدت لازم ہے

قال و عليها العدة في جميع هذه المسائل احتياطا استحسانا لتوهم الشغل والعدة حق الشرع والولد فلا يصدق في ابطال حق الغير بخلاف المهر لانه مال لا يحتاط في ايجابه وذكر القدوري في شرحه ان المانع ان كان شرعيا تجب العدة لثبوت التمكن حقيقة و ان كان حقيقا كالمرض والصغر لا تجب لعدم التمكن حقيقة

ترجمہ اورعورت پر عدت واجب ہے ان تمام مسائل میں احتیاط کی بناء پر اسحسا ناریم کے مشغول ہونے کے وہم کی وجہ سے اور عدت شریعت اور ولد دونوں کا حق ہے پس نہیں تصدیق کی جائے گی ۔ حق غیر کو باطل کرنے میں بخلاف مہر کے ۔ اسلئے کہ مہر مال ہے اس کو واجب کرنے میں احتیاط نہیں کی جاتی ہے اور قدوری نے ذکر کیا اپنی شرح میں کہ مانع اگر شرعی ہے تو عدت واجب ہوگی حقیقہ قدرت کے ثابت ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اور اگر مانع حقیقی ہے جیسے بیماری اور بچپن تو عدت واجب نہیں ہوگی ۔ حقیقت قدرت کے نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح ماقبل میں خلوت صحیحہ اور خلوت فاسدہ کا حکم معلوم ہوا کہ خلوت صحیحہ وطی کے قائم مقام ہے۔ لہذا خلوت صحیحہ کی صورت میں شوہر پر کامل مہر واجب کیا گیا ہے، اور خلوت فاسدہ چونکہ ولی کے قائم مقام نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے خلوت فاسدہ کی صورت میں شوہر پر نصف مہر واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اس عبارت میں بیان کیا گیا کہ مذکورہ بالا تمام مسائل میں خواہ خلوت صحیحہ پائی گئی ہو یا خلوت فاسدہ یا مقطوع الذکر کے ساتھ خلوت ہو۔ تمام صورتوں میں طلاق کے بعد عورت پر عدت واجب ہوگی۔ ان صورتوں میں عدت کا وجوب خلاف قیاس ہے احتیاط کی بناء پر۔ حاصل دلیل . یہ ہے کہ ان صورتوں میں رحم کے مشغول ہونے کا وہم ہے۔ اور وہم کی بنیاد یہ ہے کہ شاید دخول کی وجہ سے یا رگڑنے سے منی بہہ کر رحم میں پہنچ گئی ہو۔ لہذا احتیاط اسی میں ہے کہ عدت واجب کر دی جائے۔ اور مرد کا قول کہ میں نے وطی نہیں کی یا عورت کا قول کہ مجھ سے وطی نہیں کی گئی قابل قبول نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ عدت شریعت اور ولد کا حق ہے۔ شریعت کا حق تو اسلئے ہے کہ اگر میاں بیوی دونوں عدت کو ساقط کرنا چاہیں تو ساقط نہیں کر سکتے۔ اور والد کا حق اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ماقبل میں گذر چکی کہ جو شخص اللہ اور یوم آخرت پر ایمان رکھتا ہو وہ اپنے پانی سے کسی دوسرے کی کھیتی کو سیراب نہ کرے۔ اس حدیث کا مقصود ولد کے نسب کی رعایت کرنا ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ یہ ولد کا حق ہے۔ اور قاعدہ ہے کہ حق غیر کو باطل کرنے کیلئے کسی کا قول معتبر نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذا زوجین نے اگر اتفاق کرلیا کہ وطی نہیں کی گئی تو عدت کو باطل کرنے میں ان دونوں کی تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی۔ البتہ خلوت فاسدہ سے کامل مہر واجب نہیں ہوتا ہے کیونکہ مہر مال ہے اور وجوب مال میں زیادہ احتیاط نہیں کی جاتی ہے۔ قدوری نے اپنی شرح میں مانع کی تفصیل کی ہے چنانچہ فرمایا کہ اگر مانع شرعی ہے جیسے حیض و نفاس تو عدت واجب ہوگی کیونکہ مانع شرعی کے ہوتے ہوئے اگر خلوت پائی گئی تو شرعا عام قدرت ہو سکتی ہے لیکن حقیقتا ولی پر قدرت ثابت ہے پس متو ہم وطی کی وجہ سے رحم کے مشغول ہونے کا وہم پیدا ہو گیا۔ اس وجہ سے احتیاطاً عدت واجب کر دی گئی اور اگر مانع حقیقی ہے جیسے بیماری یا ایسا صغیر جو نا قابل جماع ہو تو اس صورت میں عدت واجب نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ مانع حقیقی کے ہوتے ہوئے حقیقت وطی پر قدرت نہیں ہے۔ پس رحم کے مشغول ہونے کا بھی وہم نہیں ہوگا۔
And upon her is the iddah in all these cases as a precaution, by way of istihsan, due to the suspicion of occupation (pregnancy). And the iddah is a right of the Sharia and the child, so he is not believed in invalidating the right of another, unlike the mahr because it is property, and precaution is not taken in making it obligatory. And al-Quduri mentioned in his commentary that if the barrier is sharii, iddah is obligatory due to the actual establishment of ability; if it is real, like illness or minority, iddah is not obligatory due to the absence of actual ability.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on iddah (waiting period) in all cases of seclusion, whether valid or invalid. The key point: iddah is obligatory (wajib) in every case where there is even a possibility of pregnancy, even if the seclusion was invalid. The proof is istihsan based on ihtiyat (precaution) because there is a suspicion that the womb may have been occupied by semen due to rubbing or other means. The iddah is a right of both the Sharia (cannot be waived by the spouses) and the child (to establish lineage). Therefore, the statements of the spouses denying intercourse are not accepted to invalidate this right. The commentator distinguishes between mahr (property, where precaution is not applied) and iddah (a personal right requiring caution). Al-Quduri's distinction: if the barrier to intercourse is a sharii barrier (like menstruation), actual ability to have intercourse is presumed, so iddah is wajib. If the barrier is real and physical (like illness or minority), actual ability is absent, so no iddah.

Key Terms
العدة (al-iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband to determine if she is pregnant.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that departs from strict analogy for a stronger reason, here precaution.
المانع الشرعي (al-mani' al-shar'i): A barrier to intercourse that is based on sacred law, such as menstruation or postnatal bleeding.
المانع الحقيقي (al-mani' al-haqiqi): A real physical barrier to intercourse, like illness, childhood, or actual castration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Quduri's distinction, if a woman secludes with her husband while she is menstruating (a sharii barrier), and he divorces her, what is the ruling on iddah?
A) Iddah is not required because actual intercourse cannot occur.
B) Iddah is required because the sharii barrier still allows for the possibility of impregnation.
C) Iddah is only required if the seclusion was valid.
D) Iddah is required but only half the normal duration.

Key Takeaway
Iddah is obligatory after any seclusion where pregnancy is legally possible, based on istihsan to protect lineage, with the exception of real barriers that negate the possibility.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
Mut'ah is Mustahabb for Every Divorced Woman Except One
States the ruling on mut'ah and addresses Shafi'i's objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mut'ah for each category of divorced woman, explain the Hanafi proof using the khalaf principle, and resolve the apparent textual ambiguity in al-Quduri's statement.

Core Idea
Mut'ah is a substitute for mahr; it cannot coexist with any mahr payment.

The issue of mut'ah (consolation gift) highlights the Hanafi school's precise legal reasoning. While the Shafi'i school views mut'ah as a compulsory gift to compensate the woman's desolation, the Hanafi school categorizes mut'ah as a substitute (khalaf) for mahr al-mithl in cases where no mahr was fixed. This lesson unpacks the full spectrum of rulings for divorced women, the inter-madhhab dispute, and a subtle textual clarification in al-Quduri's matn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of divorced women
List: (1) divorced before consummation with mahr specified, (2) divorced before consummation without mahr specified, (3) divorced after consummation (with or without mahr). For (1) mut'ah is neither wajib nor mustahabb; for (2) mut'ah is wajib; for (3) mut'ah is mustahabb.
This categorization is essential to understand the exception.
2
State the Hanafi ruling and its proof
The Hanafi position is that mut'ah is mustahabb for all except the first category. The proof: mut'ah is a khalaf (substitute) for mahr al-mithl in the mufawwadah case. The khalaf cannot coexist with the original (mahr) or any part of it. Therefore, when any mahr is due (half or full), mut'ah is not wajib.
The husband is not a criminal; thus no compensation.
3
Present the Shafi'i view and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds mut'ah wajib for all divorced women except the first category, arguing it is a gift to console the woman's desolation. In the exception, half the mahr already serves that purpose.
This is based on a different underlying principle.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response: divorce is permitted, so the husband is not a wrongdoer. Therefore mut'ah is not a penalty but a voluntary act. The khalaf principle prevents it from being obligatory where mahr is due.
The Shafi'i proof does not address the substitute argument.
5
Resolve the apparent ambiguity in al-Quduri's statement
Al-Quduri said 'mustahabb for every divorced woman except one'. The exception seems to include the same woman as in the general statement, creating a self-negation. The resolution: the excepted woman is the one with fixed mahr (no mut'ah), while the general statement excludes the mufawwadah (whose mut'ah is wajib). Thus the categories are distinct.
This shows the importance of precise terminology.

Source Text

تشریح قدوری کی عبارت میں ایک اشتباہ ہے پہلے اس کی وضاحت کر لی جائے۔ اشتباہ یہ ہے کہ قدوری کا صدر کلام ہر مطلقہ کیلئے استخباب متعہ کے عموم پر دلالت کرتا ہے۔ کیونکہ لفظ کل کی جب نکرہ کی طرف اضافت کی جائے تو وہ عموم افراد کا تقاضا کرتا ہے۔ پھر اس سے مطلقہ غیر مدخول بہا کا استثناء کیا ہے۔ پس یہاں صدر کلام اور استثناء دونوں پر اشکال ہے استثناء میں تو اسلئے کہ مبسوط میں ذکر کیا کہ مطلقہ غیر مدخول بہا سمی لہا کیلئے متعہ مستحب ہے اور تنتخب لکل مطلقہ میں یہ بھی شامل ہے۔ پس مستی اور مستثنی منہ میں اتحاد ہو گیا یعنی اولا تو کہا گیا کہ ہر مطلقہ کیلئے متعدہ مستحب ہے۔ پھر اس مطلقہ کا استثناء کر کے کہا مگر اس مطلقہ کیلئے مستحب ہے تو یہ استثناء عن نفسہ ہے جو متعذر ہے یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کوئی کہے جاءنی خالد الا خالد یعنی میرے پاس خالد آیا مگر خالد اس کو حماقت کے سوا کیا کہا جاسکتا ہے۔ صدر کلام میں اشکال یہ ہے کہ قدوری نے کہا ہر مطلقہ کیلئے متعدہ مستحب ہے اور ہر مطلقہ میں مطلقہ غیر مدخول بہا غیر سمی لہا بھی ہے۔ الہذا اس کیلئے بھی متعہ مستحب ہوگا حالانکہ ایسا نہیں، بلکہ اس کیلئے متعہ واجب ہے۔ استثناء میں جو اشکال تھا اس کا جواب تو یہ ہے کہ قدوری کے نزدیک صورت مستثنیہ میں متعہ مستحب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ قدوری نے اپنی شرح میں ذکر کیا کہ متعہ بعض صورتوں میں واجب اور بعض میں مستحب ہے۔ پس مطلقہ غیر مدخول بہا غیر سمی لہا کیلئے واجب ہے اور ہر مطلقہ کیلئے مستحب ہے علاوہ مطلقہ غیر مدخول بہا غیر سمی لہا کے۔ کیونکہ اس کیلئے مستحب نہیں بلکہ واجب ہے۔ پس اب مستثنی منہ اور مستثنیٰ میں تغایر ہو گیا۔ لہذا استثناء عن نفسہ لازم نہیں آئے گا اور یہ استثنا درست ہو گا۔ صدر کلام میں جو اشکال تھا اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ہر مطلقہ کیلئے متعہ مستحب ہے علاوہ مطلقہ غیر مدخول بہا غیر سمی لہا کے۔ کیونکہ اس کا حکم پہلے گزر چکا کہ اس کیلئے متعہ مستحب نہیں بلکہ واجب ہے۔ پس جب آپ نے ہر مطلقہ کے عموم سے اس مطلقہ کو خارج کر دنیا تو اب صدر کلام میں کوئی اشکال باقی نہیں رہا۔
بعض حضرات نے قدوری کے کلام کے معنی بیان کئے ہیں تستحب المتعة لكل مطلقة سوى التي تقدم ذكرها وهى
التي طلقها قبل الدخول و قبل التسمية فان متعتها واجبة الا لمطلقة واحدة وهى التي طلقها قبل الدخول بعد التسمية فان متعتها ليست بواجبة و لا مستحبة ۔ یعنی متعہ مستحب ہے مطلقہ کیلئے علاوہ اس کے جس کا ذکر پہلے گزر چکا اور وہ یہ
Mut'ah is mustahabb for every divorced woman. He said: It is mustahabb (recommended) for every divorced woman except one: the one whom the husband divorced before consummation and for whom he had specified a mahr. Imam al-Shafi'i said it is wajib for every divorced woman except this one, because it is a gift from the husband due to the woman's desolation upon separation, but in this case, half the mahr serves as mut'ah, since divorce is a nullification in this situation, and mut'ah is not repeated. Our proof is that mut'ah is a substitute (khalaf) for mahr al-mithl in the case of a woman with unfixed mahr (mufawwadah), because mahr al-mithl falls away and mut'ah becomes obligatory. The marriage contract obligates exchange, so it becomes a substitute, and the substitute does not combine with the original or any part of it. Therefore it is not obligatory with the obligation of any part of the mahr. The husband is not a criminal in causing desolation, so compensation (gharamah) is not imposed upon him. Thus mut'ah is an act of generosity (faḍl). Translation: And mut'ah is mustahabb for every divorced woman except one: the one divorced before consummation with mahr specified. Imam al-Shafi'i said it is wajib for every divorced woman except this one, because it is a gift from the husband due to desolation. But in this case, half the mahr takes the way of mut'ah, because divorce here is a nullification, and mut'ah is not repeated. Our proof is that mut'ah is a substitute for mahr al-mithl in mufawwadah, because mahr al-mithl falls and mut'ah becomes obligatory. The contract necessitates compensation, so it becomes a substitute, and the substitute does not combine with the original or any part thereof. So it is not obligatory with the obligation of any part of the mahr. The husband is not a criminal in causing desolation, so compensation does not apply. Thus mut'ah is an act of generosity. Explanation: There is an ambiguity in Quduri's statement. The ambiguity is that his initial statement indicates generality: 'mut'ah is mustahabb for every divorced woman', because the word 'kull' when added to a nakirah implies general coverage of individuals. Then he makes an exception: 'except one'. In the exception, there is an issue because in al-Mabsut it is mentioned that for a non-consummated divorced woman with mahr specified, mut'ah is mustahabb, and that is included in 'every divorced woman'. So the excepted and the excepted-from become the same, making it a self-negating exception (mustahīl) like saying 'Khalid came to me except Khalid.' In the initial statement, the issue is that it says 'every divorced woman', which includes the non-consummated woman without mahr specified, but for her mut'ah is not mustahabb; it is wajib. The answer to the exception issue is that according to Quduri, in the excepted case, mut'ah is not mustahabb, as he mentioned in his commentary that mut'ah is wajib in some cases and mustahabb in others. So the non-consummated woman without mahr specified is wajib, and for every other divorced woman it is mustahabb. Thus the excepted and excepted-from are different, so the exception is valid. The answer to the initial statement issue is that 'every divorced woman' is mustahabb except the non-consummated woman without mahr specified, because her ruling was already given that mut'ah is not mustahabb but wajib. So when you exclude her from the general statement, no ambiguity remains. Some scholars have explained Quduri's words as: 'Mut'ah is mustahabb for every divorced woman except the one previously mentioned: the one divorced before consummation and before specification, for her mut'ah is wajib. Except one: the one divorced before consummation after specification, for her mut'ah is neither wajib nor mustahabb.'
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of mut'ah (consolation gift) given to a divorced woman. The Hanafi position is that mut'ah is mustahabb (recommended) for every divorced woman, except one specific case: a woman divorced before consummation whose mahr was already specified (musamma). For her, mut'ah is not recommended because she already receives half the specified mahr. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that mut'ah is wajib for all divorced women except the same woman, arguing from the principle of compensating the woman for the desolation of divorce. The Hanafi response is that mut'ah is a substitute (khalaf) for mahr al-mithl in the case where no mahr was fixed (mufawwadah). Since a substitute cannot exist alongside the original or any part of it, mut'ah is not required when any mahr is payable. The husband is not a wrongdoer by divorcing, so no penalty (gharamah) applies; rather it is a voluntary gift. The passage goes on to clarify an apparent inconsistency in al-Quduri's wording: he says 'every divorced woman' then excepts one, but in al-Mabsut that excepted woman is also included in 'every divorced woman'. The commentator resolves this by showing that Quduri's excepted woman is actually the one with fixed mahr, not the one without fixed mahr (for whom mut'ah is wajib). Thus there is no contradiction.

Key Terms
متعہ (mut'ah): A consolation gift (usually of money or goods) given by the husband to the divorced woman.
مفوضہ (mufawwadah): A marriage contract where no specific mahr was fixed at the time of marriage; instead, mahr al-mithl is owed.
خلف (khalaf): A legal substitute that takes the place of the original obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For which divorced woman is mut'ah not mustahabb according to Hanafi?
A) She who was divorced after consummation without specified mahr.
B) She who was divorced before consummation with specified mahr.
C) She who was divorced after consummation with specified mahr.
D) She who was divorced before consummation without specified mahr.

Key Takeaway
Mut'ah is a substitute (khalaf) for mahr; therefore, it is only wajib when no mahr is due, and is otherwise recommended except for one specific case.

Nikah — Marriage

Hanafi Ruling on Mut'ah and Dispute with Shafi'i
Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on mut'ah obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mut'ah for each of the four categories of divorced women and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the principle of khalifah.

Core Idea
Mut'ah is wajib only when it substitutes a fallen dower; it cannot coexist with any dower.

The consolatory gift (mut'ah) for divorced women is a well-known Quranic injunction, but its precise legal obligation differs between schools. In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi classification of four types of divorced women and the detailed proof based on substitution (khalifah). We also examine Imam Shafi'i's view that loneliness (wahshah) triggers obligation, and the Hanafi rebuttal that mut'ah is generally voluntary except when it fills a financial gap.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on mut'ah
Identify the four categories of divorced women and the ruling for each: wajib, mustahabb, or neither. Note that the Hanafi school considers mut'ah wajib only for one type.
The four categories are: (1) ghayr madkhul biha ghayr musamma — wajib; (2) madkhul biha ghayr musamma — mustahabb; (3) madkhul biha musamma — mustahabb; (4) ghayr madkhul biha musamma — neither.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i (according to his qawl jadid) holds mut'ah wajib for all divorced women except the fourth category (ghayr madkhul biha musamma). Understand the scope of disagreement.
The Shafi'i view is based on the cause of loneliness.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i argues that separation causes loneliness, so mut'ah is obligatory to console. In the fourth case, half the dower already serves that purpose, avoiding repetition.
Repetition (takrar) in mut'ah is considered invalid.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that loneliness does not impose financial compensation (gharamah). Mut'ah is from the chapter of generosity (bāb al-fadl) except when it serves as a substitute (khalifah) for a fallen dower.
The principle of substitution (khalifah) is key: the substitute cannot combine with the original or its part.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference occurs in the two madkhul biha cases: Hanafis say mustahabb, Shafi'is say wajib. In the first and fourth cases, both schools agree on wajib and not wajib respectively.
This difference affects actual legal obligation in divorce settlements.

بعض حضرات نے قدوری کے کلام کے معنی بیان کئے ہیں تستحب المتعة لكل مطلقة سوى التي تقدم ذكرها وهى التى طلقها قبل الدخول و قبل التسمية فان متعتها واجبة الا لمطلقة واحدة وهى التي طلقها قبل الدخول بعد التسمية فان متعتها ليست بواجبة و لا مستحبة ۔ یعنی متعہ مستحب ہے مطلقہ کیلئے علاوہ اس کے جس کا ذکر پہلے گزر چکا اور وہ یہ

کتاب النکاح
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چهارم ہے کہ اس کو طلاق دی دخول سے پہلے اور تسمیہ مہر سے پہلے۔ اسلئے کہ اس کا متعہ واجب ہے مگر ایک مطلقہ کیلئے ۔ اور وہ یہ کہ اس کو طلاق دی کے بعد اسلئے کہ اس کا متعہ نہ واجب ہے اور نہ مستحب ہے۔
دخول سے پہلے اور تسمیہ مہر بعض حضرات نے جواب میں کہا کہ عبارت میں قد سمى لها مهر کی جگہ ولم يسم لها مهراً تھا۔ کا تب سے سہو ہو گیا۔ اب مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ ہر مطلقہ کیلئے متعہ مستحب ہے مگر ایک مطلقہ وہ یہ کہ اس کو طلاق دی شوہر نے قبل الدخول اور اس کیلئے مہر مذکور نہیں تھا۔ کیونکہ اس کیلئے متعہ مستحب نہیں بلکہ واجب ہے اس صورت میں بھی کوئی اشکال نہیں ہوگا ۔ ( عینی شرح ہدایہ )
ایک جواب محشی ہدایہ نے دیا ہے اس کو بھی دیکھ لیا جائے ۔ حاصل کلام یہ کہ مطلقات چار ہیں ۔ اول یہ کہ مطلقہ غیر مدخول بہا غیر رسمی لہا ہو اس کیلئے متعہ واجب ہے۔ قرآن کی آیت و متعوهن على الموسع قدره و على المفتر قدرہ کی وجہ سے ۔ دوم یہ کہ مطلقہ مدخول بہا غیر سمی لہا۔ سوم یہ کہ مطلقہ مدخول بہا سمی لہا ان دونوں کیلئے متعہ مستحب ہے۔ وللمطلقات متاع بالمعروف کی وجہ سے۔ یعنی مطلقہ عورتوں کیلئے متعہ ہے دستور شرع کے مطابق ۔ چہارم یہ کہ مطلقہ غیر مدخول بہا سمی لہا۔ اس کے واسطے متعہ نہ واجب ہے اور نہ مستحب یہی صورت متن میں مستثنیٰ ہے دلیل ابن عمر کا قول ہے لكل مطلقة متعة الا التى فرض لها و لم يدخل بها فحسبها نصف المهر - یعنی ہر مطلقہ کیلئے متعہ ہے مگر یہ کہ اس کیلئے مہر مقرر کیا گیا اور اس کے ساتھ دخول نہیں کیا تو اس کیلئے نصف مہر کافی ہے۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ ہر مطلقہ کیلئے متعہ واجب ہے مگر مطلقہ غیر مدخول بہا سمی لہا کیلئے متعہ واجب نہیں ۔ قول جدید کے مطابق اور قول قدیم کے مطابق اس کیلئے بھی متعہ واجب ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ مطلقہ غیر مدخول بہا غیر سمی لہا میں احناف و شوافع دونوں متفق ہیں کہ متعہ واجب ہے اور مطلقہ غیر مدخول بہا غیر سمی لہا میں دونوں متفق ہیں کہ متعہ واجب نہیں اور باقی دو صورتوں میں احناف استحباب کے قائل ہیں اور شوافع وجوب کے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر نے عورت کو اپنے سے جدا کر کے وحشت میں مبتلا کر دیا ہے۔ پس ہم نے وحشت فراق کو دور کرنے کیلئے بطور صلہ اور عطا کے متعہ واجب کر دیا تا کہ وحشت فراق کی تلافی ہو سکے لیکن صورت مستثنیہ میں اسلئے واجب نہیں کیا گیا کہ مطلقہ غیر مدخول بہا مسمی لہا کیلئے نصف مہر بطریق متعہ واجب ہوا ہے کیونکہ طلاق قبل الدخول معنی فسخ نکاح ہے اسلئے کہ اس حالت میں عورت کے منافع بضع بسلامت اس کی طرف لوٹ آئے اور اس کا تقاضا ہے کہ کل مہر ساقط ہونا چاہئے جیسا کہ منسخ بیچ میں مشتری کے ذمہ ہے کل ثمن ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ لیکن شریعت نے نصف مہر بطور متعہ کے واجب کر دیا ہے اور متعہ میں تکرار نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ پس اگر اس مطلقہ کیلئے نصف مہر کے ساتھ متعہ بھی واجب کر دیا جائے تو تکرار متعہ لازم آئے گا جو شرعاً درست نہیں۔ اسلئے اس مطلقہ کے متعہ واجب نہیں کیا گیا۔
ہماری دلیل سے پہلے یہ ذہن نشین کر لیجئے کہ عقد نکارح عوض سے خالی نہیں ہوتا ان تبتغوا باموالکم کی وجہ سے عوض مسمی ہوگا یا مہر مثل ۔ دوسری بات یہ کہ خلیفہ اصل کے ساتھ جمع نہیں ہو سکتا ہے اور نہ اصل کے جز کے ساتھ جیسے تیم وضو کے ساتھ جمع نہیں ہو سکتا ہے۔ اب دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہو گا کہ مطلقہ غیر مدخول بہا غیر سمی لہا کے حق میں متعہ مہر مثل کا خلیفہ ہے کیونکہ طلاق قبل الدخول کی وجہ سے مہر مثل تو ساقط ہو گیا اور عقد نکاح کیلئے عوض ضروری ہے۔ لہذا مہر مثل کا خلیفہ یعنی متعہ واجب ہوگا اور باقی تین صورتوں میں متعہ اسلئے واجب نہیں ہو سکتا کہ ہم نے ضابطہ بیان کیا ہے کہ خلیفہ نہ اصل کے ساتھ جمع ہو سکتا ہے اور نہ اس کے کسی جز کے ساتھ ۔ پس مطلقہ مدخول بہا مسمی لبا اور . مطلقہ مدخول بہا غیر سمی لہا کیلئے اگر متعہ واجب کیا گیا تو خلیفہ کا اصل یعنی کل مسمی یا مہر مثل کے ساتھ جمع ہونا لا زم آئے گا۔ اور اگر مطلقہ غیر
Mut'ah is recommended for every divorced woman except one: the woman divorced before consummation for whom a dower was specified. Imam Shafi'i said mut'ah is obligatory for every divorced woman except that one, because mut'ah is an obligatory gift from the husband due to causing loneliness by separation. But in that case, half the dower serves as mut'ah, because divorce before consummation is like annulment, and mut'ah is not repeated. Our proof is that mut'ah is a substitute (khalifah) for mahr al-mithl in the mufawwada case, because mahr al-mithl falls away and mut'ah becomes obligatory. The contract necessitates consideration, so mut'ah becomes a substitute, and the substitute does not combine with the original or any part of it. So it is not obligatory alongside any part of the dower. The husband is not a criminal causing loneliness, so compensation is not incurred. Thus mut'ah is from the chapter of generosity. Explanation: There is an ambiguity in Quduri's text: his initial statement implies mut'ah is recommended for all divorced women generally, then he excludes a specific type. The ambiguity is resolved by understanding that mut'ah is recommended for every divorced woman except those whose ruling was previously mentioned: the one divorced before consummation without dower specification, for whom mut'ah is obligatory; and the one divorced before consummation with dower specification, for whom it is neither obligatory nor recommended. Some scholars said that in Quduri's text, 'for whom a dower was specified' is a scribal error and should be 'for whom a dower was not specified'. The summary is that divorced women are four types: (1) ghayr madkhul biha ghayr musamma: mut'ah wajib, based on Quran 2:236; (2) madkhul biha ghayr musamma; (3) madkhul biha musamma: mut'ah mustahabb for both, based on Quran 2:241; (4) ghayr madkhul biha musamma: neither wajib nor mustahabb, based on the hadith of Ibn Umar. Imam Shafi'i held mut'ah wajib for every divorced woman except the fourth type, according to his new opinion. In the first type, Hanafis and Shafi'is agree it is wajib; in the fourth, they agree it is not wajib; in the other two, Hanafis say mustahabb, Shafi'is say wajib. Shafi'i's proof: the husband causes loneliness, so mut'ah is obligatory to console, but in the fourth case, half the dower suffices, so no repetition. Our (Hanafi) proof: remember that the marriage contract is not devoid of consideration, either specified or mahr al-mithl. The substitute cannot combine with the original or any part of it, like tayammum with wudu. For ghayr madkhul biha ghayr musamma, mut'ah is a substitute for mahr al-mithl because it falls; therefore it is wajib. For the other three, mut'ah cannot be wajib because the substitute would combine with the original (full dower or mahr al-mithl) or its part.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with the ruling of mut'ah (consolatory gift) for divorced women, presenting the Hanafi position and the dispute with Imam Shafi'i. It begins by summarizing the ruling: mut'ah is recommended (mustahabb) for every divorced woman except one specific type: a woman divorced before consummation for whom a dower was specified (ghayr madkhul biha musamma laha). For this woman, mut'ah is neither obligatory nor recommended; she receives half the dower instead. The author then notes an ambiguity in Quduri's text and provides a detailed correction. According to Quduri's initial statement, mut'ah is recommended for all divorced women, then an exception is made for one type. However, this seems problematic because the exception would be the same as the general ruling. The correction is that Quduri's text actually means mut'ah is recommended for every divorced woman except those whose ruling was previously given: the one divorced before consummation without a dower (for whom mut'ah is obligatory) and the one divorced before consummation with a dower (for whom it is neither). Thus the exception is valid. The passage then categorizes divorced women into four types: (1) ghayr madkhul biha ghayr musamma (divorced before consummation without dower): mut'ah is wajib based on Quran 2:236; (2) madkhul biha ghayr musamma (divorced after consummation without dower): mustahabb; (3) madkhul biha musamma (divorced after consummation with dower): mustahabb; (4) ghayr madkhul biha musamma (divorced before consummation with dower): neither wajib nor mustahabb. The Hanafi proof for making mut'ah wajib only in the first case is based on the principle of substitution (khalifah). In the case of mufawwada (marriage without dower), the dower (mahr al-mithl) falls due to divorce before consummation, and mut'ah becomes a substitute for that dower. The substitute cannot coexist with the original or any part of it. Therefore, when some dower (like half in type 4) or the full dower (in types 2 and 3) is present, mut'ah cannot be wajib; it may be recommended. The Shafi'i position, according to his new opinion, is that mut'ah is wajib for all divorced women except type 4. His proof is that the husband causes loneliness (wahshah) by separation, so mut'ah is obligatory to comfort her. But for type 4, she already receives half the dower as a substitute, so doubling would cause repetition (takrar), which is not valid in mut'ah. The Hanafi response is that the loneliness factor does not impose a financial compensation (gharamah); mut'ah is generally a voluntary act (bāb al-fadl) except when it serves as a substitute for a fallen dower. The practical difference between the two schools appears in types 2 and 3: Hanafis hold it as mustahabb, while Shafi'is hold it as wajib. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is as described.

Key Terms
متعہ (mutʿah): A consolatory gift given to a divorced woman as compensation for emotional distress, as prescribed in the Quran.
خلیفہ (khalīfah): A substitute that takes the place of an original obligation when the original falls due to impossibility or other reasons.
مفوضہ (mufawwaḍah): A marriage contract where no dower is specified (tafwīḍ).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, for which of the following divorced women is mut'ah (consolatory gift) wajib (obligatory)?
A) A woman divorced after consummation with a specified dower.
B) A woman divorced before consummation without a specified dower.
C) A woman divorced before consummation with a specified dower.
D) A woman divorced after consummation without a specified dower.

Key Takeaway
Mut'ah is wajib only when it serves as a substitute for a fallen dower; otherwise it is recommended or not applicable.

The Validity of Nikah Shighar and the Hanafi-Shafi‘i Dispute
Ruling on exchange marriage and its validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nikah shighar, explain the Hanafi proof by qiyas to invalid dower, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi‘i position.

Core Idea
In nikah shighar, the contract remains valid; proper dower (mahr al-mithl) becomes wajib.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, the author addresses a contentious form of marriage known as nikah shighar, where two men exchange female relatives without a separate dower. The Hanafi school upholds its validity while the Shafi‘i school declares it void. Understanding this dispute reveals a key principle: an invalid dower condition does not invalidate the marriage itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the Hanafi position
Describe the exchange marriage (nikah shighar) and state the Hanafi ruling: the contracts are valid (ja’iz) and each woman is entitled to mahr al-mithl.
2
Understand the Shafi‘i objection
Imam al-Shafi‘i argues that the mixed roles of dower and subject create a partnership in the vulva, which is invalid, so the marriage contract is void.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof by qiyas
The Hanafi school draws an analogy to naming wine or pig as dower: naming an item unfit for dower does not invalidate the contract but necessitates mahr al-mithl.
Note the 'illa: naming something not legally suitable as dower.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis consider the marriage valid and require mahr al-mithl; Shafi‘is require a new marriage contract with proper dower.
5
Note the tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi) because the analogy is strong and the principle that an invalid dower does not void the marriage is well-established.

A man married his daughter on the condition that the other also marry his daughter or sister to him, and both contracts become consideration for each other. Both contracts are valid and mahr al-mithl is obligatory. 'And when a man marries his daughter on the condition that the man marrying her marries his daughter or sister to him so that one of the two contracts is consideration for the other, then the two contracts are valid and each of them has mahr al-mithl. Al-Shafi'i said: the two contracts are void because he made half of the vulva as dower and half as the subject of marriage, and there is no partnership in this matter, so the declaration is void. Our proof is that he mentioned something that is not suitable as dower, so the contract is valid and mahr al-mithl is obligatory, just as when one names wine and pig (as dower). And there is no partnership without entitlement.' Translation: And when a man marries his daughter on the condition that the man marrying him marries his daughter or sister, so that one of the two contracts is consideration for the other, then both contracts are valid and for each of them there is mahr al-mithl. Imam Shafi'i said: both contracts are void because he made half of the vulva as dower and half as the subject of marriage, and there is no partnership in this matter, so the declaration is void. Our proof is that he mentioned something that is not suitable as dower, so the contract is valid and mahr al-mithl is obligatory, just as when one names wine and pig (as dower). And there is no partnership without entitlement. Commentary: The scenario is that Hamid married his daughter to Majid on the condition that Majid marry his daughter to Hamid so that each woman's vulva is the dower of the other. This marriage is called nikah shighar. 'Shighar' is derived from 'shaghura' meaning to raise and empty. Taking the meaning of raise, the reason for naming is that the spouses removed the dower from the contract. If the meaning is emptying, the reason is that this marriage is empty of dower. Some opine that 'shighar' means distance; in that case the reason is that the spouses denied the dower and distanced themselves from truth. Therefore this...
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on nikah shighar (exchange marriage), where two men marry each other's female relatives without a separate dower, making the marriage contracts themselves the consideration. The Hanafi position is that such a marriage is valid (ja'iz) and the women are entitled to mahr al-mithl (proper dower). Imam al-Shafi'i declared both contracts void because he considered that half of the vulva is made dower and the other half is the subject of marriage, which he sees as invalid due to lack of proper consideration. The Hanafi response uses qiyas (analogy): just as naming wine or pig as dower (items not valid as dower) does not invalidate the contract but instead requires mahr al-mithl, similarly naming the vulva of another as dower – which is not a valid dower – results in a valid contract with mahr al-mithl. The passage also provides a linguistic analysis of the term 'shighar', explaining its derivation and why this type of marriage is so named. The key principle is that a marriage contract is not invalidated by an invalid dower clause; instead, the contract stands and the proper dower is obligatory. This is consistent with the Hanafi principle that the dower is not a pillar (rukn) of the marriage contract but a financial obligation that can be corrected.

Key Terms
نکاح شغار (nikah shighar): A marriage where two men exchange female relatives without a separate dower, making the marriage itself the consideration.
مہر مثل (mahr al-mithl): Proper dower determined by the woman's social status, obligatory when dower is not specified or invalid.
عوض (iwad): Consideration; in this context, the marriage contract itself serves as the dower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a nikah shighar where two men exchange their daughters in marriage without a separate dower?
A) The marriage is void and both must remarry with a proper dower
B) The marriage is valid and each woman receives mahr al-mithl
C) The marriage is valid only if the women consent after the fact
D) The marriage is void because the dower is invalid

Key Takeaway
In nikah shighar, the contract remains valid despite an invalid dower condition; proper dower (mahr al-mithl) becomes wajib.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
Ruling on Nikah Shighar: Valid with Mahr al-Mithl
Determines validity of exchange marriage and compares Hanafi and Shafi'i views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates Nikah Shighar with Mahr al-Mithl and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the prohibition hadith.

Core Idea
A marriage contract is not invalidated by an invalid condition on the dower; instead, the default proper dower applies.

Nikah Shighar, an exchange marriage where the marriage itself serves as the dower, is a contested issue between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. In this lesson, we examine the ruling from Al-Hidayah, where Imam al-Marghinani presents the Hanafi position with a qiyas on wine and pork, and responds to Shafi'i's rational and hadith-based arguments. Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi principle that an invalid condition (shart fasid) does not necessarily void the underlying contract.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its core proof
Identify that the Hanafi school deems the marriages valid but requires each woman to receive mahr al-mithl. The proof is qiyas: naming something unsuitable as dower (like wine or pork) does not invalidate the contract.
The condition to use one marriage as dower is fasid, but the contract itself remains sahih.
2
Identify the opposing Shafi'i position and its rational proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds both marriages void because each man makes half his daughter's vulva a dower and the other half marriage, creating an invalid partnership in the vulva.
The Shafi'i view relies on the principle that the vulva cannot be shared between two parties.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the rational proof
The Hanafi response argues that partnership does not arise because the vulva cannot be owned by another; the condition is merely fasid and does not void the contract.
The Hanafi distinguish between ownership (milk) and right of use (intifa'), which cannot be shared.
4
Evaluate the Shafi'i hadith evidence and the Hanafi response
The Shafi'i cite hadiths 'La shighar fi al-Islam' and 'Nahi an al-shighar'. The Hanafi respond that the prohibition is on leaving the marriage without a named dower, not on the act of marriage itself, analogous to the prohibition of sale after Friday adhan.
The hadiths are interpreted as prohibiting the practice of omitting dower, not the contract structure.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Hanafi, the marriages stand and each woman gets mahr al-mithl. Under Shafi'i, the marriages are void and must be renewed with proper dower.
This difference affects legal recourse and the status of any children born.

نکاح شغار .. احناف کے نزدیک صحیح ہے۔ لیکن دونوں عورتوں میں سے ہر ایک کیلئے مہر مثل واجب ہوگا۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ دونوں عقد باطل ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے امام شافعی کی دلیل عقلی تو بیان کی ہے لیکن ان کی تائید میں جو حدیثیں ہیں ان کو ذکر نہیں فرمایا ہے۔ حالانکہ دو حدیثیں ان کا مستدل بن سکتی ہیں۔ اول ابن عمر کی حدیث لا شغار في الاسلام ۔ یعنی اسلام میں نکاح شغار کی کوئی گنجائش نہیں ہے۔ ترندی نے بھی اس حدیث کو عمران بن حصین سے روایت کیا ہے۔ اور دوسری حدیث جابر ہے جس کو مسلم نے روایت کیا۔ الفاظ حدیث یہ ہیں نھی رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن الشغار یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے نکاح شغار سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ یہ دونوں حدیثیں نکاح شغار کے عدم جواز پر شاہد عدل ہیں۔
امام شافعی کی عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ شخص جس نے اپنی بیٹی کا نکاح کیا دوسرے شخص سے اس شرط پر کہ وہ اپنی بیٹی کا نکاح مجھ سے کر دے تو گویا ان دونوں بیٹیوں میں ہر ایک کا نصف بضع مہر اور نصف آخر منکوحہ بن گیا۔ حاصل یہ کہ ہر ایک کا بضع شوہر اور اس کی بیٹی کے درمیان مشترک ہو گیا نصف بضع شوہر کیلئے ہوگا بحکم نکاح اور نصف اسکی بیٹی کیلئے ہوگا بحکم مہر ۔ پس اشتراک لازم آئے گا اور منافع بضع مشترک نہیں ہوتے جیسا کہ ایک عورت دو مردوں سے اپنا نکاح کرے یہ درست نہیں۔ پس جب اشتراک صحیح نہیں تو ایجاب باطل ہو گیا
اور جب ایجاب باطل ہو گیا تو عقدہی باطل ہوگا۔ اسلئے امام شافعی کے نزدیک دونوں عقد باطل ہیں۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں عقدوں میں ایسی چیز کو ہر بنایا گیا ہے جو مہر بنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتی ہے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ جو چیز مہر بنے کی صلاحیت نہ رکھے اگر اس کو مہر بنا دیا جائے تو عقد نکاح صحیح اور مہر مثل واجب ہوگا۔ مثلا خم اور خنزیرکومبر بنا دیا تو نکاح صحیح ہے اور مہر مثل واجب ہوگا۔ ایسے ہی یہاں بھی ہوگا۔ امام شافعی کی عقلی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ بضع جب مہر بنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا تو اشتراک بھی محقق نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ایک عورت کے منافع بضع دوسری عورت کے مملوک نہیں بن سکتے ہیں۔ پس جب شرکت ثابت نہیں ہوئی تو بضع کو مہر بنانے کی شرط ، شرط فاسد ہوگی اور نکاح شرط فاسد سے باطل نہیں ہوتا بلکہ خود شرط فاسد، باطل ہو جاتی ہیں۔ لہذا اس نکاح شغار میں بضع کو مہر بنانے کی شرط باطل ہو جائے گی اور نکاح درست ہوگا اور شوہر پر مہر مثل واجب ہوگا۔
امام شافعی کی جانب سے پیش کردہ حدیثوں کا جواب یہ ہے کہ نبی عین نکاح کیلئے نہیں ہے بلکہ حدیث میں نبی وارد ہوئی یہ ہے نکاح کو تسمیہ مہر سے خالی کرنے کی وجہ سے۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا مقصد عین نکاح سے منع کرنا نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کی ممانعت کی کہ نکاح کو تسمیہ مہر سے خالی رکھا جائے اور تسمیہ مہر سے اگر نکاح کو خالی رکھا گیا تو اس سے نکاح باطل نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ اذان جمعہ کے بعد بیع سے منع کیا گیا ہے تو یہاں نفس بیع ممنوع نہیں بلکہ اذان جمعہ کے وقت ممنوع ہے۔
A man married his daughter on condition that the other man marry his daughter or sister to him, so that the two contracts become one the price of the other. The two contracts are valid and each woman is entitled to mahr al-mithl. Imam Shafi'i said: The two contracts are invalid because he made half the vulva as dower and the other half as the married woman, and there is no partnership in this matter, so the offer is invalid. Our proof: He named something that is not suitable as dower, so the contract is valid and mahr al-mithl is obligatory, just as when one names wine or pork [as dower]. And there is no partnership without entitlement. Translation: And when a man marries his daughter on condition that the married (the groom) marry his daughter or sister, so that one of the contracts becomes the price of the other, then both contracts are valid and each woman gets mahr al-mithl. Imam Shafi'i said: Both contracts are invalid because he made half the vulva as dower and half the married woman, and there is no partnership in this matter, so the offer is invalid. Our proof: He mentioned something that does not have the capacity to be dower, so the contract is valid and mahr al-mithl is obligatory, like when one names wine and pork. And partnership does not occur without entitlement. Explanation: The scenario is: Hamid married his daughter to Majid on condition that Majid marry his daughter to Hamid, so that one's vulva becomes the mahr of the other. This marriage is called nikah shighar. Shighar is derived from shu'ur... and the meaning of shighar is lifting and emptying... The author of Hidayah has stated the rational proof of Imam Shafi'i but did not mention the hadiths that support it, although two hadiths could be used: Ibn Umar's hadith 'La shighar fi al-Islam' and Jabir's hadith narrated by Muslim: 'Nahi Rasulullah sallallahu alaihi wasallam an al-shighar'. These are witnesses against permissibility. Shafi'i's rational proof: The man made half the vulva of each woman as dower and the other half as married, so partnership in vulva arises which is invalid. Our proof: The vulva is not suitable as dower, so by qiyas on wine and pork, the contract is valid with mahr al-mithl. Response to Shafi'i's rational proof: Since vulva cannot be dower, partnership does not arise; the condition is fasid and does not void the marriage. Response to hadith: The prohibition is on leaving the marriage without naming a dower, not on the marriage itself, like the prohibition of sale after Friday adhan.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on Nikah Shighar, an exchange marriage where two men marry each other's daughters or sisters with the marriage itself as the dower. The Hanafi school holds that such contracts are valid, but each woman is entitled to mahr al-mithl (proper dower) because the condition to use the marriage as dower is invalid (fasid) but does not void the marriage. Imam Shafi'i argues that both marriages are void because it creates a share in the vulva. The author of Hidayah provides the Hanafi response: using something that is not suitable as dower (like wine or pork) does not invalidate the marriage; rather, it makes the condition void and mahr al-mithl obligatory. The passage also responds to Shafi'i's hadith evidence ('La shighar fi al-Islam', 'Nahi an al-shighar') by arguing that the prohibition is against leaving the marriage without named dower, not against the marriage itself. The analogy is made to the prohibition of selling after Friday adhan, which restricts timing not the act itself.

Key Terms
شغار (shighar): An exchange marriage where two men marry each other's female relatives and the marriage itself serves as the dower.
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower equivalent to that of women of similar status to the bride.
بضع (bud'): Vulva or sexual organ, used metonymically for the right to sexual enjoyment.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): An invalid condition in a contract that does not void the contract itself but is itself void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on Nikah Shighar?
A) Both marriages are invalid
B) Both marriages are valid but each woman gets mahr al-mithl
C) Both marriages are valid and the condition is valid
D) One marriage is valid, the other is invalid

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an invalid dower condition does not void a marriage; rather, the default mahr al-mithl applies, as in the case of Nikah Shighar.

Nikah — Marriage

Service or Teaching Quran as Mahr: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on marrying with condition of service or teaching Quran as dower and intra-Hanafi differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a man marries with the condition of service or teaching as dower, identify the intra-Hanafi difference, and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Service or teaching the Quran is not valid dower; the wife gets mahr al-mithl.

This lesson examines a case where a man marries a woman with the condition that he will serve her for a year or teach her the Quran as her dower (mahr). While the marriage is valid, the specified dower is not considered valid in the Hanafi school because it is not tangible property (mal mutaqawwim) at the time of contract. There is an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether the wife receives mahr al-mithl (proper dower) or the value of the service. We will explore the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and also note the cross-madhhab view of Imam Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is marriage with a condition of service or teaching as the dower. According to all Hanafi imams, the marriage itself is sahih (valid), but the condition regarding the specified dower is fasid (invalid).
The validity of marriage is separate from the validity of the dower condition.
2
Determine the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the proper dower) because the specified service or teaching is not mal mutaqawwim (valuable property) at the time of the contract. The condition is thus void and the default dower applies.
This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
3
Contrast with Muhammad al-Shaybani
Muhammad al-Shaybani argues that the wife is entitled to the value of the service (or teaching), because service has monetary value and can be measured. He considers the condition effective to that extent.
This is a minority view within the Hanafi school.
4
Apply the mufta bihi and note the slave exception
The mufta bihi is mahr al-mithl (al-fatwa 'ala qawl al-imamayn). However, if a slave marries with his master's permission on condition of his service, the service can be valid dower because the slave has no property and the master's permission gives value.
This exception avoids hardship for slaves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک سال کی خدمت یا تعلیم قرآن کو مہر مقرر کر نے کا حکم
وان تزوج حرامرأة على خدمته اياها سنة او على تعليم القرآن فلها مهر مثلها وقال محمد لها قيمة خدمته و ان تزوج عبد امرأة باذن مولاه على خدمته سنة جازولها خدمته وقال الشافعى لها تعليم القرآن والخدمة في الوجهين
The ruling on making service for one year or teaching the Quran as dower. And if a free man marries a woman on condition of her service for one year or on teaching the Quran, then she is entitled to mahr al-mithl. And Muhammad (al-Shaybani) said: She is entitled to the value of his service. And if a slave marries a woman with his master's permission on condition of his service for one year, it is valid and she is entitled to his service. And al-Shafi'i said: She is entitled to teaching the Quran and service in both cases.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on valid dower. If a man marries a woman with the condition that he will serve her for a year or teach her the Quran as dower, the marriage is valid but the dower is not fixed by that condition. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, she gets mahr al-mithl (proper dower) because the specified service or teaching is not a valid dower. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that she gets the value of the service, because service has value and can be taken as compensation for the vulva. For a slave, with his master's permission, the service can be valid dower. Imam Shafi'i says she is entitled to the teaching or service as specified. The Hanafi position is that service and teaching are not suitable as dower because they are not tangible property (mal mutaqawwim) at the time of contract, so the condition is fasid, and mahr al-mithl is obligatory.

Key Terms
خدمت (khidmah): Personal service, here specified as service for one year as dower.
تعلیم القرآن (ta'lim al-Quran): Teaching of the Quran, specified as dower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a free man marries a woman with the condition that he will teach her the Quran as mahr, what is the ruling?
A) Marriage is invalid
B) Marriage is valid and she gets the teaching
C) Marriage is valid and she gets mahr al-mithl
D) Marriage is valid and she gets value of teaching

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, marriage with a condition of service or teaching as mahr is valid, but the wife receives mahr al-mithl, not the specified service/teaching.

Nikah Shighar: Valid or Invalid?
Inter-madhhab dispute with rational and textual proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on Nikah Shighar and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the concepts of shart fasid and mahr al-mithl.

Core Idea
A void condition (shart fasid) does not invalidate the marriage — the contract stands with mahr al-mithl.

Nikah Shighar — where two men exchange their daughters in marriage, each conditioning the other's marriage on his own — is a well-known point of ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. In this passage, the author of al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi ruling, then cites and refutes the Shafi'i rational and textual proofs. You will learn why the Hanafis uphold the validity of both marriages and how they interpret the Prophetic prohibitions.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling of the Hanafi school on Nikah Shighar: both marriages are valid (sahih), and each woman is entitled to mahr al-mithl.
The mahr specified (the vulva) is invalid, but the contract is not affected.
2
Identify the Shafi'i proofs
Note the two lines of evidence Imam al-Shafi'i employs: (1) rational argument based on impermissible sharing of the vulva, and (2) hadiths prohibiting shighar.
The passage mentions two hadiths: 'La shighar fi al-Islam' and the explicit prohibition.
3
Follow the Hanafi response to each proof
Analyse how the Hanafis rebut each Shafi'i argument: the vulva cannot be mahr, so no sharing occurs; the condition is merely fasid (void). The hadiths are interpreted as prohibiting omission of mahr specification, not the marriage itself.
The analogy with wine/pork as mahr illustrates the principle: an invalid mahr does not nullify the contract.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical consequence of the dispute: under Hanafi law, the marriages remain valid and mahr al-mithl is due; under Shafi'i law, both marriages are batil and the couples must separate.
This difference affects the status of any children and financial obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم کا نام نکاح شغار رکھا گیا ہے۔
102
کتاب النکاح
نکاح شغار .. احناف کے نزدیک صحیح ہے۔ لیکن دونوں عورتوں میں سے ہر ایک کیلئے مہر مثل واجب ہوگا۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ دونوں عقد باطل ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے امام شافعی کی دلیل عقلی تو بیان کی ہے لیکن ان کی تائید میں جو حدیثیں ہیں ان کو ذکر نہیں فرمایا ہے۔ حالانکہ دو حدیثیں ان کا مستدل بن سکتی ہیں۔ اول ابن عمر کی حدیث لا شغار في الاسلام ۔ یعنی اسلام میں نکاح شغار کی کوئی گنجائش نہیں ہے۔ ترندی نے بھی اس حدیث کو عمران بن حصین سے روایت کیا ہے۔ اور دوسری حدیث جابر ہے جس کو مسلم نے روایت کیا۔ الفاظ حدیث یہ ہیں نھی رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن الشغار یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے نکاح شغار سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ یہ دونوں حدیثیں نکاح شغار کے عدم جواز پر شاہد عدل ہیں۔
امام شافعی کی عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ شخص جس نے اپنی بیٹی کا نکاح کیا دوسرے شخص سے اس شرط پر کہ وہ اپنی بیٹی کا نکاح مجھ سے کر دے تو گویا ان دونوں بیٹیوں میں ہر ایک کا نصف بضع مہر اور نصف آخر منکوحہ بن گیا۔ حاصل یہ کہ ہر ایک کا بضع شوہر اور اس کی بیٹی کے درمیان مشترک ہو گیا نصف بضع شوہر کیلئے ہوگا بحکم نکاح اور نصف اسکی بیٹی کیلئے ہوگا بحکم مہر ۔ پس اشتراک لازم آئے گا اور منافع بضع مشترک نہیں ہوتے جیسا کہ ایک عورت دو مردوں سے اپنا نکاح کرے یہ درست نہیں۔ پس جب اشتراک صحیح نہیں تو ایجاب باطل ہو گیا اور جب ایجاب باطل ہو گیا تو عقدہی باطل ہوگا۔ اسلئے امام شافعی کے نزدیک دونوں عقد باطل ہیں۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں عقدوں میں ایسی چیز کو ہر بنایا گیا ہے جو مہر بنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتی ہے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ جو چیز مہر بنے کی صلاحیت نہ رکھے اگر اس کو مہر بنا دیا جائے تو عقد نکاح صحیح اور مہر مثل واجب ہوگا۔ مثلا خم اور خنزیرکومبر بنا دیا تو نکاح صحیح ہے اور مہر مثل واجب ہوگا۔ ایسے ہی یہاں بھی ہوگا۔ امام شافعی کی عقلی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ بضع جب مہر بنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا تو اشتراک بھی محقق نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ایک عورت کے منافع بضع دوسری عورت کے مملوک نہیں بن سکتے ہیں۔ پس جب شرکت ثابت نہیں ہوئی تو بضع کو مہر بنانے کی شرط ، شرط فاسد ہوگی اور نکاح شرط فاسد سے باطل نہیں ہوتا بلکہ خود شرط فاسد، باطل ہو جاتی ہیں۔ لہذا اس نکاح شغار میں بضع کو مہر بنانے کی شرط باطل ہو جائے گی اور نکاح درست ہوگا اور شوہر پر مہر مثل واجب ہوگا۔
امام شافعی کی جانب سے پیش کردہ حدیثوں کا جواب یہ ہے کہ نبی عین نکاح کیلئے نہیں ہے بلکہ حدیث میں نبی وارد ہوئی یہ ہے نکاح کو تسمیہ مہر سے خالی کرنے کی وجہ سے۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا مقصد عین نکاح سے منع کرنا نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کی ممانعت کی کہ نکاح کو تسمیہ مہر سے خالی رکھا جائے اور تسمیہ مہر سے اگر نکاح کو خالی رکھا گیا تو اس سے نکاح باطل نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ اذان جمعہ کے بعد بیع سے منع کیا گیا ہے تو یہاں نفس بیع ممنوع نہیں بلکہ اذان جمعہ کے وقت ممنوع ہے۔
The name of this section is Nikah Shighar. According to the Hanafis, it is valid, but each of the two women is entitled to mahr al-mithl. Imam al-Shafi'i said both contracts are invalid. The author of al-Hidayah mentioned al-Shafi'i's rational proof but did not mention the hadiths that support it, although two hadiths could be their evidence. First: the hadith of Ibn 'Umar 'La shighar fi al-Islam' (no shighar in Islam). Al-Tirmidhi also narrated it from 'Imran ibn Husayn. Second: the hadith of Jabir narrated by Muslim: 'Naha Rasul Allah salla Allah 'alayhi wa sallam 'an al-shighar' (the Messenger of Allah forbade shighar). These two hadiths are just witnesses against the permissibility of Nikah Shighar. Al-Shafi'i's rational proof: The man who marries his daughter to another on condition that the other marries his daughter to him — then each of the two daughters, half of her vulva becomes mahr and the other half becomes the object of marriage. So the vulva of each is shared between the husband and his daughter: half for the husband by marriage, half for his daughter as mahr. Thus sharing (ishtirak) occurs, and the benefits of the vulva cannot be shared, just as one woman marrying two men is invalid. Since sharing is not valid, the offer is invalid, and thus the contract is invalid. Therefore both contracts are invalid according to al-Shafi'i. Our proof: In both contracts, something that is not capable of being mahr has been made mahr, and the rule is: if something incapable of being mahr is specified as mahr, the marriage contract is valid and mahr al-mithl is obligatory — e.g., if wine or pork is specified as mahr, the marriage is valid and mahr al-mithl is due. The same applies here. Response to al-Shafi'i's rational proof: Since the vulva is not capable of being mahr, sharing does not actually occur, because the benefits of one woman's vulva cannot be owned by another woman. When sharing is not established, the condition of making the vulva mahr is a void condition (shart fasid), and a marriage is not invalidated by a void condition; rather the condition itself is void. Therefore in this Nikah Shighar, the condition of making the vulva mahr becomes void, the marriage is valid, and the husband must pay mahr al-mithl. Response to the hadiths presented by al-Shafi'i: The prohibition (nahy) is not for the marriage itself, but the hadith prohibits leaving the marriage empty of the specification of mahr (tasmiyat al-mahr). The intent is not to forbid the marriage itself, but to forbid leaving it without specifying mahr; and if it is left without specifying mahr, the marriage is not invalid. Just as selling after the Friday adhan is prohibited, the sale itself is not prohibited, but selling at that time.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage addresses the dispute regarding Nikah Shighar. The text first states the Hanafi position: Nikah Shighar is valid (sahih), but each woman receives mahr al-mithl. Then it presents the Shafi'i position that both contracts are invalid. The author notes that al-Hidayah only mentioned al-Shafi'i's rational proof but omitted two hadiths that support it: 'La shighar fi al-Islam' (Ibn 'Umar) and the explicit prohibition by the Prophet (Jabir). Al-Shafi'i's rational proof argues that in Nikah Shighar, each woman's vulva (bud') becomes shared between the husband and his daughter, leading to impermissible sharing. The Hanafi response: The vulva is not capable of being mahr, so no actual sharing occurs. The condition making the vulva mahr is void (shart fasid), but the marriage remains valid with mahr al-mithl, analogous to specifying wine or pork as mahr. As for the hadiths, the Hanafis interpret the prohibition as applying to leaving the marriage without specifying any mahr (tasmiyat al-mahr), not to the contract itself. The marriage without mahr specification is valid in Hanafi fiqh, so the hadith is not a prohibition of the contract but of a practice that omits mahr. The analogy with Friday adhan illustrates that the prohibition targets the circumstance, not the act itself.

Key Terms
نکاح شغار (nikah shighar): A marriage where two men exchange their daughters or female wards in marriage, each making the other's marriage conditional on his own.
مہر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr equivalent to that of women of similar status (e.g., paternal relatives) when no mahr is specified or an invalid mahr is specified.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): A condition that is void (invalid) but does not nullify the contract; the condition itself is disregarded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi exposition in this lesson, why does the void condition (shart fasid) not invalidate the Nikah Shighar contract?
A) Because the condition is not mention in the contract itself.
B) Because the vulva cannot be made mahr, so no actual sharing occurs; the condition is merely fasid.
C) Because the Prophet's prohibition was only for non-Arabs.
D) Because the women consented to the exchange.

Key Takeaway
In Nikah Shighar, the Hanafi school rules both marriages valid (sahih) with mahr al-mithl, because the invalid condition (specifying the vulva as mahr) is shart fasid and does not invalidate the contract.

Ruling on Setting Service or Teaching Quran as Mahr
Discusses the validity of mahr being a year's service or teaching Quran, with Hanafi and Shafi'i views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi and Shafi'i rulings on mahr being service or teaching, and apply the Hanafi position with its intra-madhhab differences.

Core Idea
Mahr must be property; a free husband's service or teaching Quran cannot be mahr due to qalb al-mawdu'.

This lesson examines the validity of mahr when specified as a year of service or teaching the Quran. The Hanafi school holds that these are not valid mahr for a free husband, but differs on the consequence: mahr al-mithl (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf) or value of service (Muhammad). The Shafi'i school allows them as valid mahr. We will trace the proofs, the concept of qalb al-mawdu' (inversion of the subject), and the practical differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenarios
Note the two scenarios: free husband vs slave husband. The ruling differs based on the husband's status. Also note the condition: service or teaching.
Free husband's service is the main point of dispute.
2
State the Hanafi Ruling and Intra-Madhhab Ikhtilaf
For a free husband: Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf say mahr al-mithl; Muhammad says value of service. For a slave husband with master's permission: service is valid mahr.
The slave case is distinct because the service effectively belongs to the master.
3
Understand the Shafi'i Argument
Shafi'i holds that anything suitable for compensation by condition can be mahr, analogizing to service of another free man with consent or herding goats.
This is based on the idea of mu'awada (exchange).
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
Hanafis argue mahr must be property (mal). Teaching is not property. Free husband's service cannot be entitled due to qalb al-mawdu'—the husband serving the wife inverts the marital hierarchy. Distinguish from other valid analogies.
Key distinctions: no contradiction in another's service or domestic work.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Difference)
Hanafis: free husband's service/teaching is not mahr; mahr al-mithl or value is due. Shafi'is: the specified service/teaching constitutes the mahr.
The difference affects what the wife is entitled to claim.

Ruling on setting a year's service or teaching the Quran as mahr: And if a free man marries a woman on condition of his serving her for a year or on condition of teaching the Quran, then she is entitled to her mahr al-mithl. Muhammad said: She is entitled to the value of his service. And if a slave marries a woman with his master's permission on condition of his serving her for a year, it is permissible, and she is entitled to his service. Al-Shafi'i said: She is entitled to teaching the Quran and the service in both cases. Because that which is suitable to take compensation for by condition is suitable as mahr according to him, for thereby consideration (mu'awada) is realized. It is as if he married her on condition of the service of another free man with his consent, or on condition of the husband herding her goats. Our proof: What is legislated is the seeking of compensation with property (mal), and teaching is not property, and likewise benefits according to our usul. The service of a slave is seeking compensation with property because it implies delivery of the slave's person (raqaba). The free man is not like that. Because the service of the free husband cannot be entitled by the marriage contract due to the inversion of the subject (qalb al-mawdu'). Unlike the service of another free man with his consent, because there is no contradiction (munaqada). Unlike the service of a slave, because he serves his master in meaning, since he serves her by his master's permission and command. Unlike herding goats, because it is among domestic affairs, so no contradiction. Moreover, in one narration it is not even acknowledged. Then according to Muhammad's statement, the value of the service is obligatory because the specified thing is property, but he is unable to deliver it due to contradiction, so it becomes like marrying on [the service of] another's slave. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's statement, mahr al-mithl is obligatory because service is not property, since it is not entitled in any case, so it becomes like specifying wine and pork. This is because its valuation (taqawwum) in a contract is for necessity, so when delivery is not obligatory in the marriage contract, its taqawwum does not appear, so the ruling remains on the original, which is mahr al-mithl.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage addresses the validity of mahr being a year's service or teaching the Quran. It presents the dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is, and also an intra-Hanafi dispute. The text first gives the ruling: if a free man marries a woman on condition of his service or teaching Quran, she gets mahr al-mithl according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; Imam Muhammad says she gets the value of the service. If a slave marries with his master's permission on condition of his service, it is permissible and she gets that service. Shafi'i says she gets the teaching or service in both cases because anything that can be taken as compensation by condition can be mahr. The Hanafi response: The legislated principle is that mahr must be property (mal). Teaching Quran is not property. Benefits (manafi') of a free husband are not property in marriage because they are not independently transferable; they cannot be the subject of a contract due to qalb al-mawdu' (inversion of the subject, i.e., the husband's service would invert the roles). A slave's service is valid because it effectively belongs to the master, and the slave serves by the master's permission. Another free man's service with his consent is also valid because no contradiction exists. Herding goats is domestic work, no contradiction. Thus, the service of a free husband cannot be mahr. Muhammad's view: Since the specified service is property but delivery is impossible due to contradiction, it becomes like marrying on the service of another's slave (where the value is due). Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: Service is not property at all in marriage, so mahr al-mithl is due, like wine/pork. The text explains taqawwum (valuation) only appears in contracts where delivery is obligatory; here it is not, so the original ruling of mahr al-mithl remains.

Key Terms
قلب موضوع (qalb al-mawdu'): Inversion of the subject: the husband serving the wife contradicts the marital relationship where the husband is the head; thus such a condition is invalid.
تقوم (taqawwum): Valuation or consideration in law; something that can be evaluated and compensated.
منافع (manafi'): Benefits or usufruct; here referring to services that could be considered as compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what is the mahr when a free man marries a woman on condition of teaching the Quran?
A) The value of teaching.
B) Mahr al-mithl.
C) The specified teaching is the mahr.
D) No mahr is due.

Key Takeaway
Mahr must be property; a free husband's service or teaching Quran cannot be mahr, but the marriage remains valid with mahr al-mithl due.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Can Teaching Quran or Husband's Service Be Valid Mahr?
Dispute over validity of service/teaching as dower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr consisting of teaching Quran or husband's service, explain the evidence (Quran 4:24 and concept of mal), and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad on the consequence.

Core Idea
Service of a free husband as mahr inverts marital roles, so proper dower is due.

This passage from Al-Hidayah examines a dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is over what can constitute mahr. The Shafi'i school allows teaching Quran and service as mahr, while the Hanafi school restricts mahr to property (mal) that can persist. The passage also highlights an intra-Hanafi difference: while both sides agree that teaching Quran and free husband's service cannot be valid mahr, Imam Muhammad rules that the value of the service is due, whereas Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule that the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) is owed. Understanding this debate clarifies the Hanafi definition of property and the purpose of marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i position and its dalil
Read the passage to find how Imam al-Shafi'i justifies teaching Quran and free service as valid mahr. Note his principle: anything that can be a consideration (iwad) by condition can be mahr, because marriage is an exchange (mu'awada).
The Shafi'i examples: service of another free man with his consent, and the husband tending his wife's goats.
2
Identify the Hanafi dalil
Find the Quranic verse (4:24) cited by the Hanafis: '...that you seek with your wealth' (an tabtaghu bi-amwalikum). Understand how the word 'amwalikum' (your wealth) restricts the dower to property (mal). Also note the Hanafi definition: property must persist over time; services (manafi') do not persist, so they are not mal.
The dalil_block has full details: dalil_type = Quran, thubut = qati, dalala = zanni (because it requires interpretation of 'amwal' to exclude services).
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal: qalb al-mawdu'
The passage argues that a husband's service as mahr inverts the natural order (qalb al-mawdu'): the husband becomes a servant and the wife becomes the one served. This contradicts the purpose of marriage (al-bu'dha al-tabi'iyya). Determine why service of another free man or a slave does not cause this inversion.
Service of another free man with his consent does not invert marital roles; a slave's service is actually service to his master, not his wife (since he serves with the master's permission).
4
Distinguish between slave's service and free man's service
The Hanafi view permits a slave's service as mahr because it entails surrender of his person (raqabah), which is property. A free man's service does not involve surrender of person, so it is not property. Confirm this distinction in the passage.
Also note that tending goats (ra'i al-ghanam) is permissible as mahr because it is part of marital duties, not a service that inverts roles.
5
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Muhammad and the two seniors
Find the lines where Imam Muhammad says the value of the service is due (qimat al-khidma) vs. Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf who say the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) is due. Understand the reasoning: Muhammad considers the named thing (service) as property but impossible to deliver, so its value is due; the two seniors consider service not property at all, so the original rule (proper dower) applies.
The mufta bihi position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: proper dower is due.
