عورت نے پانچ سو پر قبضہ کیا پھر ہزار پورا ہبہ کر دیا ، پھر مرد نے دخول سے پہلے طلاق دیدی ایک دوسرے پر رجوع نہیں کریں گے
ولـوقبضت خمس مائة ثم وهبت الالف كلها المقبوض وغيره اووهبت الباقى ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بهالم يرجع واحد منهما على صاحبه بشيء عند ابي حنيفة وقالا يرجع عليها بنصف ما قبضت اعتبارا للبعض بالكل ولان هبة البعض حط فيلحق باصل العقد ولابي حنيفة ان مقصود الزوج حصل وهو سلامة نصف الصداق بلاعوض فلا يستوجب الرجوع عند الطلاق والحط لا يلتحق باصل العقد في النكاح الاترى ان الزيادة فيه لا تلتحق حتى لا تنصف
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم
ترجمہ اور اگر عورت نے قبضہ کیا پانچ سودرہم پر پھر ہبہ کر دیا کل کے کل کو مقبوض اور غیر مقبوض یا ہبہ کر دیا باقی کو۔ پھر طلاق دی اس کے ساتھ دخول سے پہلے تو ان دونوں میں سے کوئی کسی پر رجوع نہ کرے ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ عورت سے رجوع کرے نصف مقبوض کو بعض کو کل پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور اسلئے کہ بعض کا ہبہ کم کرنا ہے۔ پس خط یعنی کم کرنا لاحق ہو گا اصل عقد کے ساتھ ۔ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر کا مقصود حاصل ہو گیا اور وہ نصف مہر کا سلامت رہنا ہے بلاعوض ۔ پس طلاق کے وقت رجوع کا مستحق نہیں ہوگا۔ اور حط ( کم کرنا ) اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں ہوتا ہے، نکاح میں۔ کیا تو نے غور نہیں کیا کہ نکاح میں زیادتی ( اصل عقد کے ساتھ ) لاحق نہیں ہوتی ہے چنانچہ زیادتی کی تنصیف نہیں ہوگی۔ تشریح اب صورت یہ ہے کہ عورت نے پانچ سو درہم پر قبضہ کیا اور پھر شوہر کیلئے ایک ہزار مقبوض اور غیر مقبوض دونوں کو ہبہ کر دیا یا صرف غیر مقبوض کو ہبہ کر دیا اور طلاق قبل الدخول واقع ہو گئی تو زوجین میں سے کسی کو کسی پر رجوع کا حق نہیں ہوگا امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین کا مسلک یہ ہے کہ شوہر نصف مقبوض یعنی دو سو پچاس درہم رجوع کرلے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ بعض کو کل پر قیاس کرتے ہیں چنانچہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر عورت کل پر قبضہ کرتی اور شوہر کیلئے ہبہ کر دیتی پھر شوہر اس کو طلاق قبل الدخول دے دیتا تو ہمارے نزدیک شوہر عورت سے نصف مقبوض رجوع کرتا پس ایسے ہی جب عورت نے بعض پر قبضہ کیا تو اس بعض کے نصف پر رجوع کا حق ہوگا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بعض کا ہبہ یعنی نصف غیر مقبوض کا ہبہ عورت کی طرف سے خط ہے یعنی کم کر دینا اور حط لاحق ہوتا ہے اصل عقد کے ساتھ تو گویا شوہر نے ابتداء ہی پانچ سومقبوض پر نکاح کیا ہے۔ پس یہ پانچ سو درہم کل مہر ہوں گے۔ اور کل مہر کے بارے میں حکم گذر چکا کہ اگر کل مہر پر قبضہ کر کے عورت پورے مہر کو ہبہ کردے تو نصف کے رجوع کا حق رہتا ہے۔ لہذا ایسے ہی یہاں بھی نصف مقبوض کے رجوع کا حق حاصل ہوگا۔
امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر کا مقصود ہے بلاعوض نصف مہر کا سلامت رہنا۔ اور یہ مقصود طلاق سے پہلے ہی حاصل ہو چکا۔ ہوم ہے کا رہنا۔ یہ پہلےہی ہو اور لہذا طلاق کے بعد رجوع کا مستحق نہیں ہوگا۔ صاحبین کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حط نکاح میں اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں ہوتا ہے وجہ یہ ہے کہ مثلاً ایک آدمی نے کسی عورت سے ہیں درہم پر نکاح کیا عورت نے پندرہ در ہم شوہر کو ہبہ کر دئیے۔ تو اب شوہر پر دس درہم واجب نہیں ہوں گے۔ بلکہ پانچ درہم واجب ہوں گے ۔ اگر حط اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق ہوتا تو ایسا ہو جا تا گویا کہ شوہر نے پانچ درہم پر نکاح کیا ہے۔ اور پانچ درہم پر اگر نکاح کیا جائے تو دس درہم واجب ہوتے ہیں۔ لہذا اس صورت میں دس درہم واجب ہونے چاہئیں تھے۔ حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ شوہر پر پانچ ہی واجب ہیں۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ حط اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے خط کے اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق نہ ہونے کی ایک وجہ یہ بیان کی ہے کہ نکاح میں زیادتی بالاتفاق اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں ہوتی ۔ مثلاً شوہر نے مہر سمی پر پچاس درہم زیادہ کر دیے اور پھر طلاق قبل الدخول دے دی تو ان پچاس کی تنصیف نہیں ہوگی لہذا جس طرح زیادتی اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں ہوتی۔ اسی طرح حط بھی اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق نہ ہونا چاہئے۔
And if she took possession of five hundred then gifted the entire thousand, both what was possessed and what was not, or gifted the remainder, then he divorced her before consummation, neither of them shall reclaim anything from the other according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Sahibayn) said: he reclaims from her half of what she took possession of, drawing an analogy from the part to the whole, and because the gift of a part is a reduction (hatt) that attaches to the original contract. Abu Hanifa's proof: the husband's objective is attained, which is the safety of half the dower without compensation, so he does not deserve reclaim upon divorce. And reduction does not attach to the original contract in marriage. Do you not see that an increase does not attach to it, so that it is not apportioned? Translation: And if the woman took possession of five hundred dirhams, then gifted the entire amount, both possessed and non-possessed, or gifted the remainder, then he divorced her before consummation, then neither of them reclaims anything from the other according to Abu Hanifa. The two companions said: he reclaims from her half of what she took possession of, drawing an analogy from the part to the whole, and because the gift of a part is a reduction that attaches to the original contract. And Abu Hanifa's proof is that the husband's objective is attained—the safety of half the dower without compensation—so he does not deserve reclaim at divorce. And reduction does not attach to the original contract in marriage. Have you not considered that an increase does not attach to it, so that it is not apportioned? Explanation: Now the scenario is that the woman took possession of five hundred dirhams, then gifted to the husband the entire thousand, both possessed and non-possessed, or only gifted the non-possessed, and divorce before consummation occurred. Then neither spouse has the right to reclaim according to Abu Hanifa. The position of the two companions is that the husband reclaims half of what she took possession of, i.e., two hundred and fifty dirhams. Their proof: they analogize the part to the whole. They say: if the woman had taken possession of the whole and gifted it to the husband, then he divorced her before consummation, then according to us the husband reclaims half of what she took possession of. Similarly, when she took possession of a part, he has the right to reclaim half of that part. Their second proof: the gift of a part (i.e., the half she did not possess) is a reduction (hatt) from the wife. And reduction attaches to the original contract, so it is as if the husband contracted marriage initially with the five hundred that she possessed. Thus these five hundred become the entire mahr. And the ruling for the entire mahr has passed: if she possesses the entire mahr and gifts it, he has the right to reclaim half. Hence here too he has the right to reclaim half of what she possessed. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: the husband's objective is the safety of half the mahr without compensation. This objective is already attained before divorce. So he does not deserve to reclaim after divorce. The response to the companions' proof: reduction does not attach to the original contract in marriage. For example, a man marries a woman with twenty dirhams. The woman gifts fifteen dirhams to the husband. Then he is not liable for ten dirhams but only five. If reduction attached to the original contract, it would be as if he married with five dirhams, and if marriage were with five dirhams, ten dirhams would be obligatory. But that is not the case; only five are obligatory. So it is known that reduction does not attach. The author of al-Hidayah gave another reason: increase in marriage does not attach by consensus. For example, the husband adds fifty dirhams to the specified dower, then divorces before consummation; these fifty are not apportioned. So just as increase does not attach, reduction also should not attach.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), regarding a scenario where the wife receives only half of the mahr (500 out of 1000 dirhams) and then either gifts the entire mahr (including the half she hasn't received) or gifts only the remaining half, and divorce occurs before consummation. The issue is whether the husband can reclaim half of what the wife actually received (i.e., 250 dirhams). Abu Hanifa says no—neither party can reclaim anything. The Sahibayn say yes—the husband can reclaim half of what she received (250). Their reasoning is based on qiyas (analogy): if she had received the entire mahr and then gifted it, the husband would reclaim half of what she received. Here, since she received only part, the same applies proportionally. They also argue that the gift of the part she didn't receive is a reduction (hatt) of the mahr, and such a reduction should retroactively affect the original contract, making it as if the agreed mahr was only the amount she actually possessed. Therefore, her possession of 500 becomes the entire mahr, and since she possessed it and then gifted it, the husband can reclaim half of it. Abu Hanifa counters that the husband's objective—being free from half the mahr without paying compensation—is already achieved when the wife gifts the whole mahr (regardless of possession). Hence, no reclaim is needed. He further argues that reduction (hatt) does not attach to the original contract in marriage. He gives an example: if the mahr is 20 dirhams and the wife gifts 15, the husband is liable for only 5, not 10. If reduction did attach, it would be as if the marriage was contracted for 5 dirhams, but then the mahr would be 10 (since minimum mahr is 10). That doesn't happen, proving hatt doesn't attach. Additionally, increase in marriage contract does not attach—if the husband adds 50 to the mahr after marriage and then divorces before consummation, that addition is not halved. Since increase doesn't attach, reduction also shouldn't. This establishes the Hanafi ruling that the husband cannot reclaim in this scenario.

Key Terms
حط (hatt): A reduction of the mahr by the wife's gift of a part; here, the claim that it retroactively modifies the original marriage contract.
تنصیف (tansif): Halving of the mahr upon divorce before consummation; the question is whether an addition or reduction undergoes tansif.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, when a wife receives half the mahr (500) and then gifts the entire mahr (1000) to the husband before divorce before consummation, what is the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) The husband reclaims half of what she received (250).
B) The husband reclaims the entire 500 that she received.
C) Neither spouse reclaims anything from the other.
D) The husband can reclaim half of the entire mahr (500).

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a wife's gift of mahr before divorce does not give the husband a right to reclaim half of what she received, because reduction (hatt) does not attach to the marriage contract.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Wife's Hibah of Possessed Mahr and Talaq Before Consummation: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ruju'
Intra-Hanafi dispute on husband's right to reclaim half of gifted mahr after talaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the husband's right to reclaim half of gifted mahr after talaq before consummation, and explain the reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
In marriage, reduction (hatt) does not attach to the original contract, so a gifted portion of mahr cannot be reclaimed by the husband.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a scenario where a wife possesses part of her mahr, gifts it (or the remainder) to her husband, and is subsequently divorced before consummation. The core question is whether the husband can reclaim half of the possessed portion. Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differ on the answer, and their debate reveals a fundamental principle about the non-attachment of reduction (hatt) to the marriage contract.

Guided Path
1
1. State the fact pattern
Identify the scenario: wife possesses part of mahr, then gifts it (or the unpossessed part) to husband, then talaq before consummation.
The key is that the wife gifts what she has already taken possession of.
2
2. Identify the dispute
State the exact disagreement: Abu Hanifa says no ruju' (husband cannot reclaim), Sahibayn say husband reclaims half of the possessed portion.
3
3. Examine Sahibayn's dalil
Understand their qiyas to the whole mahr case and their argument that hatt attaches to the contract.
They analogize part to whole and treat the gift of unpossessed as a reduction attaching to the contract.
4
4. Examine Abu Hanifa's dalil and response
Understand his argument that the husband's objective (half without compensation) is achieved before divorce, and that hatt does not attach in marriage, proven by the 15 dirham example and the non-attachment of increase.
5
5. Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical consequence: according to Abu Hanifa, husband gets nothing; according to Sahibayn, husband gets half of what the wife possessed.
This difference affects financial outcomes in divorce settlements.

الزيادة فيه لا تلتحق حتى لا تنصف
كتاب النكاح
ترجمہ اور اگر عورت نے قبضہ کیا پانچ سودرہم پر پھر ہبہ کر دیا کل کے کل کو مقبوض اور غیر مقبوض یا ہبہ کر دیا باقی کو۔ پھر طلاق دی اس کے ساتھ دخول سے پہلے تو ان دونوں میں سے کوئی کسی پر رجوع نہ کرے ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ عورت سے رجوع کرے نصف مقبوض کو بعض کو کل پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور اسلئے کہ بعض کا ہبہ کم کرنا ہے۔ پس خط یعنی کم کرنا لاحق ہو گا اصل عقد کے ساتھ ۔ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر کا مقصود حاصل ہو گیا اور وہ نصف مہر کا سلامت رہنا ہے بلاعوض ۔ پس طلاق کے وقت رجوع کا مستحق نہیں ہوگا۔ اور حط ( کم کرنا ) اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں ہوتا ہے، نکاح میں۔ کیا تو نے غور نہیں کیا کہ نکاح میں زیادتی ( اصل عقد کے ساتھ ) لاحق نہیں ہوتی ہے چنانچہ زیادتی کی تنصیف نہیں ہوگی۔ تشریح اب صورت یہ ہے کہ عورت نے پانچ سو درہم پر قبضہ کیا اور پھر شوہر کیلئے ایک ہزار مقبوض اور غیر مقبوض دونوں کو ہبہ کر دیا یا صرف غیر مقبوض کو ہبہ کر دیا اور طلاق قبل الدخول واقع ہو گئی تو زوجین میں سے کسی کو کسی پر رجوع کا حق نہیں ہوگا امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین کا مسلک یہ ہے کہ شوہر نصف مقبوض یعنی دو سو پچاس درہم رجوع کرلے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ بعض کو کل پر قیاس کرتے ہیں چنانچہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر عورت کل پر قبضہ کرتی اور شوہر کیلئے ہبہ کر دیتی پھر شوہر اس کو طلاق قبل الدخول دے دیتا تو ہمارے نزدیک شوہر عورت سے نصف مقبوض رجوع کرتا پس ایسے ہی جب عورت نے بعض پر قبضہ کیا تو اس بعض کے نصف پر رجوع کا حق ہوگا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بعض کا ہبہ یعنی نصف غیر مقبوض کا ہبہ عورت کی طرف سے خط ہے یعنی کم کر دینا اور حط لاحق ہوتا ہے اصل عقد کے ساتھ تو گویا شوہر نے ابتداء ہی پانچ سومقبوض پر نکاح کیا ہے۔ پس یہ پانچ سو درہم کل مہر ہوں گے۔ اور کل مہر کے بارے میں حکم گذر چکا کہ اگر کل مہر پر قبضہ کر کے عورت پورے مہر کو ہبہ کردے تو نصف کے رجوع کا حق رہتا ہے۔ لہذا ایسے ہی یہاں بھی نصف مقبوض کے رجوع کا حق حاصل ہوگا۔
امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر کا مقصود ہے بلاعوض نصف مہر کا سلامت رہنا۔ اور یہ مقصود طلاق سے پہلے ہی حاصل ہو چکا۔ ہوم ہے کا رہنا۔ یہ پہلےہی ہو اور لہذا طلاق کے بعد رجوع کا مستحق نہیں ہوگا۔ صاحبین کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حط نکاح میں اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں ہوتا ہے وجہ یہ ہے کہ مثلاً ایک آدمی نے کسی عورت سے ہیں درہم پر نکاح کیا عورت نے پندرہ در ہم شوہر کو ہبہ کر دئیے۔ تو اب شوہر پر دس درہم واجب نہیں ہوں گے۔ بلکہ پانچ درہم واجب ہوں گے ۔ اگر حط اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق ہوتا تو ایسا ہو جا تا گویا کہ شوہر نے پانچ درہم پر نکاح کیا ہے۔ اور پانچ درہم پر اگر نکاح کیا جائے تو دس درہم واجب ہوتے ہیں۔ لہذا اس صورت میں دس درہم واجب ہونے چاہئیں تھے۔ حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ شوہر پر پانچ ہی واجب ہیں۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ حط اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے خط کے اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق نہ ہونے کی ایک وجہ یہ بیان کی ہے کہ نکاح میں زیادتی بالاتفاق اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں ہوتی ۔ مثلاً شوہر نے مہر سمی پر پچاس درہم زیادہ کر دیے اور پھر طلاق قبل الدخول دے دی تو ان پچاس کی تنصیف نہیں ہوگی لہذا جس طرح زیادتی اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں ہوتی۔ اسی طرح حط بھی اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق نہ ہونا چاہئے۔
The increase therein does not attach so that it is not divided into halves. Chapter of Nikah. Translation: And if the woman took possession of five hundred dirhams, then she gifted all of it, both possessed and unpossessed, or she gifted the remainder, then he divorced her before consummation, then neither of them can reclaim from the other according to Abu Hanifa. And the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said that the husband should reclaim half of the possessed from the woman, analogizing the part to the whole, and because gifting a part is a reduction. So reduction (hatt) attaches to the original contract. And Abu Hanifa's proof is that the husband's objective has been achieved, and that is the preservation of half the dower without compensation. So at the time of divorce he is not entitled to reclaim. And reduction does not attach to the original contract in marriage. Have you not considered that increase does not attach to the original contract in marriage? Consequently, the increase is not divided into halves. Explanation: Now the case is that the woman took possession of five hundred dirhams and then gifted to the husband one thousand dirhams, both possessed and unpossessed, or she gifted only the unpossessed, and divorce before consummation occurred. Then neither spouse has the right to reclaim from the other according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And the doctrine of the two companions is that the husband reclaims half of the possessed, i.e., two hundred fifty dirhams. The proof of the two companions is that they analogize the part to the whole. Thus they say: if the woman took possession of the whole and gifted it to the husband, then the husband divorced her before consummation, in our view the husband reclaims half of the possessed from the woman. So similarly, when the woman took possession of a part, he will have the right to reclaim half of that part. The second proof is that gifting a part, i.e., gifting half of the unpossessed, is a reduction from the woman's side, and reduction attaches to the original contract. So as if the husband initially married on five hundred possessed dirhams. So these five hundred dirhams become the entire dower. And the ruling regarding the entire dower has passed: if the woman took possession of the entire dower and gifted the whole dower, then the husband has the right to reclaim half. Therefore, here too the right to reclaim half of the possessed will be obtained. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the husband's objective is the preservation of half the dower without compensation, and this objective was achieved before divorce. [...] And the answer to the proof of the two companions is that reduction does not attach to the original contract in marriage. The reason is that, for example, a man married a woman for fifteen dirhams, the woman gifted fifteen dirhams to the husband. Then ten dirhams would not be obligatory upon the husband, rather five dirhams would be obligatory. If reduction attached to the original contract, it would be as if the husband married for five dirhams, and if marriage is done for five dirhams, ten dirhams become obligatory. Therefore, in this case ten dirhams should have been obligatory, but that is not the case; rather, only five are obligatory upon the husband. So it is known that reduction does not attach to the original contract. The author of Al-Hidayah stated one reason why reduction does not attach: that increase, by consensus, does not attach to the original contract in marriage. For example, the husband added fifty dirhams to the named dower and then divorced before consummation, then those fifty are not divided into halves. So just as increase does not attach to the original contract, similarly reduction should not attach.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the husband's right to reclaim part of the mahr when the wife, having possessed only part of the mahr, gifts it to the husband and then divorce occurs before consummation. According to Abu Hanifa, the husband cannot reclaim anything because his right to half the mahr without compensation was already secured when the wife gifted the possessed portion. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), by analogy to the case where the wife possessed the entire mahr and gifted it, the husband should be able to reclaim half of the possessed portion (here, half of the 500 dirhams she possessed, i.e., 250 dirhams). They also argue that the wife's gift of the unpossessed portion is a reduction (hatt) that attaches to the original contract, making the possessed portion the entire mahr, and then the husband reclaims half of it. Abu Hanifa refutes this by showing that in marriage, neither increase nor reduction attaches to the original contract; otherwise, absurd consequences would follow. The commentary then illustrates this with an example of a marriage for 15 dirhams where the wife gifts the entire mahr back, showing that the husband is only obliged to pay 5 dirhams, not 10. The passage also notes that increase does not attach to the original contract, as extra conditions are not divided upon divorce.

Key Terms
حط (hatt): Reduction of the dower; here, the wife's act of gifting part of the mahr is considered a reduction in the husband's obligation.
تنصيف (tansif): Division into halves; here specifically, the splitting of the mahr into two halves upon divorce before consummation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what happens when a wife who possessed part of the mahr gifts it to the husband and then is divorced before consummation?
A) The husband can reclaim half of the possessed portion.
B) The husband can reclaim the entire possessed portion.
C) The husband cannot reclaim anything.
D) The wife must return the entire mahr.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a wife's gift of possessed mahr to her husband before talaq before consummation prevents the husband from reclaiming half, because reduction does not attach to the marriage contract and the husband's objective is already fulfilled.

The Husband's Right to Complete Half When the Wife Gifts Less Than Half
Intra-Hanafi dispute on husband's reclaim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the husband's reclaim when the wife gifts less than half the mahr, and apply the correct calculation.

Core Idea
When the wife gifts less than half, Abu Hanifa preserves half of the original mahr; Sahibayn take half of what she possessed.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute that arises when the wife, after receiving most of the mahr, gifts a small portion to the husband and then divorce occurs before consummation. The issue is: how much can the husband reclaim from the wife? Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ based on their view of whether the gift (hibah) attaches to the original contract as a reduction. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the principle of half-mahr in diverse scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The wife possesses most of the mahr (e.g., 800 out of 1000) and gifts a small portion (200) to the husband, then divorce before consummation occurs. Determine the relevant amounts.
The gift is less than half the full mahr.
2
State the positions
Abu Hanifa: husband reclaims enough to reach half of the full mahr (500 total). Sahibayn: husband reclaims half of what the wife possessed (half of 800 = 400).
Use the example: mahr 1000, gift 200, possess 800.
3
Understand the proofs
Sahibayn argue the gift is a reduction that attaches to the contract, making the possessed amount the effective dower. Abu Hanifa insists the original contract governs and half of the original mahr is fixed.
This is a rational (dalil aqli) dispute based on the nature of the gift.
4
Calculate the practical difference
With mahr 1000: Abu Hanifa reclaim = 300 (500-200). Sahibayn reclaim = 400. Note the difference of 100.
Apply the same logic to any numbers: half of full mahr minus gift vs. half of possessed.

Source Text

و لو كانت وهبت اقل من النصف وقبضت الباقى فعنده يرجع عليها الى تمام النصف وعندهما بنصف المقبوض
ترجمہ اور اگر عورت نے نصف سے کم ہبہ کیا اور باقی پر قبضہ کیا تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک شوہر رجوع کرے گا عورت پر تمام نصف تک اور صاحبین کے نزدیک نصف مقبوض ( رجوع کرے گا)۔ تشریح صورت یہ ہے کہ نکاح ہوا مثلاً ایک ہزار پر عورت نے دو سو روپے شوہر کو ہبہ کر دیئے اور باقی آٹھ سورو پہیہ پر قبضہ کیا۔ اس بارے میں امام صاحب کا مذہب ہے کہ اتنا اور واپس لے لے کہ نصف مہر ہو جائے یعنی تین سوروپے شوہر عورت سے اور واپس کر لے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک نصف مقبوض یعنی چار سو روپے رجوع کرے گا۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو نصف سے کم ہبہ کر دیا اور بہہ حط ہے۔ پس یہ حط اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق ہو گا تو گویا مقدار مقبوض ہی مہر ہے۔ پس جب طلاق قبل الدخول دی تو عورت سے مقدار مقبوض کے نصف کا رجوع کر سکتا ہے۔

And if she gifted less than half and possessed the remainder, then according to him (Abu Hanifa) the husband reclaims from her until the completion of half, and according to them (the Sahibayn) he reclaims half of the possessed. Translation: And if the woman gifted less than half and possessed the remainder, then according to Imam Sahib (Abu Hanifa) the husband will reclaim from the woman to complete the half, and according to the Sahibayn he will reclaim half of the possessed. Explanation: The case is that the marriage was, for example, for one thousand. The woman gifted two hundred rupees to the husband and possessed the remaining eight hundred. In this regard, Imam Sahib's doctrine is that he should take back enough to make half the dower, i.e., the husband recovers three hundred rupees from the woman. And according to the Sahibayn, he will reclaim half of the possessed, i.e., four hundred rupees. The proof of the Sahibayn is that what he gifted less than half is a reduction. So this reduction attaches to the original contract, so as if the possessed amount is the dower. So when he divorced before consummation, he can reclaim half of the possessed amount. And Imam Sahib's proof is that in the case of divorce before consummation, half the dower should be preserved for the husband, whatever happens. So he recovers three hundred rupees from the woman so that the husband obtains half the dower.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage presents a second intra-Hanafi dispute. When the wife possesses most of the mahr (e.g., 800 out of 1000) and gifts a small part (200) to the husband, then divorce before consummation occurs, the husband may reclaim some amount. According to Abu Hanifa, the husband should reclaim enough to make his total half of the full dower (500), so he reclaims 300 (since he already has 200 from the gift). According to the Sahibayn, he reclaims half of the possessed amount (half of 800 = 400). The Sahibayn again argue that the gift (200) is a reduction that attaches to the contract, making the possessed amount the effective dower, so half of that is reclaimable. Abu Hanifa argues that the principle is that the husband must have half of the originally agreed mahr preserved, so he takes whatever is needed to complete that half.

Key Terms
تمام النصف (tamam al-nisf): The completion of half; means the husband reclaims until he has exactly half the full dower.
حط (hatt): Reduction; the Sahibayn's argument that the gift operates as a reduction of the dower, attaching to the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 200
B) 300
C) 400
D) 500

Key Takeaway
The husband's right to half the original mahr is preserved even when the wife gifts a portion, according to the relied-upon view of Abu Hanifa.

Mahr as Specific Commodity: Gift and Divorce
Ruling on husband's ruju' following wife's gift of specific mahr before talaq before consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling of istihsan when a wife gifts a specific commodity mahr to her husband and he divorces before consummation, distinguishing it from the qiyas position of Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
When a wife gifts a specific mahr to her husband, his right to half is fulfilled by the gift itself—istihsan allows him to keep it.

This passage addresses a subtle scenario in Hanafi marriage law: the wife receives a specific commodity as mahr, gifts it to her husband, and then the husband divorces her before consummation. Does the husband owe half its value? The text presents a clash between strict qiyas, which would require repayment of half the value, and istihsan (juristic preference), which rules that the husband owes nothing. Understanding this ruling requires grasping why the gift changes the nature of the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is: wife gifts a specific commodity mahr to her husband, then husband divorces before consummation. The ruling by istihsan is that the husband reclaims nothing.
This is the relied-upon Hanafi position.
2
Recognize the Qiyas Position
According to qiyas (Imam Zufar), the husband would reclaim half the value of the commodity. This is because in divorce before consummation, half the specific dower must be returned.
Qiyas treats the gift as irrelevant; the obligation to return half still stands.
3
Understand the Istihsan Reasoning
Istihsan argues that the husband's right at divorce is to have half the possessed mahr safe from the wife's side. Since the wife gifted it, that half has already reached him. Therefore, she cannot be required to give anything else.
The key: the husband's right is fulfilled by the very gift.
4
Compare with Other Cases
The text distinguishes two cases: (1) when mahr is a debt (fungible) – then the husband would reclaim half; (2) when the wife sells the mahr to the husband – then it reaches him for a price, so no ruju'. Compare to the gift case where no consideration is given.
These distinctions clarify why the gift is unique.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The Hanafi school follows istihsan: the husband keeps the entire gift and owes nothing. Zufar's qiyas is not adopted for fatwa.
This is a clear example of istihsan overriding qiyas within the Hanafi madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ .... اور اگر نکاح کیا عورت سے کسی متعین سامان پر پھر عورت نے قبضہ کیا یا قبضہ نہیں کیا پھر شوہر کو ہبہ کر دیا پھر اس کو طلاق قبل الدخول دی تو شوہر عورت پر کچھ جوع نہیں کرے گا۔ اور قیاس میں اور یہی قول ہے امام زفر کا کہ عورت پر سامان کی نصف قیمت رجوع کرے اسلئے کہ طلاق قبل الدخول میں عین مہر کے نصف کو واپس کرنا واجب ہے۔ اس کی تقریر گذر چکی ۔ اور وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ شوہر کا حق طلاق کے وقت عورت کی جانب سے نصف مقبوض کا سلامت رہنا ہے اور نصف مقبوض شوہر کی طرف پہنچ چکا اور اسی وجہ سے عورت کیلئے جائز نہیں دوسری چیز کا اس سامان کی جگہ دینا بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ مہر دین ہو اور بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ عورت نے اپنے شوہر کے ہاتھ فروخت کیا اسلئے کہ شوہر کی طرف پہنچا بدل کے ساتھ۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نکاح کے وقت ایسی چیز کو مہر بنانا جو متعین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتی ہے۔ مثلاً سامان وغیر ہ عورت نے اس مہر پر قبضہ کیا یا قبضہ نہیں کیا حکم میں دونوں برابر ہیں۔ پھر عورت نے شوہر کو ہبہ کر دیا شوہر نے دخول سے پہلے طلاق دے دی۔ اس
And if he married her on a specific commodity, and she took possession or did not take possession, then she gifted it to him, then he divorced her before consummation, then he does not reclaim anything from her. And according to qiyas, which is the saying of Zufar, he would reclaim half its value from her, because the obligatory thing is to return half of the specific dower, as its explanation has passed. The reason for istihsan is that his right at the time of divorce is the safety of half of the possessed from her side, and it has reached him. Therefore, she is not allowed to give something else in its place, unlike the case where the dower is a debt, and unlike the case where she sold it to her husband, because it reached him for a consideration.
Explanation: The case is that at the time of marriage, a thing that becomes specified by specification, such as goods etc., was made the mahr. The woman took possession of this mahr or did not take possession — both are equal in the ruling. Then the woman gifted it to the husband, the husband divorced before consummation.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage deals with the case where the mahr is a specific commodity (e.g., a car, a house, or goods). If the wife, having possessed it or not, gifts it to the husband, and then the husband divorces her before consummation, the husband cannot reclaim any part of the mahr. This is the ruling by istihsan (juristic preference). The qiyas, supported by Imam Zufar, would say the husband must reclaim half the value of the commodity because in divorce before consummation, half the specific dower must be returned. However, istihsan prevails because the husband's right is to have half the possessed mahr safe, and it has already reached him via the gift. Since he has that half, he cannot be forced to return something else. This differs from the case where the mahr is a debt (money, which is fungible) and from the case where the wife sells the mahr to the husband, because in sale, he pays a price. The commentary notes that it doesn't matter whether the wife took possession of the specific mahr before gifting or not; the ruling is the same.

Key Terms
عرض ('ard): A specific commodity or goods that are not currency; when specified, it becomes a specific 'ayn (corporeal property).
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; preferred ruling over strict qiyas due to a stronger evidence or principle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The husband must return half the value to the wife.
B) The husband can keep the entire commodity and owes nothing.
C) The husband must return exactly half of the commodity itself.
D) The wife can demand half the value in its place.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, istihsan can override qiyas to achieve a just outcome, as seen when a wife's gift of specific mahr before divorce fulfills the husband's right to half, negating any further claim.

No Reclamation When Wife Gifts Specific Mahr Item Before Divorce
Ruling with proof using istihsan over qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a wife gifts the specific mahr item before divorce, explain the istihsan reasoning, and distinguish it from the qiyas position of Zufar and from cases where the mahr is a debt or sold.

Core Idea
If the mahr is a specific item and the wife gifts it to the husband before divorce, the husband reclaims nothing – his right to half is already fulfilled.

This passage presents a key Hanafi ruling on mahr when a specific commodity is gifted. It illustrates the school's use of istihsan to override strict qiyas, and clarifies the boundaries of the husband's right to reclaim half the mahr before consummation. We will analyze the reasoning, the contrasting view of Imam Zufar, and the exceptions when the mahr is a debt or sold by the wife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the Hanafi ruling
The case: a man marries a woman and the mahr is a specific commodity ('ard). The woman takes possession of the mahr (or not, equally valid), then gifts the entire mahr item to the husband. Then the husband divorces her before consummation. The Hanafi ruling (istihsan) is that the husband reclaims nothing from the wife.
The ruling applies whether or not the wife physically possessed the mahr before the gift.
2
Contrast with qiyas (Zufar's view)
Imam Zufar, relying on qiyas, holds that the husband should reclaim half the value of the mahr item. His reasoning: at divorce before consummation, the obligation is to return half of the specific mahr; the gift does not extinguish that obligation.
Zufar's view is a minority position within the Hanafi school; the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) follow istihsan.
3
Understand the istihsan reasoning
The istihsan argument: the husband's right at divorce is the safety of half of the possessed mahr from the wife's side. Since the wife gifted the entire possessed mahr to the husband (without compensation), that half has already reached him safely. His objective is achieved, so no reclamation is needed.
The key concept: 'safety of half of the possessed' (salamat nisf al-maqbud) not 'return of half the original mahr'.
4
Distinguish from exceptions
The ruling changes in two situations: (a) if the mahr is a debt (dīn, e.g., money), the husband reclaims half the mahr value, because money is not a specific commodity and the right is not tied to a possessed half; (b) if the wife sells the mahr item to the husband (sale with compensation), the husband reclaims half the value, because the transfer was with a substitute, so the safety condition is not met.
These exceptions highlight that the istihsan ruling is specific to gifts without compensation.
5
Apply the law to a new scenario
Now test yourself: if the mahr is a specific diamond ring, the wife gives it to the husband as a gift, then he divorces before consummation, what is the ruling? State the ruling and the reasoning.
Check your answer against the mufta bihi position.

فروخت کیا اسلئے کہ شوہر کی طرف پہنچا بدل کے ساتھ۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نکاح کے وقت ایسی چیز کو مہر بنانا جو متعین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتی ہے۔ مثلاً سامان وغیر ہ عورت نے اس مہر پر قبضہ کیا یا قبضہ نہیں کیا حکم میں دونوں برابر ہیں۔ پھر عورت نے شوہر کو ہبہ کر دیا شوہر نے دخول سے پہلے طلاق دے دی۔ اس صورت میں حکم یہ ہے کہ شوہر عورت سے اور کچھ رجوع نہ کرے یہ حکم استحسانا ہے اور یہی مذہب ہے ائمہ ثلثہ کا۔ اور امام زفر کا قول یہ ہے کہ اس کی نصف قیمت رجوع کر لے یہی قیاس ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ طلاق قبل الدخول کی صورت میں عین مہر کے نصف کولوٹا نا واجب ہے اور یہاں یہ پایا نہیں گیا۔ کیونکہ شوہر کیلئے مہر کی سلامتی عورت کے بری کر دینے سے ہوتی ہے اور شوہر نصف مہر کا مستحق تھا طلاق قبل الدخول کی وجہ سے لہذا عورت اس سے بری نہیں ہو گی۔ جس کا شوہر مستحق ہوا ہے۔ یعنی طلاق قبل الدخول کی وجہ سے نصف مین مہر ۔ پس جب عورت بری نہیں ہوئی تو شوہر کو اس نصف مہر کے رجوع کا حق حاصل رہے گا۔ وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ طلاق قبل الدخول کے وقت شوہر کا حق یہ ہے کہ عورت کی جانب سے بلا عوض نصف مقبوض سلامت رہے اور شوہر کی طرف عورت کی جانب سے بلا عوض مین مبر ہی پہنچ گیا۔ لہذا مقصود زوج حاصل ہو گیا اور جب مقصود حاصل ہو گیا تو اب کچھ رجوع کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں اور چونکہ زوج کا حق طلاق کے وقت نصف مقبوض کی سلامتی ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے عورت کیلئے جائز نہیں کہ وہ بذاتہ عرض مقبوض کی موجودگی میں اس کی جگہ کوئی دوسری چیز شوہر کو دے۔ کیونکہ عرض مقبوض دونوں میں متعین ہے اور بر خلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ مہر مالا یتعین کے قبیلہ سے ہو۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں شوہر کو نصف مہر رجوع کرنے کا حق ہے۔ اس لئے کہ شوہر کا حق نصف مقبوض میں نہیں تھا۔ اس کے متعین نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اسی وجہ سے اگر عورت نے نصف مہر کی جگہ دوسری چیز دے دی تو جائز ہے اور اس کے برخلاف کہ عورت نے شوہر کے ہاتھ سامان مہر کو فروخت کر دیا تو اس صورت میں بھی شوہر کو نصف مہر سے رجوع کرنے کا حق ہوگا کیونکہ شوہر کی طرف نصف مقبوض بعوض پہنچا ہے۔ اسلئے کہ شوہر نے عورت سے خریدا ہے اور سلامت بعوض ایسا ہے جیسا کہ سلامت ہی نہیں۔ پس یہ نصف مقبوض بعوض اسکے قائم مقام نہیں ہے تو پھر شوہر کو نصف مہر کے رجوع کا حق حاصل ہوگا۔ یا اس کو مختصر ایوں کہہ لیجئے کہ شوہر کا حق تھا نصف مہر بلا بدل میں اور اس کو پہنچا ہے ببدل تو گویا شوہر کے پاس اس کا حق پہنچا ہی نہیں اسلئے اس کو رجوع کا حق ہوگا۔واللہ اعلم بالصواب
And if he married her on (the basis of) a commodity ('ard), and she took possession or did not take possession, then she gifted it to him, then he divorced her before consummation, he does not reclaim anything from her. And in qiyas, which is the statement of Zufar, he reclaims half of its value, because what is obligatory is the return of half of the specific mahr, as its explanation has passed. The reason for istihsan is that his right at the time of divorce is the safety of half of the possessed from her side, and it has reached him. Hence she is not allowed to give something else in its place, unlike when the mahr is a debt, and unlike when she sold to her husband, because it reached him with a substitute. Translation: ... Explanation: ... (full translation omitted for brevity but follows the text closely).
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof regarding the case where the mahr is a specific item (like a commodity) and the wife gifts it to the husband before divorce. The Hanafi position (istihsan) is that the husband reclaims nothing, because his right at divorce is to have half of the possessed amount safe from the wife, and since the entire item (the possessed mahr) has been gifted to him, that half is already in his possession. Imam Zufar, relying on qiyas, argues that the husband should reclaim half the value of the item, because the original obligation at divorce is to return half of the specific mahr, and since the gift was a transfer, the obligation to return half remains. The Hanafi response uses istihsan, preferring the principle that the husband's right is fulfilled by the safe arrival of half the possessed mahr, and since the gift is without compensation, it satisfies the requirement. The passage also distinguishes cases where the mahr is a debt (money) or where the wife sells the mahr to the husband, in which cases the husband does have a right to reclaim, because in those cases the mahr is not a specific item or the transfer is with compensation. The practical result: for specific items, husband gets nothing; for debts or sales, he reclaims half.

Key Terms
عرض (ard): A commodity, a specific item of property that is not money. In this context, it is any tangible non-fungible item used as mahr.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that sets aside strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable ruling based on broader principles.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; drawing a ruling for a new case from an existing case due to shared underlying cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where mahr is a specific commodity and the wife gifts it to the husband before divorce, what is the Hanafi ruling (mufta bihi)?
A) Husband reclaims half the value of the commodity
B) Husband reclaims nothing
C) Husband reclaims the entire commodity
D) Husband reclaims half of the commodity itself

Key Takeaway
When a wife gifts a specific mahr item to her husband before divorce, the husband's right to half is fulfilled by the gift itself, so he reclaims nothing.

Mahr in Dhimmah: Validity and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on mahr in dhimmah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on mahr in dhimmah and explain the key difference with the Shafi'i view regarding jahl in mahr.

Core Idea
A mahr specified as an unindividualized animal or goods in dhimmah is valid in Hanafi law due to tolerance of jahl in marriage.

In this passage, Al-Hidayah extends the previous ruling on mahr to cases where the mahr is an undefined item in the husband's liability (dhimmah). The core issue is whether such uncertainty (jahl) invalidates the contract. The Hanafi school maintains validity, while the Shafi'i school insists on mahr al-mithl, and the Maliki and Hanbali schools go further to invalidate the marriage. We will examine the reasoning and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school considers the marriage valid and the mahr determined by an average specimen of the described type. The husband does not reclaim if the wife gifts the mahr before divorce.
The ruling is consistent with the previous case of specific mahr.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Name the opposing schools: Shafi'i holds the specification invalid so mahr al-mithl is due; Maliki and Hanbali (in one narration) hold the marriage invalid due to jahl.
The text mentions Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik (one narration), and Imam Ahmad (one narration).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Explain that the Shafi'i school analogizes jahl in mahr to jahl in sales, which invalidates the contract. The Maliki/Hanbali view treats jahl as a defect in the contract itself.
The opponent's dalil is qiyas on sales, where jahl about the subject matter invalidates.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that jahl is tolerated in marriage because the contract is based on affection; uncertainty can be remedied by determining an average quality once the type is specified.
This is a rational (dalil aqli) argument based on the nature of marriage.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi – marriage valid, mahr is average specimen; Shafi'i – marriage valid but mahr al-mithl (proper mahr); Maliki/Hanbali – marriage invalid.
The ruling on reclaim when the wife gifts the mahr remains the same for Hanafi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if he married her on (the basis of) an animal or commodities in the dhimmah, then the answer is like that, because the possessed is determined in the return; and this is because ignorance is tolerated in marriage, so when it is specified, it is as if the specification (tasmia) occurred upon it. Translation: And if he married her on an animal or commodities in the dhimmah, then the same ruling applies, because the possessed is determined in the return; and this is because ignorance is tolerated in marriage, so when it becomes specified, it is as if the specification occurred upon it. Explanation: The scenario is that he married and made the mahr an animal, e.g., a horse or donkey, or commodities that are owed in the husband's dhimmah, e.g., he said the mahr is a cloth of such and such type. Then the wife took possession or did not take possession, but she gifted (hiba) to the husband, then the husband divorced before consummation, so the husband has no right to reclaim from the wife. Imam Shafi'i says that this specification is not valid; therefore, mahr al-mithl is due. And a narration from Imam Malik and a narration from Imam Ahmad say that the marriage is invalid due to ignorance of the specified thing. But according to us, the marriage contract is valid, and an average animal and average cloth are due. In the original issue, we said that the husband has no right to reclaim from the wife. The evidence is that the possessed is determined in the matter of return; i.e., if the wife took possession, then upon it exactly... (text cuts off).
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage extends the previous ruling to cases where the mahr is an animal or commodity that is in the husband's dhimmah (i.e., a debt to be delivered). The ruling is the same: if the wife gifts the mahr to the husband before divorce, he does not reclaim anything. The reasoning is that once the specific item is delivered and possessed, it becomes determined for the purpose of return. The passage also addresses an inter-madhhab dispute: Imam Shafi'i holds that such a specification (of an unspecified animal or commodity in the dhimmah) is invalid due to uncertainty (jahl), so mahr al-mithl (proper mahr) is due. Imam Malik (in one narration) and Imam Ahmad (in one narration) hold that the marriage is invalid altogether because of the uncertainty. The Hanafi position is that the marriage is valid, and the mahr is determined by an average quality of the specified type. The key principle is that ignorance (jahl) is tolerated in marriage contracts to a degree not tolerated in sales, so the specification is effective. The practical consequence for the ruling on reclamation is the same: no reclamation when the wife gifts the possessed mahr.

Key Terms
ذمة (dhimmah): Liability or obligation; in this context, the animal or goods are owed by the husband in his dhimmah, meaning they are a debt to be delivered.
جہالت (jahl): Ignorance or uncertainty about the specific identity of the mahr item. In sales, jahl invalidates, but in marriage it is tolerated.
تسمية (tasmia): Specification or naming of the mahr. When a type is specified, it becomes the effective mahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a man marries a woman on the basis of an unspecified horse in his dhimmah (i.e., he says 'the mahr is a horse'), and the wife then gifts the horse to him before divorce?
A) The marriage is invalid
B) The husband must pay mahr al-mithl
C) The husband does not reclaim anything
D) The husband reclaims half the value of the horse

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits specification of mahr by type in dhimmah, and the ruling on no reclaim remains consistent when the wife gifts the mahr before divorce.

Husband's Right to Reclaim Half Mahr After Wife's Gift (Hibah) Before Consummation
Explaining istihsan vs qiyas on husband reclaiming half mahr after wife gifts it back

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school (three Imams) holds that the husband does not reclaim half the mahr when the wife gifts it back before consummation divorce, and distinguish this from Imam Zufar's position based on qiyas.

Core Idea
When the wife gifts back the mahr, the husband's right to half is satisfied without reclaiming—istihsan overrides qiyas.

In a pre-consummation divorce, the husband is normally entitled to reclaim half the mahr (Quran 2:237). But what happens if the wife voluntarily gifts the entire mahr back to the husband before the divorce? Does the husband still reclaim half? The Hanafi school has an internal difference, with the majority ruling by istihsan that the husband keeps the full mahr, while Imam Zufar argues by qiyas that he must still reclaim half. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind both positions and the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad: the husband does not reclaim half the mahr. This is the madhhab and mufta bihi.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Zufar holds that the husband reclaims half the mahr (by qiyas). Understand his reasoning.
Zufar is a Hanafi mujtahid; his view is a minority within the school.
3
Follow the opponent's proof (qiyas)
Zufar analogizes to the standard pre-consummation divorce rule: half the mahr is due. The wife's gift does not cancel this obligation; the husband should physically take back half.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response (istihsan)
The majority argues that the husband's right at divorce is to have half the mahr safe without compensation. The wife's gift achieves this directly, so no reclaim is needed. Istihsan is applied because qiyas would lead to an unjust result.
The gift is without exchange, so the husband's objective is perfectly met.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the majority, the husband keeps the full mahr; under Zufar, he must return half. The practical difference is clear. The mufta bihi is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صورت میں حکم یہ ہے کہ شوہر عورت سے اور کچھ رجوع نہ کرے یہ حکم استحسانا ہے اور یہی مذہب ہے ائمہ ثلثہ کا۔ اور امام زفر کا قول یہ ہے کہ اس کی نصف قیمت رجوع کر لے یہی قیاس ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ طلاق قبل الدخول کی صورت میں عین مہر کے نصف کولوٹا نا واجب ہے اور یہاں یہ پایا نہیں گیا۔ کیونکہ شوہر کیلئے مہر کی سلامتی عورت کے بری کر دینے سے ہوتی ہے اور شوہر نصف مہر کا مستحق تھا طلاق قبل الدخول کی وجہ سے لہذا عورت اس سے بری نہیں ہو گی۔ جس کا شوہر مستحق ہوا ہے۔ یعنی طلاق قبل الدخول کی وجہ سے نصف مین مہر ۔ پس جب عورت بری نہیں ہوئی تو شوہر کو اس نصف مہر کے رجوع کا حق حاصل رہے گا۔ وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ طلاق قبل الدخول کے وقت شوہر کا حق یہ ہے کہ عورت کی جانب سے بلا عوض نصف مقبوض سلامت رہے اور شوہر کی طرف عورت کی جانب سے بلا عوض مین مبر ہی پہنچ گیا۔ لہذا مقصود زوج حاصل ہو گیا اور جب مقصود حاصل ہو گیا تو اب کچھ رجوع کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں اور چونکہ زوج کا حق طلاق کے وقت نصف مقبوض کی سلامتی ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے عورت کیلئے جائز نہیں کہ وہ بذاتہ عرض مقبوض کی موجودگی میں اس کی جگہ کوئی دوسری چیز شوہر کو دے۔ کیونکہ عرض مقبوض دونوں میں متعین ہے اور بر خلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ مہر مالا یتعین کے قبیلہ سے ہو۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں شوہر کو نصف مہر رجوع کرنے کا حق ہے۔ اس لئے کہ شوہر کا حق نصف مقبوض میں نہیں تھا۔ اس کے متعین نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اسی وجہ سے اگر عورت نے نصف مہر کی جگہ دوسری چیز دے دی تو جائز ہے اور اس کے برخلاف کہ عورت نے شوہر کے ہاتھ سامان مہر کو فروخت کر دیا تو اس صورت میں بھی شوہر کو نصف مہر سے رجوع کرنے کا حق ہوگا کیونکہ شوہر کی طرف نصف مقبوض بعوض پہنچا ہے۔ اسلئے کہ شوہر نے عورت سے خریدا ہے اور سلامت بعوض ایسا ہے جیسا کہ سلامت ہی نہیں۔ پس یہ نصف مقبوض بعوض اسکے قائم مقام نہیں ہے تو پھر شوہر کو نصف مہر کے رجوع کا حق حاصل ہوگا۔ یا اس کو مختصر ایوں کہہ لیجئے کہ شوہر کا حق تھا نصف مہر بلا بدل میں اور اس کو پہنچا ہے ببدل تو گویا شوہر کے پاس اس کا حق پہنچا ہی نہیں اسلئے اس کو رجوع کا حق ہوگا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
The ruling in this situation is that the husband does not take back anything from the woman. This ruling is based on istihsan, and this is the madhhab of the three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). Imam Zufar's opinion is that he takes back half of its value; this is qiyas. Imam Zufar's proof is that in the case of divorce before consummation, returning half of the specific mahr is obligatory, and here it is not found. Because the husband's safety of the mahr is achieved by the woman freeing him, and the husband was entitled to half the mahr due to divorce before consummation. Therefore, the woman does not free the husband from what he became entitled to, i.e., half the mahr due to divorce before consummation. So when the woman did not free him, the husband retains the right to take back that half mahr. The reason for istihsan is that at the time of divorce before consummation, the husband's right is that half of the possessed (mahr) remains safe from the woman's side without compensation, and the husband's half of the mahr has reached him from the woman without compensation. Thus, the husband's objective is achieved, and when the objective is achieved, there is no need to take back anything. Moreover, since the husband's right at the time of divorce is the safety of half of the possessed, for this reason it is not permissible for the woman to give the husband something else in its place in the presence of the specific possessed good, because the possessed good is specific to both. And contrary to the case where the mahr is from the category of non-specific property, because in that case the husband has the right to take back half the mahr, since the husband's right was not in half of the possessed due to its non-specificity. For this reason, if the woman gave something else instead of half the mahr, it is permissible. And contrary to the case where the woman sold the mahr goods to the husband, in that case also the husband has the right to take back half the mahr, because half of the possessed reached the husband with compensation. Since the husband bought from the woman, and safety with compensation is like no safety. So this half of the possessed with compensation does not stand in place of his right; then the husband retains the right to take back half the mahr. Or you may say briefly: the husband's right was half the mahr without exchange, and it reached him with exchange, so it is as if his right did not reach him; therefore, he has the right to take back. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between the majority of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Imam Muhammad – the 'three Imams') and Imam Zufar on the ruling when a wife, after receiving the mahr (dower), gifts it back to the husband, and then the husband divorces her before consummation. The core question: does the husband have the right to reclaim half the mahr (as normally required by Quran 2:237 in pre-consummation divorce)? The majority say no, based on istihsan (juristic preference), while Imam Zufar says yes, based on qiyas (analogy). Imam Zufar's qiyas: In pre-consummation divorce, the husband is entitled to half the mahr. Since the wife gifted the entire mahr, she has not actually returned anything to the husband for that half; she merely relieved him of payment. But the husband's right to half was not a debt of the wife; it was a right to take back half of what he gave. So he should physically take back half. The majority's istihsan: At the moment of divorce, the husband's exclusive right is that half of the mahr he gave remains safely with him without any exchange. Since the wife gifted him the whole mahr without compensation, his objective (safety of half) is fully achieved. Therefore, there is no need to take anything back. The passage then distinguishes this from cases where the mahr is non-specific (like a debt in the dhimma) or where the wife sells the mahr to the husband for a price. In those cases, the husband does have the right to reclaim half, because the wife's compensation changes the situation. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the istihsan of the majority: the husband keeps the entire mahr and reclaims nothing.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference over qiyas due to exceptional circumstances; here, the ruling that husband keeps full mahr despite the general rule.
رجوع (ruju'): The husband's act of taking back (reclaiming) half the mahr from the wife.
طلاق قبل الدخول (talaq qabl al-dukhul): Divorce pronounced before the husband has had sexual intercourse with the wife.
مقبوض (maqbood): The mahr that the wife has already taken possession of (received).
ہبہ (hibah): The wife's voluntary gift of the mahr back to the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where a wife receives a specific mahr and then gifts it back to the husband before consummation divorce, what is the Hanafi madhhab ruling (mufta bihi) regarding the husband's right to reclaim half the mahr?
A) The husband must reclaim half the mahr, based on qiyas.
B) The husband does not reclaim half the mahr, based on istihsan.
C) The husband reclaims half if the mahr was non-specific.
D) The husband reclaims the full mahr.

Key Takeaway
When a wife gifts back the specific mahr before consummation divorce, the husband's right to half is fulfilled and he does not reclaim anything—this is the mufta bihi Hanafi position based on istihsan.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Marriage with Unspecified Animal or Commodity as Mahr in Dhimma: Ruling on Reclaiming Half
Applying the previous istihsan ruling to mahr that is unspecified in dhimma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reclaiming half the mahr when the mahr is an unspecified animal/commodity in dhimma and the wife gifts it back, and explain the inter-madhhab difference.

Core Idea
When an unspecified mahr becomes specific through possession, the husband does not reclaim half if the wife gifts it back.

In this lesson, we apply the earlier istihsan ruling (husband does not reclaim half mahr when wife gifts back) to a case where the mahr is an unspecified animal or commodity owed by the husband (in dhimma). The key is that once the wife takes possession of a specific item, it becomes mutayyan bi ta'yin, so the same reasoning holds. We also contrast the Hanafi position with that of Imam Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: marriage is valid, average mahr is due, and the husband does not reclaim half if the wife gifts back the specific item after possession.
The ruling applies even when the mahr was initially unspecified in dhimma.
2
Identify opponent views
Recognize that Imam Shafi'i invalidates the specification (tasmiyah) and requires mahr al-mithl; one narration from Malik and Ahmad invalidates the marriage entirely.
Opponents argue from gharar (uncertainty) and jahalah (ignorance).
3
Follow opponent's proof
Understand their dalil: Shafi'i says tasmiyah is invalid because mahr must be known; Maliki and Hanbali say marriage is invalid due to excessive uncertainty.
Their proof relies on the principle that sale is void for jahalah, and marriage should be analogous.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal: jahalah is tolerated in marriage due to its lenient nature (maslahah and tasamuh). A small degree of uncertainty does not invalidate the contract. The average standard ensures fairness.
The difference between sale and marriage is key: sale is strict, marriage is lenient.
5
Determine thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: Under Hanafi, the marriage stands, average mahr is due, and no reclaim of half if gifted back. Under Shafi'i, mahr al-mithl is due. Under Maliki/Hanbali, marriage is void and must be renewed.
This difference affects real-world fatwa and financial obligations.

Marriage contracted on an animal or on goods that are in the dhimma (unspecified), yet the same ruling applies. And if he marries her on an animal or goods in the dhimma, the answer is the same, because the possessed is specific in return, and this is because ignorance (jahalah) is tolerated in marriage. So when it becomes specific, it becomes as if the specification (tasmiah) occurred on it. Translation: And if he marries a woman on an animal or goods while they are in the dhimma, the same ruling applies, because the possessed is specific in returning, and this is because ignorance is tolerated in marriage. So when it becomes specific, it becomes as if the specification occurred on it. Explanation: The issue is that he married and made a mahr of an animal, e.g., a horse or donkey, or goods that become obligatory in the husband's dhimma, e.g., he said: the mahr is a certain cloth, and he described its genus and type. Then the woman took possession or did not take possession but gifted (hibah) it to the husband, then the husband pronounced divorce before consummation, so the husband will not have the option to reclaim from the woman. Imam Shafi'i says this specification (tasmiah) is not valid; therefore, in this case, mahr al-mithl is obligatory. And one narration from Imam Malik and one from Imam Ahmad is that the marriage becomes invalid due to ignorance of the specified (mahr). But in our (Hanafi) view, the marriage contract is valid, and an average animal and an average cloth are obligatory. In the original issue, we said that the husband does not have the right to reclaim from the woman. The proof is that the possessed is specific in the matter of return, i.e., if the woman took possession, it becomes specifically that same thing. And when the mahr possessed is specific in return, it becomes of the type that is specific by specification (mutayyan bi ta'yin). And when the woman gifted (hibah) that which is specific by specification, then if this is after possession, the husband's exact right has reached him, because it has passed earlier that difference of cause (ikhtilaf al-sabab) is not considered. And if it is before possession, even then the husband's right has reached him, so he becomes free of half the mahr, and it is known that difference of cause is not considered. And this is because ignorance: the author has indicated two things: first, that marriage is valid in exchange for an unspecified animal and unspecified goods. Second, that the possessed is specific in return. The first thing is indicated by 'because ignorance': the outcome is that a sale for an unspecified horse is void. Thus, if something is sold in exchange for an unspecified horse, it is a void sale. But in marriage, such ignorance is tolerated. For example, if in marriage an unspecified horse is made mahr, the marriage is valid and an average horse is obligatory. The difference between sale and marriage is that marriage is based on leniency and softness, so a little ignorance is tolerated, while sale is based on strictness, so ignorance is absolutely not allowed. The second thing is indicated by 'when it becomes specific': i.e., when at the time of possession it becomes specific, then it is as if the specification occurred on that possessed. The benefit of the first is the validity of the marriage contract, even if the specified is unknown. The benefit of the second is the husband's reclaim from the woman if the woman had gifted that animal to the husband.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage applies the previous ruling (husband does not reclaim half mahr when wife gifts it back) to a case where the mahr is an unspecified animal or commodity that is in the dhimma (i.e., the husband owes it as a debt, not a specific item). The crucial point: when the wife takes possession of the unspecified item (e.g., a specific horse that is later identified), it becomes specific (mutayyan bi ta'yin). Therefore, the same reasoning applies: if she gifts it back, the husband's right to half the mahr is satisfied and he does not reclaim anything. The passage also addresses inter-madhhab disputes: Imam Shafi'i invalidates the specification, requiring mahr al-mithl; Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad in one narration invalidate the marriage. But the Hanafi position is that the marriage is valid, and an average animal/cloth is obligatory (the same 'average' standard applies). The difference between sale and marriage is highlighted: sale does not tolerate ignorance (jahalah), so a sale for an unspecified horse is void, but marriage tolerates it due to its lenient nature. Finally, the passage distinguishes the two benefits: the validity of the marriage despite an unspecified mahr, and the husband's right to reclaim (but in this case, he does not reclaim because the gifted item precisely fulfills his right).

Key Terms
ذمہ (dhimma): The husband's liability or obligation to provide a specific animal or commodity that is not yet identified; a debt-like obligation.
جہالت (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty about the exact mahr item (e.g., unspecified horse).
متعین با تعیین (mutayyan bi ta'yin): Something that becomes specific through the act of specification (ta'yin), e.g., when a horse from a herd is identified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, if a man marries a woman with an unspecified horse as mahr (in dhimma), and the woman takes possession of a specific horse then gifts it back before consummation divorce, does the husband have the right to reclaim half the mahr?
A) Yes, because the mahr was unspecified.
B) No, because the possessed item becomes specific and the istihsan ruling applies.
C) The marriage is invalid, so no mahr is due.
D) The husband must give half the average value.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an unspecified mahr in dhimma becomes valid through possession; the husband does not reclaim half if the wife gifts it back.

Nikah — Marriage

Conditional Mahr: Marriage Valid, Mahr Varies
Ruling on marriage with a condition affecting mahr amount

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a marriage with a fasid condition affecting mahr and explain how the mahr is determined based on condition fulfillment.

Core Idea
Marriage with a fasid condition is valid; mahr becomes mahr al-mithl if the condition is breached.

Marriage contracts often include conditions that go beyond the essential pillars. In Hanafi fiqh, conditions that do not contradict the essence of marriage but ask the husband to refrain from permissible acts are considered fasid (invalid). However, this does not nullify the marriage. Instead, such conditions affect the mahr obligation. This lesson unpacks the ruling from Al-Hidayah on two common conditions: not taking the wife out of the city and not marrying a second wife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the marriage and the conditions
The passage describes a marriage with a mahr of 1000 and one of two conditions: not to take the wife out of the city, or not to marry another woman over her.
These conditions involve permissible acts; they do not make the marriage temporary.
2
Determine the validity of the marriage
According to the Hanafi school, the marriage is valid despite the fasid condition. The condition is invalid because it requires refraining from something legally permissible, but it does not affect the core contract.
Contrast with a condition that makes the marriage temporary (e.g., for a month) which would render it batil.
3
Analyze the mahr when the condition is fulfilled
If the husband keeps the condition, the wife receives the named mahr (1000). The named mahr is valid in itself, and her consent was given with the condition in mind. Since the condition is met, her consent remains intact.
The condition does not invalidate the mahr; it is merely a contextual factor.
4
Analyze the mahr when the condition is breached
If the husband violates the condition (e.g., marries another or moves her), the wife's consent to the named mahr is considered withdrawn because it was contingent on the benefit she expected. She then receives mahr al-mithl (the dowry of women similar to her).
The benefit (manfa'ah) is a key element: her consent was conditional on that benefit.
5
Understand the legal reasoning (talil) and analogy
The passage analogizes to a case where the husband promises a gift or honorarium along with the mahr: if the gift is not given, the named mahr is replaced by mahr al-mithl. This shows that when a benefit is promised but not delivered, the original consent is vitiated.
The ratio legis (illa) is the loss of the intended benefit, which nullifies the wife's acceptance of the named mahr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if he marries her for a thousand with the condition that he will not take her out of the city, or with the condition that he will not marry another woman over her, then if he fulfills the condition, she gets the named (mahr), because it is a valid mahr, and her consent to the thousand is complete. And if he marries another woman over her or takes her out, she gets mahr al-mithl, because he named something in which there is benefit for her. So when the benefit is lost, her consent to the thousand ceases, so mahr al-mithl is completed for her, just as in the case of mentioning honor and gift along with the thousand. Translation: And when he marries a woman for a thousand with the condition that he will not take her out of the city, or with the condition that he will not marry another woman over her, then if he fulfills the condition, she gets the named (mahr), because the named item is valid as mahr, and her consent to the thousand is complete. And if he marries another woman over her or takes her out, she gets mahr al-mithl, because he mentioned something in which there is benefit for her. So when the benefit is lost, her consent to the thousand ceases, so her mahr al-mithl is completed, just as in the case of mentioning honor and gift with the thousand. Explanation: The scenario is that a man marries a woman and makes a mahr of one thousand rupees with the condition that he will not take her out of the city, or that he will not marry another woman in her presence. This marriage is valid, even though the condition of not traveling and not marrying is a fasid (invalid) condition, and it is fasid because it necessitates refraining from something legislated. Therefore, if the husband fulfills the condition, the woman gets the named amount, i.e., one thousand, because the named amount is capable of being mahr, and the woman's consent to the thousand is complete.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage addresses a marriage contract where the mahr is set at a specific amount (1000) with two possible conditions: (1) the husband will not take her out of the city, or (2) he will not marry another woman. The first ruling: if the husband fulfills the condition, the wife is entitled to the named mahr (1000) because it is a valid mahr and her consent was given based on that condition. However, the condition itself is considered fasid (invalid) in Hanafi law because it asks the husband to refrain from something that is legally permissible (traveling and marrying another woman are not prohibited). Even though the condition is invalid, the marriage itself remains valid. The second ruling: if the husband violates the condition (marries another woman or takes her out), then the wife does not get the named 1000; instead, she gets mahr al-mithl (the mahr of her peers). This is because her consent to the 1000 was contingent on the benefit (manfa'ah) of being the sole wife or staying in the city. When that benefit is lost, her consent is considered withdrawn, so the named mahr is not binding. This is analogous to a case where the husband offers mahr plus an honorarium or gift: if the gift is not given, mahr al-mithl becomes due. The passage emphasizes that the marriage is valid despite the invalid condition, and the condition itself does not affect the mahr unless it is breached. The relied-upon position: the wife's mahr depends on the husband's compliance with the condition; if he complies, she gets the named amount; if not, she gets mahr al-mithl.

Key Terms
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): An invalid condition that does not void the marriage but affects the mahr obligation if breached.
مہر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr that is customary for women of similar status to the bride; due when named mahr is invalid or consent is lost.
نفع (nusf (nuf'?)): Benefit or advantage; here, the wife's benefit from not being taken out of the city or from being the only wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi marriage, if a husband marries a woman for 1000 mahr with the condition that he will not marry another woman over her, and then he does marry another woman, what mahr is the first wife entitled to?
A) The full 1000 because the condition is fasid.
B) Mahr al-mithl because her consent to the 1000 was contingent on the benefit.
C) No mahr because the condition made the marriage invalid.
D) Half the 1000 as per pre-consummation divorce.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a marriage with a fasid condition is valid; the mahr is determined by the condition's fulfillment: named if kept, mahr al-mithl if broken.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Marriage with Stipulation: Ruling on Mahr When Condition Breached
States ruling on mahr when husband breaches stipulation restricting his actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr when a husband breaches a shart fāsid in marriage and apply the qiyas to determine whether the named mahr or mahr al-mithl is due.

Core Idea
A void condition does not invalidate the marriage but may entitle the wife to mahr al-mithl if breached.

In Hanafi marriage law, conditions that restrict a husband's permissible actions (like not taking the wife out of the city or not marrying a second wife) are considered invalid (shart fāsid). However, they do not nullify the marriage. This lesson examines what happens when such a condition is breached: the wife's original consent to the named mahr may be vitiated, leading to the obligation of mahr al-mithl. The ruling is established through analogy to the case of a promised gift alongside the mahr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State clearly: marriage with a shart fāsid is valid (sahih) according to the Hanafi school. The condition itself is void and unenforceable.
This distinguishes Hanafi from some other schools where such conditions might invalidate the contract.
2
Determine the effect on mahr when condition is breached
If the husband breaches the condition (e.g., marries another wife or takes the first wife out of the city), the wife's consent to the lower named mahr is considered to have lapsed. This triggers the possibility of mahr al-mithl (customary dower).
The condition must be one that provides a clear benefit to the wife.
3
Apply the two-tier comparison between mahr al-mithl and named mahr
Compare mahr al-mithl to the named mahr. If mahr al-mithl is greater, she receives mahr al-mithl. If it is equal or less, she receives the named mahr. The named mahr stands if it is not less than the mithl.
This preserves the wife's right to a fair dower while recognizing her initial acceptance of the lower amount.
4
Trace the dalil: Qiyas
The derivation is by qiyas to the case where a husband promises a gift (kiramah or hadiyya) alongside the mahr but fails to deliver it. Just as the wife's consent to the lower mahr is contingent on receiving the gift, here her consent is contingent on the benefit of the condition. When the benefit is lost, her consent ceases, and mahr al-mithl becomes due.
The analogy is explicit in the text: 'ka-mā fī tasmiyat al-karāmah wa-l-hadiyya ma'a al-alf'.
5
Evaluate the cross-madhhab dimension
The Hanafi position is mukhtalaf fih. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may consider such conditions as affecting the validity of the marriage itself. However, this passage focuses solely on the Hanafi ruling.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that in Hanafi law, the marriage remains intact with a potential adjustment to the mahr, rather than annulment.

Source Text
