Book of Nikah. This action becomes specified. And when the mahr is specified in the return of the object taken, then what is specified is of the same type as the specification. And when the woman gifted the specified object, then if this is after possession, the husband's right to that specific thing has been established, because it has passed earlier that difference of cause is not considered. And if this is before possession, then also the husband's right to it has been established, and he is freed from half of the mahr, and it is known that difference of cause is not considered. The author pointed to two things by saying 'this is because of ignorance'. First, that marriage in exchange for an unspecified animal or unspecified goods is permissible. Second, that the received object is specified in the return. The first point: from 'because of ignorance' it follows that sale in exchange for an unspecified horse is invalid. However, in marriage such ignorance is tolerated. The benefit of the first is that the marriage contract is valid even if the named dower is unknown. The benefit of the second is the husband's right to take back from the woman if she gifted the animal. He married the woman on the condition that he would not take her out of the city or would not marry another over her. If he fulfills the condition, the named mahr is due; otherwise, mahr al-mithl. And if he married her for one thousand on the condition that he would not take her out of the town or that he would not marry another over her, if he fulfills the condition, she has the named mahr because it is capable of being mahr and her consent to the one thousand was complete. And if he married another over her or took her out, she has mahr al-mithl because he mentioned something that has benefit for her; upon loss of that benefit, her consent to the one thousand ceases, so her mahr al-mithl is completed, just as in the naming of honorarium and gift along with one thousand. Explanation: The case is that a man married a woman and made a dower of one thousand rupees on the condition that he would not take her out of the city or would not marry another in her presence. This marriage is valid even though the condition of not traveling and not marrying is an invalid condition, because it necessitates refraining from a commanded matter. So if the husband fulfills the condition, the woman gets the named one thousand. And if he does not fulfill it, then it is seen whether mahr al-mithl is less than, more than, or equal to the named dower. If mahr al-mithl is more than the named one thousand, then the woman gets mahr al-mithl. The proof is that the husband mentioned something that has benefit for her; hence due to that benefit she agreed to lower the mahr below the mithl, so the reduction in mahr is in exchange for that benefit. Upon the loss of that benefit, her consent to the one thousand ceases, so her mahr al-mithl is completed. So if this condition of honorarium and gift is not fulfilled, then mahr al-mithl is obligatory. Similarly here. And if mahr al-mithl is less than or equal to the named one thousand, then even if the condition is not fulfilled, the named one thousand is obligatory, and this condition is a gratuitous act from the husband.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with rational proof regarding marriage with stipulations that restrict the husband. The author first discusses the effect of a wife gifting the mahr that was specified after possession, and then transitions to the core issue: marriage conditioned on the husband not taking the wife out of town or not marrying another wife. The marriage is valid despite the condition being invalid (since it prohibits something permissible), but the condition itself is not binding. If the husband fulfills the condition voluntarily, the named mahr is due. If he breaches it, the rule depends on whether mahr al-mithl exceeds the named mahr. The proof is rational: the wife's consent to the lower mahr was contingent on the benefit of the condition. When that benefit is lost, her consent ceases, and she is entitled to mahr al-mithl—by analogy to the case where a husband promises a gift ('kiramah' or 'hadiyya') along with the mahr but fails to provide it. If the mithl is equal or less, the named mahr stands because there was no actual loss.

Key Terms
شرط فاسد (shart fāsid): A stipulation that is not recognized by the Law, such as a condition that restricts a permissible action, considered invalid but does not nullify the contract in nikah.
مہر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The customary dower for a woman of similar status to the bride, used when the named mahr is invalid or when consent is vitiated.

Nikah — Marriage

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Alternative Conditional Mahr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of alternative mahr conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three Hanafi positions on alternative conditional mahr and apply Abu Hanifa's ruling to determine the mahr due.

Core Idea
In a marriage with two alternative mahr conditions, each condition is evaluated independently; a condition that incentivizes harm is invalid.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute over a marriage contract where the mahr depends on whether the husband keeps the wife in her city or takes her out. Three positions are recorded: Imam Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and Imam Zufar. Understanding how each evaluates the conditions is crucial for determining the mahr in such cases. The text also draws an analogy to the law of ijarah (hire), illustrating how alternative conditions are treated across contract types.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the alternative conditions
The marriage contract specifies two mutually exclusive conditions: if the husband keeps the wife in her city, mahr = 1000; if he takes her out, mahr = 2000. These are conditions on the basis of alternative (shart 'ala al-sabil al-badal).
The key is that the husband's action determines which condition is triggered.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifa holds the first condition valid (1000 for staying) and the second invalid. Because taking the wife out is disapproved (makruh) and incentivizing it with a higher mahr is invalid. If he takes her out, she gets mahr al-mithl, bounded between 1000 and 2000.
This position protects the wife from being pressured to relocate for financial gain.
3
State Sahibayn's position and reasoning
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider both conditions valid. If he keeps her, she gets 1000; if he takes her out, she gets 2000. They view the conditions as permissible private agreements.
They prioritize party autonomy over potential harm.
4
State Zufar's position and reasoning
Zufar deems both conditions invalid because they introduce uncertainty (gharar) into the mahr. She gets mahr al-mithl in all cases, but not less than 1000 nor more than 2000.
Zufar avoids any uncertainty about the amount from the outset.
5
Compare practical outcomes (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, if the husband takes her out, she gets mahr al-mithl (not necessarily 2000); under Sahibayn, she gets 2000; under Zufar, she gets mahr al-mithl bounded by 1000-2000. The difference is significant when mahr al-mithl differs from the stipulated amounts.
The text implies Abu Hanifa's view is preferred by presenting it first and in detail.

Source Text

مرد نے عورت سے اس شرط پر نکاح کیا کہ شہر میں رکھے گا تو ایک ہزار دور نہ دو ہزار ، اگر شرط پوری کرے تو مہر ایک ہزار ہو گا ورنہ مہرشل جو دو ہزار سے بڑھے بھی نہیں اور ایک ہزار سے کم بھی نہ ہو
و لوتزوجها على الف ان اقام بها و على الفين ان اخرجها فان اقام بهافلها الالف وان اخرجها فلها مهر المثل لایزاد على الفين ولا ينقص عن الألف وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقالا الشرطان جميعا جائز ان حتى كان لها الالف ان اقام بها و الالفان ان اخرجها وقال زفر الشرطان جميعا فاسدان ويكون لهامهر مثلها لا ينقص من الف ولا يزاد على الفين واصل المسئالة فى الاجارات فى قوله ان خطته اليوم فلک درهم وان خطته غدا فلک نصف درهم وسنبينها فيه ان شاء الله
ترجمہ اور اگر نکاح کیا عورت سے ایک ہزار پراگر ٹھہرایا اس کو اس کے شہر میں اور دو ہزار پر اگر نکالا اس کو (اس کے شہر سے ) پس اگر قیام کرایا اس کو اس کے (شہر میں ) تو عورت کیلئے ایک ہزار ہے اور اگر نکالا اس کو تو اس کیلئے مہر مثل ہے نہ دو ہزار پر زیادہ کیا جائے اور نہ ایک ہزار سے کم کیا جائے۔ اور یہ ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ دونوں شرطیں جائز ہیں ۔ حتی کہ عورت کیلئے ایک ہزار ہوگا اگر قیام کرایا اس کو اس کے (شہر) میں اور دو ہزار ہیں اگر نکالا اسکو۔ اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ دونوں شرطیں فاسد ہیں اور عورت کیلئے مہر مثل ہو گا۔ ایک ہزار سے کم نہ کیا جائے اور دو ہزار پر زیادہ نہ کیا جائے اور مسئلہ کی دلیل کتاب الاجارات میں ہے اس کے اس قول کے تحت۔ کہ اگر سیا تو نے اس (کپڑے) کو آج تو تیرے لئے ایک درہم ہے اور اگر سیا تو نے اس (کپڑے) کو کل آئندہ تو تیرے لیئے نصف درہم ہے ۔ اور ہم بیان کریں گے اس کو انشاء اللہ ۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک مرد نے کسی عورت سے نکاح کیا اور دو شرطیں علی السبیل البدل ذکر کر دیں مثلاً کہا کہ اگر عورت کو اس کے شہر میں مقیم رکھا تو مہر ایک ہزار ہوگا۔ اور اگر اس کو اس کے شہر سے نکالا تو مہر دو ہزار ہوگا۔ اس مسئلہ میں امام ابو حنیفہ کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ شرط اول جائز ہے اور شرط ثانی فاسد ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر مقیم رکھا تو عورت کیلئے ایک ہزار ہو گا اور اگر اس کو اس کے شہر سے نکال دیا تو مہر دو ہزار ہوگا۔ اس مسئلہ میں امام ابو حنیفہ کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ شرط اول جائز ہے اور شرط ثانی فاسد ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر مقیم رکھا تو عورت کیلئے ایک ہزار ہو گا اور اگر اس کو اس کے شہر سے نکال دیا تو مہر مثل واجب ہوگا اور صاحین کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ دونوں شرطیں جائز ہیں چنانچہ اقامت کی صورت میں ایک ہزار مہر ہوگا اور اخراج کی صورت میں مہر مثل واجب ہوگا۔ جو ایک ہزار سے کم اور دو ہزار سے زائد نہ ہو۔ صاحب ہدایہ
A man married a woman on condition that if he keeps her in the city, (the mahr is) one thousand, and if he takes her out, two thousand. If he fulfills the condition, the mahr is one thousand, otherwise mahr al-mithl, which does not exceed two thousand nor fall below one thousand. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Both conditions are valid, so she has one thousand if he keeps her in the city, and two thousand if he takes her out. Zufar said: Both conditions are invalid, and she has mahr al-mithl, not less than one thousand nor more than two thousand. The origin of the issue is in the book of Ijarat in his statement: 'If you sew it today, you have one dirham; if you sew it tomorrow, you have half a dirham.' We will explain it there, if Allah wills. Translation: ... Explanation: The case is that a man married a woman and mentioned two conditions as alternatives. The madhhab of Abu Hanifa is that the first condition is valid and the second is invalid; so if he keeps her, she gets one thousand; if he takes her out, mahr al-mithl is obligatory. Sahibayn said both conditions are valid; so if he keeps her, one thousand; if he takes her out, two thousand. Zufar said both are invalid, and she gets mahr al-mithl between one and two thousand.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute over a marriage contract with alternative stipulations for mahr: if the husband keeps the wife in her city, the mahr is 1000; if he takes her out, it is 2000. Three positions are recorded: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the first condition (residence) is valid, but the second (departure) is invalid because it incentivizes a harmful act (taking the wife out). Therefore, if he keeps her, she gets 1000; if he takes her out, she gets mahr al-mithl, capped at 2000 and floored at 1000. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider both conditions valid, so she gets 1000 if she stays and 2000 if she is taken out—emphasizing that the condition is permissible as it is a private agreement. Imam Zufar deems both conditions invalid, leading to mahr al-mithl in all cases, but not less than 1000 nor more than 2000. The author notes the origin of this dispute in the law of ijarah (hire), where a tailor's wage depends on time of completion, illustrating how alternative conditions in contracts are evaluated. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated, but the text presents Abu Hanifa's view in detail, implying its weight.

Key Terms
شرط علی السبیل البدل (shart 'alā al-sabīl al-badal): Alternative conditions; two stipulations that are mutually exclusive, one of which will be fulfilled depending on the husband's action.
مہر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The standard dower for a woman of equal status, used when the named mahr is invalid or unenforceable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the alternative mahr scenario (stay: 1000, leave: 2000), if the husband takes his wife to another city, what does Imam Abu Hanifa rule regarding the mahr?
A) 1000 because he did not fulfill the first condition
B) 2000 as per the second condition
C) Mahr al-mithl, not less than 1000 nor more than 2000
D) No mahr at all

Key Takeaway
In a marriage with alternative mahr conditions, each stipulation is evaluated independently; one that incentivizes harm is invalid, and the wife receives mahr al-mithl instead.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Conditional Mahr: Residency-Based Alternatives
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of alternative mahr conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on alternative mahr conditions based on residency, explain their proofs, and identify the practical (thamarah al-khilaf) differences.

Core Idea
When mahr is conditioned on the husband's future action, gharar invalidates the uncertain term, but the marriage remains valid.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: if a husband stipulates two different mahr amounts depending on whether he keeps his wife in her hometown or moves her elsewhere, which condition is valid? The three positions—Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Zufar—reveal different approaches to uncertainty (gharar) and the binding force of stipulations. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to analyze contractual conditions in nikah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the three rulings
Read the passage and note the conditional mahr scenario: 1000 if kept, 2000 if taken out. Then identify the three rulings: Abu Hanifa (first valid, second fasid), Sahibayn (both valid), Zufar (both fasid).
The mukhtalaf fih is the second condition.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa views the second condition as creating jahalah (uncertainty) because it contradicts the first—the husband's future action makes the exact mahr unknown at contract time. This makes it fasid, so mahr al-mithl is due, capped between 1000 and 2000.
The cap protects the wife from being underpaid.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's reasoning
The Sahibayn rely on the hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions' (al-muslimuna 'ala shurutihim). For them, both conditions are valid because the parties consented and the amount is determined by the husband's choice, not uncertain.
They see no gharar because the condition is tied to an event that will occur.
4
Analyze Zufar's reasoning
Zufar holds that both conditions are fasid because at the time of contract, the mahr is completely unknown—it depends on an uncertain future event. Hence mahr al-mithl is due from the start.
Zufar applies the strictest view on gharar.
5
Connect to the ijarah analogy
The author notes that the basis of this issue is in ijarah (hire contracts) with alternative wages. The same three positions appear there, showing the consistency of the Hanafi school's approach to uncertainty across different contract types.
This qiyas (analogy) is the illa behind the rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لوتزوجها على الف ان اقام بها و على الفين ان اخرجها فان اقام بهافلها الالف وان اخرجها فلها مهر المثل لایزاد على الفين ولا ينقص عن الألف وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقالا الشرطان جميعا جائز ان حتى كان لها الالف ان اقام بها و الالفان ان اخرجها وقال زفر الشرطان جميعا فاسدان ويكون لهامهر مثلها لا ينقص من الف ولا يزاد على الفين واصل المسئالة فى الاجارات فى قوله ان خطته اليوم فلک درهم وان خطته غدا فلک نصف درهم وسنبينها فيه ان شاء الله
And if he marries her for one thousand if he keeps her in her city, and for two thousand if he takes her out, then if he keeps her in her city, she gets one thousand; and if he takes her out, she gets mahr al-mithl, not exceeding two thousand and not less than one thousand. This is according to Abu Hanifa. Both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: both conditions are valid, so she gets one thousand if he keeps her, and two thousand if he takes her out. Zufar said: both conditions are void, and she gets mahr al-mithl, not less than one thousand and not more than two thousand. The basis of the issue is in the Book of Ijarah in his saying: 'If you sew it today, you get one dirham; if you sew it tomorrow, you get half a dirham.' We will explain it there, God willing.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a marriage contract where the husband stipulates two alternative mahr amounts contingent on whether he keeps the wife in her hometown or takes her elsewhere. Abu Hanifa rules: only the first condition (keeping her) is valid; if he takes her out, mahr al-mithl is wajib, capped between 1000 and 2000. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider both conditions valid, so each scenario triggers its specified amount. Zufar deems both conditions fasid, leading to mahr al-mithl within the same range. The commentator notes that the underlying legal analogy is from ijarah contracts with alternative wages. The reasoning revolves around gharar (uncertainty): Abu Hanifa sees the second condition as creating jahalah (uncertainty) because it is contradicted by the first, making it void. The Sahibayn prioritize the hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions.' Zufar emphasizes the inherent uncertainty of two alternative amounts for a single act.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The standard dowry for a woman of her status, determined by her social position, family, and beauty, etc.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): A condition that is invalid because it creates uncertainty (jahalah) or contradicts the nature of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a husband marries a woman with the condition that if he keeps her in her city, mahr is 1000, and if he takes her out, mahr is 2000, what happens if he takes her out?
A) She gets 2000 as specified.
B) She gets mahr al-mithl, not exceeding 2000 and not less than 1000.
C) The marriage is invalid.
D) She gets nothing because the condition is void.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, conditional mahr can be valid or fasid depending on uncertainty; the marriage always remains valid, and mahr al-mithl compensates any fasid condition.

Mahr with an Unspecified Choice Between Two Slaves
Intra-Hanafi dispute on alternative mahr objects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on mahr when the wife has a choice between two items of different value and apply the ruling to similar ambiguous mahr cases.

Core Idea
When mahr is ambiguous, Abu Hanifa defaults to mahr al-mithl for justice; the Sahibayn give the certain minimum (inferior).

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: a marriage contract specifies mahr as 'this slave or that slave'—one inferior, one superior. The question is: what does the wife receive? Abu Hanifa ties the amount to her mahr al-mithl, while his two disciples insist on the inferior in all cases. Understanding the reasoning behind each view deepens your grasp of how Hanafi jurists handle contractual ambiguity and protect equity.

Guided Path
1
State the case and the ruling difference
Identify the facts: nikah with mahr as a choice between two slaves of unequal value. Note that both sides agree the marriage is valid; only the amount of mahr is disputed.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not a cross-school one.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's three-scenario ruling
Recall: if mahr al-mithl is less than the inferior → inferior; if mahr al-mithl is more than the superior → superior; if between → mahr al-mithl.
Mahr al-mithl is the typical mahr for a woman of her status.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's single ruling
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say: she gets the inferior (awks) in all scenarios, whether before or after consummation (with halving if divorced before).
They hold the contract implies certainty of the minimum.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's dalil (evidence)
Their reasoning: since the named mahr cannot be specified (due to the choice), the certain minimum is taken by default. They analogize to khul' and manumission where ambiguous property clauses default to the lesser amount.
The key point is they consider specification (ta'yin) impossible.
5
Analyze Abu Hanifa's dalil
Abu Hanifa argues the original obligation (asl) is mahr al-mithl because it is the most just (al-adl). The ambiguity does not justify abandoning equity; rather, mahr al-mithl fills the gap to ensure fairness.
He prioritizes justice over mechanical certainty.
6
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical difference: under Abu Hanifa the wife may get more than the inferior; under Sahibayn she always gets the minimum. The hidayah often follows Abu Hanifa, but later practice may lean toward the Sahibayn for predictability.
The text does not explicitly state mufta bihi; both views remain within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لوتزوجها على هذا العبد او على هذا العبد فاذا احدهما اوكس والأخر ارفع فان كان مهر مثلها اقل من اوكسهما فلها الاوكس و ان كان اكثر من ارفعهما فلها الارفع وان كان بينهما فلها مهر مثلها و هذا عند ابي حنيفة وقالا لها الاوكس فى ذلك كله فان طلقها قبل الدخول بها فلها نصف الاوكس في ذلك كله بالاجماع لهما ان المصير الى مهر المثل لتعذر ايجاب المسمى وقدامكن ايجاب الاوكس اذا الاقل متيقن وصار كالخلع والاعتاق على مال ولا بى حنيفة ان الموجب الاصلى مهر المثل اذهو الاعدل
And if he marries her upon this slave or upon this slave, and one of them is inferior and the other superior, then if her mahr al-mithl is less than the inferior, she gets the inferior; if it is more than the superior, she gets the superior; and if it is between them, she gets her mahr al-mithl. This is according to Abu Hanifa. Both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: she gets the inferior in all these cases. If he divorces her before consummation, she gets half the inferior in all these cases by consensus. Their evidence: recourse to mahr al-mithl is not possible because specifying the named amount is impossible, but it is possible to give the inferior because the lesser is certain, and it is like khul' and manumission for property. And Abu Hanifa's evidence: the original obligation is mahr al-mithl because it is the most just.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This is another intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a marriage contract where the mahr is left as an unfixed alternative between two slaves—one of lower value, one higher. The exact mahr is unknown until the husband's choice? Actually, the contract seems to give the wife a choice of one of two slaves. Actually reading: 'on this slave or on this slave' suggests the mahr is either one or the other, but it's not determined. The ruling: Abu Hanifa says that if the wife's mahr al-mithl is less than the lower-valued slave, she gets the lower; if mahr al-mithl exceeds the higher, she gets the higher; if mahr al-mithl falls between the two values, she gets mahr al-mithl. The Sahibayn say in all cases she gets the inferior slave. If divorce before consummation, half the inferior. The Sahibayn's reasoning: since the exact mahr cannot be specified due to ambiguity, the certain minimum (the inferior) is given, analogous to khul' and manumission where the certain amount is taken. Abu Hanifa argues that the original basis is mahr al-mithl (the just amount), and since choosing between the extremes is arbitrary, mahr al-mithl takes precedence to achieve justice.

Key Terms
أوكس (awks): The inferior, lower-value item (here, the less valuable slave).
أرفع (arfa'): The superior, higher-value item (here, the more valuable slave).
مهر مثلها (mahr al-mithl): The standard mahr for a woman of similar status in her family and community.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, if a woman is married with a choice between a slave worth 300 and one worth 800 as mahr, and her mahr al-mithl is 500, what does she receive?
A) The inferior slave (300).
B) The superior slave (800).
C) Mahr al-mithl (500).
D) Half of the inferior (150).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when mahr is left as an unfixed choice between two items of different value, there is an intra-madhhab dispute: Abu Hanifa defaults to mahr al-mithl for justice, while the Sahibayn give the certain minimum (inferior).

Mahr for One of Two Unspecified Slaves: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr ambiguity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding mahr when the husband specifies it as one of two unnamed slaves, and apply the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn to determine the wife's entitlement.

Core Idea
When mahr is ambiguous, Abu Hanifa falls back to the just equivalent (mahr al-mithl), while the Sahibayn default to the lower of the two possible values.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: a husband marries his wife on a mahr of one of two slaves without specifying which. One slave is low-value (awks), the other high-value (arfa'). What does the wife receive? The two founding disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), disagree with Imam Abu Hanifa over the proper legal method. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi approach to ambiguous stipulations in marriage contracts and the role of mahr al-mithl as the default obligation.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the two positions
First, describe the case: husband says 'I marry you on one of these two slaves,' one worth 1000, the other 2000. Then state Abu Hanifa's position (wife gets mahr al-mithl if between, awks if less, arfa if more) and the Sahibayn's position (always awks).
Make sure to note that the marriage itself is valid; only the mahr amount is disputed.
2
Identify the core legal principle (موجب اصلی)
The dispute turns on what the original obligator (al-mujib al-asli) is. For Abu Hanifa it is mahr al-mithl; for the Sahibayn it is the specified mahr (mahr musamma). Understand why each side takes this view.
Mahr al-mithl is the fair equivalent of the vulva's benefit; mahr musamma is a voluntary agreement.
3
Trace Abu Hanifa's dalil
Abu Hanifa argues that since the specification is invalid due to ambiguity (jahala), we revert to the original obligor: mahr al-mithl. Then he uses ijtihad: if mahr al-mithl exceeds arfa, wife accepted less; if below awks, husband agreed to more; otherwise mahr al-mithl stands.
This is based on presumed consent.
4
Trace the Sahibayn's dalil
The Sahibayn argue that the original obligor is the specified mahr, but since it is impossible to determine, we must give the least certain amount (awks) by qiyas on khul' and itq where ambiguous consideration resolves to the minimum.
They claim the wife knew the ambiguity and agreed to the lower possibility.
5
Analyze the qiyas and Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa rejects the qiyas as ma'a al-fariq (diss analogous) because in khul' and itq there is no original obligor for the consideration, unlike marriage where mahr al-mithl is fixed. He thus preserves the priority of mahr al-mithl.
This step highlights the methodological difference in analogical reasoning.
6
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa the wife may receive a higher value (arfa) if her mahr al-mithl is high; under the Sahibayn she always gets the lower (awks). In divorce before consummation, both agree on half of aws.
The dispute shows how different usul assumptions lead to different fiqh results.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اللقب الهدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد چهارم کتاب النکاح والعدول عنه عند صحة التسمية وقد فسدت لمكان الجهالة بخلاف الخلع والاعتاق لانه لا موجب له في البدل الا ان مهر المثل اذاكان اكثر من الارفع فالمرأة رضيت بالحط وان كان انقص من الاوكس فالزوج رضى بالزيادة والواجب في الطلاق قبل الدخول فى مثله المتعة ونصف الاوكس يزيد عليها في العادة فوجب لاعترافه بالزيادة
ترجمہ اور اگر نکاح کیا اس غلام پر یا اس غلام پر پس ان دونوں میں سے ایک اوکس ہے اور دوسرا ارفع پس اگر مہر مثل ان دونوں میں اوکس سے کم ہے تو عورت کیلئے اوکس ہوگا اور اگر مہر مثل ان دونوں میں کے ارفع سے زائد ہے تو عورت کیلئے ارفع ہو گا۔ اور اگر مہر مثل ان دونوں کے درمیان میں ہے تو عورت کیلئے مہر مثل ہوگا۔ اور یہ ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ عورت کیلئے ان تمام صورتوں میں اوکس ہے۔ پس اگر طلاق دی اس عورت کو دخول سے پہلے تو اس کیلئے نصف اوکس ہوگا۔ ان تمام صورتوں میں بالا تفاق۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مہر مثل کی طرف رجوع مسمی کو واجب کرنے کے متعذر ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے۔ اور اوکس کا واجب کرنا ممکن ہے۔ اسلئے کہ اقل متیقن ہے اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ ضلع اور اعتاق علی مال۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ موجب اصلی مہر مثل ہے کیونکہ وہ اعدل ہے۔ اور عدول اس سے صحت تسمیہ کے وقت ہوگا۔ اور تسمیہ فاسد ہو گیا جہالت کی وجہ سے بخلاف خلع اور اعتماق کے اسلئے کہ اس کیلئے بدل میں کوئی موجب اصلی نہیں ہے۔ مگر یہ کہ مہر مثل جب ارفع سے زیادہ ہو تو عورت کم کر دینے پر راضی ہوگئی اوراگر مہر مثل اوکس سے کم ہے تو شوہر زیادہ کرنے پر راضی ہو گیا اور واجب طلاق قبل الدخول میں اس جیسی صورت میں متعہ ہے اور نصف اوکس عادة متعہ سے زائد ہوتا ہے پس نصف اوکس واجب ہوگا۔ شوہر کے زیادتی کا اعتراف کرنے کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ دو غلام سامنے موجود ہیں ان میں ایک کی قیمت کم ہے اور دوسرے کی زیادہ مثلاً ایک ایک ہزار کی مالیت کا ہے اور دوسرا دو ہزار کی مالیت کا شوہر نے بغیر متعین کیئے ان دونوں میں سے ایک کو مہر مقرر کیا اور کہا کہ مہر میں یہ غلام دوں گا۔ یا یہ تو اس مسئلہ میں امام صاحب کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ مہر مثل کو دیکھا جائے کہ وہ اوکس یعنی جو غلام قیمت میں انقص ہے اس سے کم ہے یا مہر مثل اوکس کے مساوی ہے یا ارفع سے زائد ہے یا اوکس اور ارفع کے درمیان میں ہے۔ اگر مہر مثل اوکس سے کم یا مساوی ہے تو اس صورت میں عورت کیلئے غلام اوکس ہوگا اور اگر مہر مثل غلام ارفع سے زائد ہے تو اس صورت میں عورت کیلئے غلام درمیان میں ہو البتہ اگر شوہر نے طلاق قبل الدخول دے دی تو بالا تفاق تمام صورتوں میں نصف اوکس ہو گا۔ دلائل سے پہلے یہ سمجھ لیجیے کہ بدل بضع میں موجب اصلی کیا ہے؟ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ موجب اصلی مہر سمی ہے۔ پس جب تک مہر مسمی کا واجب کر ناممکن ہے مہرمشکل کی طرف عدول نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اور امام صاحب فرماتے ہیں کہ موجب اصلی مہرمشکل ہے کیونکہ مہرشل بضع کا معادل یعنی مساوی ہے کمی زیادتی کو قبول نہیں کرتا ہے وجہ یہ ہے کہ مہر مثل منافع بضع کی قیمت ہے۔ اور شیء کی قیمت کمی اور زیادتی کو قبول نہیں کرتی ہے بخلاف تسمیہ کے کہ وہ زیادتی اور کی کو قبول کر لیتا ہے لہذا امام صاحب کے نزدیک مہر مثل سے مہر سمی کی طرف عددل اس وقت ہوگا جبکہ تسمیہ صحیح ہو ورنہ عدول نہیں کیا جائے گا۔
اب صاحبین کی دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہوگا کہ مہر مثل کی طرف عدول اسی وقت ہو سکتا ہے جبکہ مہر سمی کا واجب کرنا متعذ رہو۔ اور یہاں غلام اوکس کا واجب کرنا ممکن ہے۔ کیونکہ غلام اوکس اقل بے قیمت میں اور اقل متعین ہوتا ہے لہذا اس متعین کو واجب کر دیں گے۔ اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسا کہ کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا کہ میں نے تجھ سے خلع کیا اس غلام پر یا اس غلام پر یا مولیٰ نے غلام سے کہا کہ میں نے تجھ کو آزاد کیا اس غلام پر یا اس غلام پر ۔ ان دونوں مسئلوں میں اوکس متعین ہے۔ لہذا مسئلہ مہر میں بھی غلام اوکس متعین ہوگا۔ امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ موجب اصلی مہر مثل ہے اور مہرشل سے عدول صحت تسمیہ کے وقت ہوگا اور یہاں دو غلاموں میں تردد اور شک کی وجہ سے جہالت پیدا ہو گئی۔ پس اس جہالت کی وجہ سے تسمیہ فاسد ہو گیا۔ لہذا مہر سمی واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ اور رہا ضلع اور
اعتاق تو ان پر قیاس درست نہیں کیونکہ بدل کے سلسلہ میں ان دونوں کیلئے کوئی موجب اصلی نہیں ہے لہذا یہ قیاس مع الفارق ہوگا۔ الاان مهر المثل سے ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے۔ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ جب مہر مثل اصل ہے تینوں حالتوں میں تو مہر مثل واجب ہونا چاہئے تھا ۔ خواہ مہر مثل اوکس سے کم ہو یا ارفع سے زائد ہو یا دونوں کے درمیان میں ۔ حالانکہ امام صاحب اس کے قائل نہیں ہیں۔ جواب ۔ حکم تو یہی ہے لیکن جس وقت مہر مثل ارفع سے زائد ہے تو عورت اپنے مہر مثل سے کم کر دینے پر راضی ہوگئی۔ اور اگر مہر مثل اوکس سے کم ہے تو شوہر مہر مثل پر زیادتی کیلئے راضی ہو گیا پس ہم نے ان دونوں کی رضامندی پر عمل کیا ہے۔
والواجب فی الطلاق سے ایک اشکال کا جواب ہے۔ اشکال یہ ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جب تسمیہ فاسد ہے تو طلاق قبل الدخول کی صورت میں متعہ واجب ہونا چاہئے تھا۔ نصف اوکس کیوں واجب کیا گیا ہے۔ جواب نصف اوکس کا وجوب بطر یقہ متعہ ہی ہے لہذا کوئی اشکال نہیں ۔ لیکن اشکال اب بھی باقی ہے۔ اسلئے کہ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ جس طرح طلاق قبل الدخول کی صورت میں فساد تسمیہ کے وقت مہر مثل واجب ہوتا ہے اسی طرح طلاق قبل الدخول کی صورت میں متعہ واجب ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ جس طرح طلاق بعد الدخول میں مہر مثل موجب اصلی ہے اس طرح طلاق قبل الدخول میں متعہ موجب اصلی ہے۔ جواب واجب تو متعہ ہی ہونا چاہئے تھا لیکن چونکہ بالعموم نصف اوکس متعہ سے زائد قیمت کا ہوتا ہے اور شوہر اس زیادتی کا اعتراف بھی کر چکا اسلئے متعہ واجب کر دیا گیا۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر متعہ نصف اوکس سے زیادہ مالیت کا ہے تو نصف اوکس واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ بلکہ متعہ کا حکم کریں گے۔ واللہ اعلم
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the mahr when a husband marries his wife on one of two slaves without specification—one low-value (awks) and one high-value (arfa'). The Arabic matn from al-Hidayah states the core ruling: the default obligator is mahr al-mithl (standard mahr), but deviation occurs when specification is valid. Here specification is invalid due to ambiguity (jahāla), so mahr al-mithl is considered. If mahr al-mithl exceeds the higher slave, the wife is deemed to have accepted less; if less than the lower slave, the husband agreed to more; if between, mahr al-mithl applies. The Urdu commentary explains two positions: Imam Abu Hanifa looks to mahr al-mithl, giving the wife awks if mahr al-mithl is less than awks, arfa if mahr al-mithl exceeds arfa, and mahr al-mithl if between. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the wife always gets awks in all cases. In case of divorce before consummation, all agree on half of awks. The passage then provides proofs: The Sahibayn argue that the original obligor is the specified mahr, but since it's impossible to determine, we fall back to the minimum (awks) by analogy with khul' and itq. Abu Hanifa responds that the original obligor is mahr al-mithl because it is the just equivalent of the vulva's benefit; specification only diverts from it when valid. Since the specification here is invalid due to ambiguity, we revert to mahr al-mithl. The analogy with khul' and itq is rejected because in those contracts there is no original obligor for the consideration. The passage also addresses objections regarding why mahr al-mithl is not applied in all cases and why half awks is given instead of mut'ah in divorce before consummation. The reasoning is that the amount is essentially mut'ah, but since half awks typically exceeds mut'ah and the husband acknowledged it, it becomes wajib.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The standard mahr for a woman of similar status, not specified by the parties.
اوکس (awks): The lower-priced item among the two slaves.
ارفع (arfa'): The higher-priced item among the two slaves.
متعہ (mut'ah): A consolation gift given to a divorced woman before consummation when no mahr was specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what does the wife receive when the husband marries her on one of two unspecified slaves (awks and arfa')?
A) She receives her mahr al-mithl
B) She receives the lower slave (awks)
C) She receives the higher slave (arfa')
D) She receives half of the lower slave

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when mahr is ambiguous, the wife's entitlement depends on whether one takes mahr al-mithl (Abu Hanifa) or awks (Sahibayn) as the fallback.

Nikah — Marriage

Mahr of an Unspecified Animal: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on marriage with mahr of an unspecified animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr when a husband specifies an animal without description and explain the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i by analyzing the nature of marriage as mu'āwaḍa māl bi ghayr māl.

Core Idea
Marriage is not a sale; ignorance of mahr’s detail is tolerated if the genus is known.

What happens if a man marries a woman and promises a horse or donkey as mahr, but does not describe its breed, age, or condition? Is the marriage valid? What does the wife receive? This lesson examines the Hanafi position that the marriage is valid and the wife gets an average animal, and contrasts it with Imam al-Shafi'i's view that mahr al-mithl is required. At stake is the fundamental classification of marriage as a commutative contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling on unspecified animal mahr
First, grasp the Hanafi position: when the mahr is an animal of a known genus (e.g., horse) but without description, the marriage is valid and the wife receives the average (wasat) of that genus. The husband may give the animal or its price.
This applies only when the genus is specified (e.g., horse, donkey). If the mahr is simply 'an animal' (dābba) without genus, the Hanafis rule differently.
2
Contrast the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that such unspecified mahr is invalid because it suffers from ignorance (jahl), just as in a sale. He analogizes marriage to sale, requiring clarity of the exchange object.
The Shafi'i ruling: mahr al-mithl is due in all cases of unspecified animal mahr.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response distinguishing marriage from sale
Hanafis respond that marriage is not a pure sale (mu'āwaḍa māl bi ghayr māl). The consideration is not a tradeable commodity, so a degree of ignorance is tolerated. They analogize to diya (blood-money) and iqrār (admissions), where unspecified obligations are valid.
The key: the genus must be known so that the average (wasat) can be determined; total ignorance of genus invalidates the specification.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi, the wife receives an animal of average quality; under Shafi'i, she receives mahr al-mithl (monetary value based on her family status).
This affects how the husband fulfills his obligation.
5
Evaluate the strength of each position
Consider the underlying principle: does the tolerance of ignorance in marriage serve the purpose of facilitating marriage contracts? The Hanafi view prioritizes validity over perfect specification, while Shafi'i prioritizes certainty of the exchange.
No explicit tarjih is given in this passage; it presents the Hanafi position as the relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک حیوان مہر مقرر کیا اور اس کے اوصاف بیان نہیں کئے تو درمیانہ حیوان لازم ہے، شوہر کو حیوان اور اس کی قیمت دینے میں اختیار ہے
واذاتزوجها على حيوان غير موصوف صحت التسمية ولها الوسط منه والزوج مخير ان شاء اعطاها ذلك وان شاء اعطا ها قیمته قال معنى هذه المسألة ان يسمى جنس الحيوان دون الوصف بان يتزوجها على فرس او حمار اما اذالم يسم الجنس بان يتزوجها على دابة لاتجوز التسمية و يجب مهر المثل وقال الشافعي يجب مهر المثل فى الوجهين جميعا لان عنده مالا يصلح ثمنافى البيع لا يصلح مسمى اذ كل واحد منهما معاوضة ولنا انه معاوضة مال بغير مال فجعلناه التزام المال ابتداء حتى لا يفسد باصل الجهالة كالدية والاقارير و شرطنا ان يكون المسمى مالا وسطه معلوم رعاية للجانبين وذلك عندا علام الجنس لانه يشتمل على الجيد والردى والوسط ذوحظ منهما بخلاف جهالة الجنس لانه لا واسطة لاختلاف معانى
And if he marries her on an unspecified animal, the specification is valid and she gets the middlemost of it, and the husband has the choice if he wishes to give her that or if he wishes to give her its price. He said: The meaning of this issue is that he specifies the genus of animal without description, such as marrying her on a horse or a donkey. But if he does not specify the genus, such as marrying her on an animal (dābba), then the specification is not valid and mahr al-mithl is due. Al-Shafi'i said: Mahr al-mithl is due in both cases because according to him what is not suitable as a price in sale is not suitable as a specified mahr, since each is a commutative contract. And our proof is that it is a exchange of property for non-property (i.e., the benefit of the vulva), so we treat it as an undertaking of property initially, so it is not invalidated by sheer ignorance, like blood-money (diya) and admissions (iqrārāt). And we stipulated that the specified item must be property whose middlemost is known, in consideration of both parties. And that is when the genus is known because it includes good, bad, and middle, so the middle is considered from them, unlike ignorance of the genus because there is no intermediate due to differing meanings.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on mahr when a man marries a woman on an animal (like a horse or donkey) without specifying its description (e.g. age, breed, condition). According to the Hanafi school, the marriage contract is valid and the mahr specification is valid (sahīḥ) because the genus is known. The wife is entitled to the middle (wasat) of that type. The husband has the option to give her the actual animal of average quality or to give her its monetary value (price). The author (al-Marghinani) explains that this applies when the genus is specified (e.g., horse or donkey). If the genus is not specified (e.g., just 'an animal' which is ambiguous), then the mahr specification is invalid and mahr al-mithl is wajib. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees and holds that even with genus specification, the mahr al-mithl is due because an unspecified animal is not suitable as a price in a sale contract, and marriage is a commutative contract (mu'āwaḍa) similar to sale. The Hanafi response is that marriage is an exchange of property (mahr) for a non-property (the benefit of the vulva, which is not a commodity). Therefore, we treat it as an initial undertaking of property (iltizām al-māl ibtidā'an), not as a sale. Thus, ignorance (jahāla) does not invalidate it entirely, as opposed to sale. The Hanafis draw analogy with diya (blood-money) and iqrār (admissions of debt) where a degree of ignorance is tolerated. However, they require that the specified item be property whose average (wasat) is known, which is possible when the genus is known because it includes good, bad, and average types. If the genus is unknown, there is no average to refer to, so the specification is invalid.

Key Terms
وسط (wasat): The middlemost or average quality of a genus (e.g., a horse of average value and condition).
دابة (dābba): A generic term for a riding animal; here it refers to an unspecified animal without genus specification.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr equivalent to that given to women of similar status in her family; determined by social and market factors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man marries a woman on a mahr of 'a horse' without describing its breed or age, what is the status of the marriage and mahr?
A) The marriage is invalid because the mahr is not specified.
B) The mahr is invalid and mahr al-mithl is due.
C) The mahr is valid and the wife gets an average horse; the husband may give the horse or its price.
D) The wife gets the best horse the husband owns.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, mahr can be valid even without full description as long as the genus is known; the wife gets the average, and ignorance of detail does not invalidate the marriage.

Dispute on Mahr When Specified as One of Two Unnamed Slaves: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute with qiyas analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on mahr when specified as one of two unnamed slaves, explain the qiyas argument and its rebuttal, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf for pre- and post-consummation scenarios.

Core Idea
When mahr is ambiguous, the original obligation (mahr al-mithl) prevails unless the parties' consent intervenes.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of specifying mahr as one of two unnamed slaves. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that such specification is invalid due to ignorance (jihalah), reverting to mahr al-mithl, while the Sahibayn argue that the lesser slave is due by analogy to similar cases in khul' and emancipation. We will follow the proof structure of each side and see how the ruling differs before and after consummation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
The core legal question: When a husband specifies mahr as 'this slave or this slave' without naming which, is the specification valid? Abu Hanifa says no, mahr al-mithl is due; Sahibayn say yes, the lesser slave is due.
The nikah itself remains valid; only the mahr is disputed.
2
Follow the Sahibayn's qiyas argument
The Sahibayn draw an analogy (qiyas) to two cases: (1) khul' where a husband says 'I divorce you for this slave or this slave' and (2) emancipation where a master says 'I free you for this slave or this slave'. In both, the lesser slave is obligated. The 'illa' (effective cause) is the uncertainty between two specified items where the lesser is determinable.
They use tahqiq al-manat to identify the 'illa as the ability to determine the lesser.
3
Analyze Imam Abu Hanifa's rebuttal
Imam Abu Hanifa rejects the analogy as qiyas ma'a al-fariq (analogy with a difference). He argues that mahr has an original obligation (mahr al-mithl) in the contract, whereas in khul' and emancipation there is no such original obligation. Therefore, the two cases are fundamentally different.
The 'fariq' is the presence of an original obligation in mahr, which is absent in khul' and itq.
4
Examine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The dispute leads to different outcomes. After consummation: Abu Hanifa says mahr al-mithl is due; Sahibayn say the lesser slave is due. Before consummation: Abu Hanifa says mahr al-mithl is due (or mut'ah if no mahr specified?); Sahibayn say half the lesser slave is due. The passage clarifies that if mahr al-mithl is higher than the superior slave, the woman accepts less; if it is lower than the lesser, the husband agrees to more.
This shows the nuanced application of principles of consent and mut'ah.
5
Review the objections and responses
The passage addresses two objections. First, why does Abu Hanifa not always enforce mahr al-mithl? Answer: due to the parties' consent. Second, why is half the lesser slave ordered instead of mut'ah in case of divorce before consummation? Answer: half the lesser slave is considered mut'ah and is generally greater than a typical mut'ah; if mut'ah would be greater, mut'ah itself is given.
This highlights the flexibility of Hanafi fiqh in balancing original obligations with practical consent.

متعہ واجب کر دیا گیا۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر متعہ نصف اوکس سے زیادہ مالیت کا ہے تو نصف اوکس واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ بلکہ متعہ کا حکم کریں گے۔ واللہ اعلم
Now, the summary of the Sahibayn's argument is that recourse to mahr al-mithl is only possible when it is impossible to make the specified mahr obligatory. Here, it is possible to make the lesser of the two slaves obligatory because the lesser slave is determined in terms of the lower value and the lower is specific. Therefore, we will make that specific one obligatory. This is like a man saying to his wife, 'I have divorced you by khul' for this slave or this slave,' or a master saying to his slave, 'I have set you free for this slave or this slave.' In both those cases, the lesser is specific. So in the mahr case too, the lesser slave will be specific. Imam Abu Hanifa's argument is that the original obligation is mahr al-mithl, and deviation from the specified mahr occurs at the time of valid specification. Here, due to hesitation and doubt between the two slaves, ignorance (jihalah) arises. Due to this ignorance, the specification becomes invalid, so the specified mahr is not obligatory. As for khul' and emancipation, analogy to them is not valid because in those cases there is no original obligation for consideration. Therefore, this analogy is invalid due to a difference. 'Ala an mahr al-mithl' is an answer to an objection. The objection is: When mahr al-mithl is the original in all three states, then mahr al-mithl should be obligatory, whether it is less than the lesser slave, more than the superior, or between the two. Yet Imam Abu Hanifa does not hold this. The answer: The ruling is that, but when mahr al-mithl exceeds the superior, the woman agrees to reduce her mahr al-mithl. And if mahr al-mithl is less than the lesser slave, the husband agrees to increase beyond mahr al-mithl. So we act on the consent of both. 'Wa al-wajib fi al-talaq' is an answer to an objection. The objection is: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when the specification is invalid, in case of divorce before consummation, mut'ah should be obligatory. Why is half of the lesser slave made obligatory? The answer: The obligation of half the lesser slave is by way of mut'ah, so there is no objection. But the objection remains. Because we say: Just as in case of divorce before consummation with invalid specification, mahr al-mithl is obligatory, similarly mut'ah should be obligatory because just as after consummation mahr al-mithl is the original obligation, before consummation mut'ah is the original obligation. The answer: Mut'ah should indeed be obligatory, but since generally half the lesser slave is of greater value than mut'ah, and the husband has already acknowledged this increase, half the lesser slave is made obligatory. This is why if mut'ah is of greater value than half the lesser slave, half the lesser slave is not obligatory; rather, mut'ah will be decreed. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the mahr when a husband specifies one of two unnamed slaves as mahr, e.g., 'I marry you for this slave or this slave.' The Sahibayn hold that the specification is valid and the husband must give the lesser of the two slaves, drawing qiyas to similar cases in khul' and emancipation where the lesser is determined. Imam Abu Hanifa argues that the specification is invalid due to ignorance (jihalah) because there is uncertainty between the two, so the specified mahr fails and mahr al-mithl (the proper dowry) becomes obligatory. The passage then addresses an objection: if mahr al-mithl is the original obligation in all cases, why does Abu Hanifa not always require it? The response is that the parties' consent intervenes: if mahr al-mithl is higher than the superior slave, the woman accepts less; if it is lower than the lesser, the husband agrees to more. Next, the issue of divorce before consummation: if the specification is invalid, mut'ah (a gift of consolation) is normally obligatory. Why is half the lesser slave ordered? The answer is that half the lesser slave is considered mut'ah in this context, and because it is usually greater than a typical mut'ah and the husband has acknowledged it, it stands. However, if mut'ah would be greater, mut'ah itself is given instead. This shows the nuanced application of the principles of mahr and mut'ah in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dowry for a woman of her status, determined by the dowry of her paternal female relatives.
اوکس (awkas): The lesser of two things; here, the cheaper or lower-value slave.
متاع (mut'ah): A gift given to a divorced woman for consolation, especially when no mahr was specified or before consummation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn in this passage, what mahr is due when a husband says 'I marry you for this slave or this slave' without specifying which, and consummation occurs?
A) Mahr al-mithl
B) The lesser of the two slaves
C) The greater of the two slaves
D) Half of the lesser slave

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa invalidates ambiguous mahr specification due to jihalah and requires mahr al-mithl, while the Sahibayn uphold the specification and require the lesser slave, based on qiyas to khul' and emancipation.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Mahr Specified as an Unspecified Animal: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Ruling on mahr as an animal without quality description, with Shafi'i opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on mahr specified as an undescribed animal, identify the Shafi'i objection, and explain the Hanafi response using the distinction between marriage and sale.

Core Idea
Marriage tolerates initial ignorance; mahr with a known genus is valid, average due.

When a mahr is specified as an animal without describing its quality, a critical disagreement arises between Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The Hanafi school holds the specification valid, requiring only an average animal, while Shafi'is invalidate it entirely. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind each position and the key principles governing mahr in commutative contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its conditions
First, articulate the Hanafi ruling: if the genus (e.g., horse) is mentioned, the specification is valid; the wife gets the average; the husband may give the animal or its value. Note the condition that the genus must be known.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection and its dalil
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that mahr al-mithl is due in all such cases because an unknown animal cannot be a valid price in a commutative contract, analogizing to sale.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response: qiyas to diyah/iqrar
The Hanafis rebut by distinguishing marriage from sale: marriage is a compensation of property without property, akin to diyah and iqrar where initial ignorance is tolerated.
4
Examine the distinction between marriage and sale
Key distinction: sale is based on strictness (mudaayaqah) requiring full knowledge; marriage is based on tolerance (musamahah). The average is determinable by value, so the risk is minimal.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
Practical consequence: Hanafis allow a valid mahr with average animal; Shafi'is require mahr al-mithl. The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

ہو مہر
A mahr was specified as an animal, and its qualities were not described; then the average animal is obligatory, and the husband has the choice to give the animal or its value. 'And when he marries her for an animal that is not described, the specification is valid, and she is entitled to the average of it, and the husband has the choice: if he wishes, he gives her that, and if he wishes, he gives her its value.' He said: The meaning of this case is that the genus of the animal is mentioned without the description, such as marrying her for a horse or a donkey. But if he does not mention the genus, such as marrying her for an animal (dabbah), the specification is not valid, and mahr al-mithl is obligatory. Al-Shafi'i said: Mahr al-mithl is obligatory in both cases because in his view what is not valid as a price in sale is not valid as a specified mahr, since each is a commutative contract. Our evidence is that it is a compensation of property without property, so we have considered it as an initial assumption of property so that it is not invalidated by original ignorance, like diyah and acknowledgments. And we have conditioned that the specified item be property whose average is known, for the sake of both parties. This condition is fulfilled when the genus is known, because the genus includes good, bad, and average, and the average is taken from both. Unlike ignorance of the genus, for there is no average due to the different meanings of genera. And unlike sale, for it is based on strictness and bargaining, while marriage is based on tolerance. And the husband has choice because the average is not known except by value; thus value becomes the original in terms of payment, and the animal is the original in terms of specification, so he may choose between them. Translation: And when a man marries a woman for an animal whose quality is not described, the specification is valid, and she is entitled to the average of that animal, and the husband has the choice to give her this average or to give her its value. The author (Marghinani) said: The meaning of this case is that the genus of the animal was mentioned, but not the description, such as marrying her for a horse or a donkey. However, if the genus is not mentioned, e.g., marrying her for an animal (dabbah), then the specification is not valid, and mahr al-mithl is obligatory. Imam al-Shafi'i said that mahr al-mithl is obligatory in both cases, because in his view what cannot serve as a price in sale cannot serve as a specified mahr, since both are commutative contracts. Our (Hanafi) evidence is that marriage is a compensation of property without property; thus we treat it as an initial obligation of property, so it is not invalidated by original ignorance, like diyah and acknowledgments. We have conditioned that the specified item be property whose middle is known, for the sake of both parties, and this condition is met when the genus is known, because the genus includes good, bad, and middle, and the middle partakes of both. Unlike ignorance of the genus, for there is no middle due to the different meanings of genera. And unlike sale, because sale is based on strictness and bargaining, while marriage is based on tolerance. And the husband has choice because the middle is not known except by value; thus value becomes the original in terms of payment, and the animal is the original in terms of specification, so he may choose between them. Explanation of the case: A man married a woman and made the mahr an animal whose quality was not described. According to us (Hanafis), the specification is valid, and the husband must give her a medium-grade animal, and he also has the option to give her the value of a medium animal. The author of Hidayah says that al-Quduri's intended meaning is that the genus of the animal was mentioned, but not the quality (whether the horse is low-grade, high-grade, or medium). However, if the genus itself is not mentioned, e.g., marrying for an animal (dabbah), then the specification is invalid and mahr al-mithl is due. In the Hidayah's phrase, 'jins al-hayawan' (genus of animal) actually means the type (naw'), because 'horse' and 'donkey' are types, not genera. The response from the Hidayah is that the author uses 'jins' in the juristic sense, which includes types. For example, 'human' is a type in non-juristic terminology but a genus in juristic terms. Anyway, the meaning of 'type of animal' is that there is a single meaning shared by many individuals, and the main objective is one for all. Imam al-Shafi'i said that in both cases, whether the genus is mentioned or not, mahr al-mithl is obligatory. His evidence is that what cannot be a price in a sale contract cannot be a specified mahr in marriage, because both are commutative contracts. And an unknown (i.e., undescribed) animal cannot be a price in sale, so it cannot be a specified mahr in marriage. The Hanafi evidence is that marriage is a compensation of property without property, so we treat marriage as an initial obligation of property (iltizam al-mal ibtida'an), meaning the husband takes it upon himself without...
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school on specifying mahr as an animal without describing its quality. According to the Hanafis, if the genus (such as horse or donkey) is mentioned, the specification is valid, and the wife is entitled to an average-quality animal of that type. The husband has the option to give either that average animal or its cash value. However, if the genus itself is not specified (e.g., only 'an animal' is said), the specification is invalid and mahr al-mithl becomes due. The passage then introduces the Shafi'i view: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that in both cases (whether genus is mentioned or not), the specification is invalid and mahr al-mithl is due, because an animal whose quality is unknown cannot serve as a valid price in a sale contract, and marriage is a commutative contract like sale. The Hanafis respond by distinguishing marriage from sale: marriage is a compensation of property without property (i.e., it involves a person, not just property), so they treat it as an initial obligation of property, similar to diyah (blood money) and acknowledgments (iqrar). They impose a condition that the specified item must be property whose average is known; this condition is met when the genus is known because the genus includes good, bad, and average, and the average is a recognizable midpoint. In sale, strictness demands full knowledge, but marriage is based on tolerance. The husband's choice to give value is because the average price is determined by valuation, so value becomes the true measure; the animal is the basis of specification, so he may choose. The commentary then clarifies that in the Hidayah, 'genus of animal' actually means 'type' in common parlance, but in juristic terminology, it is considered a genus. This shows the meticulousness of Hanafi legal reasoning in balancing contractual freedom and the need for clarity in mahr obligations.

Key Terms
جنس (jins): In this context, jins means the general category of the animal, such as horse or donkey, as opposed to a specific description of quality.
وسط (wast): The average or middle quality of the animal, which is obligatory when no quality is specified.
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The standard dowry for a woman of similar status, which becomes obligatory when the specified mahr is invalid.

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis in this passage, when a man marries a woman and specifies mahr as 'a horse' without describing its quality, what does the husband owe?
A) The best horse he owns
B) An average horse, or its value
C) Mahr al-mithl
D) Nothing, the marriage is invalid

Key Takeaway
Mahr specified with a known genus but unknown quality is valid in Hanafi fiqh; the average is due, and the husband may choose the animal or its value.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
12 min
Marriage with Unspecified Animal as Dower: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute over validity of unspecified animal as dower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on an unspecified animal as dower, explain the Hanafi proof based on leniency, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Ignorance of the dower's description does not invalidate marriage—only ignorance of the genus does, because marriage is built on leniency.

In this lesson, we examine a key dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the validity of specifying an animal without description as dower in marriage. The Hanafi school permits it, while the Shafi'i school insists on mahr al-mithl. The passage from Sharh al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi proof and rebuts the Shafi'i analogy to sale. Understanding this dispute reveals the Hanafi principle that marriage tolerates slight ignorance due to its lenient nature.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and scope
First, identify the Hanafi rule: if the genus (e.g., horse) is mentioned but not its quality, the dower is valid and the wife gets a medium-grade animal; if the genus itself is unknown, the dower is invalid. This scope is crucial.
The text gives examples: 'horse' or 'donkey' (genus known) vs. 'riding beast' (genus unknown).
2
Explain the Shafi'i position and their proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that mahr al-mithl is wajib in both cases because an unspecified animal cannot be a price (thaman) in sale, and marriage is analogous to sale as a commutative contract.
Shafi'i uses qiyas: sale and marriage are both mu'awada (commutative).
3
Trace the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi school distinguishes marriage from sale. Marriage is based on musamaha (leniency) and is initially a commitment of wealth (iltizam al-mal), which tolerates slight ignorance. Proofs include diyah and iqrar where ignorance is tolerated.
The text emphasizes that marriage is not built on strictness like sale.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Hanafi, the husband gives medium-grade animal or its value; under Shafi'i, only mahr al-mithl is due.
This difference affects what the wife may claim.
5
Understand the husband's option
The husband may give the medium-grade animal or its value because the medium is known only by value; thus value is primary in fulfillment, while the specific item is primary in naming.
This option arises from the dual nature of the dower: it is both a named item and a financial obligation.

اور عبد اصل ہے تسمیہ کیونکہ تسمیہ اس پر واقع ہوا ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ ایک اعتبار سے قیمت اصل ہے اور ایک اعتبار سے مسمیٰ اصل ہے۔ لہذا شو ہر کو اختیار ہو گا جو چاہے دے دے۔ ہدایہ کے اس نسخہ میں ولعبد اصل تسمیہ ہے۔ اس نسخہ کے اعتبار سے یوں کہیں گے کہ متن میں حیوان غیر موصوف کومبر بنایا تھا یہاں اس کی ایک مثال عبد کا ذکر کر دیا گیا اور بعض نسخوں میں ہے لفظ والعین اصل یہ نسخہ زیادہ واضح ہے کیونکہ اس وقت مطلب ہو گا کہ مین شی یعنی مہر سمن اصل ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
The passage begins with the Arabic text: '...and contrary to sale because it is based on strictness and haggling, while marriage is based on leniency. And he chooses because the middle is only known by value, so value becomes primary in fulfillment and the specific item is primary in naming, so he chooses between them.' Translation: When a man marries a woman on an animal whose description is not given, the naming (tasmiyah) is valid, and the wife gets the medium grade of that animal. The husband has the option to give the medium or its value. Quduri said this means the genus (jins) was mentioned but not the description. If the genus is not mentioned, e.g., marrying on a riding beast, the tasmiyah is invalid and mahr al-mithl is wajib. Imam Shafi'i said mahr al-mithl in both cases because, according to him, anything that can be a price (thaman) in sale can be a named dower in marriage, as both are commutative contracts. Our Hanafi proof: Marriage is a commutative contract without immediate property (mu'awada ka al-bighayr al-mal). Thus we consider marriage as a commitment of wealth (iltizam al-mal) from the start, so it should not be invalidated by original ignorance (jahl al-asl), like diyah (blood money) and iqrar (acknowledgment). We imposed the condition that the named property must have a known middle value, considering both parties. This condition is met when the genus is known, because a genus includes good, bad, and medium, and the medium partakes of both. Contrary to ignorance of genus, because there is no medium across different genera. And contrary to sale, because it is based on strictness, while marriage is based on leniency. The husband has the option because the medium is only known by value; thus value is primary in fulfillment, and the specific item (or slave) is primary in naming. So the husband chooses between them. Explanation: A man marries a woman and makes an animal whose description is not given as the dower. According to us, tasmiyah is valid. The husband must give the medium-grade animal, and he also has the option to give its value. The author of Hidayah says that Quduri meant that the genus of the animal was mentioned, but not the description. If the genus itself is not mentioned, e.g., 'riding beast', the tasmiyah is invalid and mahr al-mithl is wajib. By 'genus' in Hidayah, the type (naw') is meant, because examples like horse and donkey are types, not genera. The response: In Hidayah, 'genus' is used in the jurists' terminology. Imam Shafi'i holds mahr al-mithl in both cases. His proof: Whatever cannot be a price in sale cannot be a named dower in marriage. An unknown animal cannot be a price in sale, so it cannot be a named dower in marriage. Marriage is analogous to sale because both are commutative contracts. Our Hanafi proof: Marriage is a commutative contract without immediate property. We treat it as an initial commitment of wealth, which is not invalidated by original ignorance, like diyah (where Shariah prescribed 100 unspecified camels) and iqrar (acknowledgment of something is valid even if unknown). We require that the named property have a known middle value to consider both spouses. This is only possible when the genus (type) is specified, because a genus includes good, bad, and medium, and the medium relates to both. Summary: Marriage is initially a commitment of wealth and ultimately a commutative exchange. The commitment aspect means it is not invalidated by original ignorance, like iqrar. The commutative aspect means it does not tolerate absolute ignorance – neither gross (fahish) nor slight (yasir). So we reconcile: marriage does not tolerate gross ignorance (jahl al-asl) but tolerates slight ignorance (jahl al-yasir). Thus, specifying the genus is essential, but specifying the description is not. Specifying the genus is also necessary because if the genus is unknown, the middle cannot be known, as there is no middle across different genera. A story: someone asked 'which is greater, intellect or buffalo?' The answer: the question itself is wrong because greatness only exists within a single genus, not across different genera. The phrase 'contrary to sale' is a response to Shafi'i's proof: Analogy to sale is invalid because sale is based on strictness while marriage is based on leniency. The phrase 'and he chooses because the middle' addresses an objection: If the medium-grade horse is the named dower, and the rule is that the named dower must be given as is if possible, why does the husband have the option to give value? Answer: The medium is only known by value; value is primary in fulfillment, while the specific item is primary in naming. Thus the husband has the option. In this edition of Hidayah, the phrase is 'wa al-'abd asl al-tasmiyah' (the specific item is the basis of naming). According to this, we say that in the text, the unspecified animal was made the named dower; here an example of a slave ('abd) is given. In some editions it is 'wa al-'ayn asl' (the specific item is the basis). This version is clearer, meaning that the named item (al-musamma) is the basis. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage from Sharh al-Hidayah presents a detailed inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i concerning the validity of specifying an unspecified animal as dower in marriage. The Hanafi position, derived from al-Quduri and expanded by al-Marghinani, holds that such a tasmiyah is valid if the genus is mentioned, even without description. The wife is entitled to the medium grade, and the husband may give the medium or its value. The Shafi'i position holds that in all cases of ignorance, only mahr al-mithl is obligatory. Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes marriage to sale, arguing that what cannot be a price (thaman) in sale due to ignorance cannot be a named dower. The Hanafi proof distinguishes marriage from sale: marriage is based on leniency (musamaha) and is initially a commitment of wealth (iltizam al-mal) that tolerates slight ignorance, as seen in diyah and iqrar. Sale, by contrast, is based on strictness (muda'yaqa). The Hanafi school thus requires only knowledge of the genus, not the description, because the genus has a middle value that can be determined. If the genus is unknown, there is no middle, and the dower is invalid. The passage addresses objections and explains the husband's option: the medium is known only by value, so value is primary in fulfillment while the specific item is primary in naming. Variant readings of the text are discussed. This is a foundational Hanafi principle in mahr rulings.

Key Terms
تسمیہ (tasmiyah): The act of specifying or naming the dower (mahr) in the marriage contract.
مہر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower, determined by the dower of women of similar status, used when the specified dower is invalid.
جہالت (jahl): Ignorance or uncertainty regarding the subject matter, which can invalidate a contract depending on its severity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man marries a woman and specifies as dower 'a horse' without describing its quality, what is the ruling?
A) The dower is invalid and mahr al-mithl is wajib.
B) The dower is valid and the wife gets a medium-grade horse; the husband may give its value instead.
C) The dower is valid only if the horse is described in detail.
D) The husband must give the best horse.

Key Takeaway
Ignorance of the dower's description is tolerated in marriage because it is built on leniency, but ignorance of the genus invalidates the dower and substitutes mahr al-mithl.

Dower Validity: Ignorance of Genus (Jahl al-Jins)
Ruling and reasoning on unspecified cloth as dower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that ignorance of genus (jahl al-jins) in the dower renders the specified dower invalid, and distinguish when the dower is valid by specifying a type within the genus.

Core Idea
A dower must specify the genus; merely saying "a cloth" is jahl al-jins and invalid.

In a marriage contract, the dower must be known to avoid uncertainty (gharar). The Hanafi school holds that if the dower is specified only by a general category like 'cloth' without describing the type, the specification is invalid because cloth encompasses many genera. This lesson explores the distinction between ignorance of genus (jahl al-jins) and tolerable ignorance of description, and how a specific type within the genus restores validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is marriage where the dower is specified as 'a cloth' (thawb) without description. The ruling: the specified dower (tasmiyah) is invalid (batil), and the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl.
2
Trace the reasoning
The text states the cause: 'this is ignorance of genus (jahl al-jins) because cloths are multiple genera.' Understand that 'thawb' is not a single genus but includes linen, silk, cotton, etc. Thus, the dower is unknown in its genus, which is unacceptable.
Jahl al-jins makes the dower invalid; jahl al-wasf (ignorance of description within a known genus) is tolerable.
3
Distinguish the valid case
If the husband specifies a type like 'Harawi' (a cloth from Herat), then the genus is known, and the dower becomes valid. The husband then has the option to give the medium quality or its value.
This is analogous to specifying 'horse' versus just 'animal'.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: with an invalid tasmiyah, mahr al-mithl is wajib; with a valid one, the specified dower is binding (with husband's option).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایسے کپڑے پر نکاح کیا جس کا وصف بیان نہیں کیا تو مہر مثل لازم ہے وان تزوجها على ثوب غير موصوف فلها مهر المثل ومعناه انه ذكر الثوب ولم يزد عليه ووجهه ان هذه جهالة الجنس لان الثياب اجناس ولوسمي جنسا بان قال هروى تصح التسمية ويخير الزوج لما بينا
If he marries her on a cloth (thawb) whose description is not given, then mahr al-mithl is compulsory. And if he marries her on an unspecified cloth, she gets mahr al-mithl. Its meaning is that he mentioned 'cloth' and did not add anything. The reasoning is that this is ignorance of genus (jahl al-jins) because cloths are multiple genera. If he specifies a genus, like saying 'Harawi', then the tasmiyah is valid and the husband has the option, as we have explained.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage from al-Hidayah presents a ruling on the validity of specifying an unspecified cloth as dower. The author states that if the husband merely says 'a cloth' without any description, the specified dower is invalid due to jahl al-jins (ignorance of the genus), because cloth is a category that encompasses many different types (ajnas). This is similar to the case of specifying an animal without mentioning its genus. Therefore, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl. However, if the husband specifies a particular type of cloth, such as Harawi (a type from Herat), then the dower becomes valid (tasmiah sahihah), and the husband has the option to give the medium quality of that type or its value, following the same rule as for the animal when the genus was known. This ruling reinforces the Hanafi principle that knowledge of the genus is essential for the validity of the specified dower, while lack of description within a known genus is tolerable due to the leniency of marriage.

Key Terms
ثوب (thawb): A cloth or garment; used as an example of an unspecified dower that falls under multiple genera.
جہالت الجنس (jahl al-jins): Ignorance or uncertainity regarding the genus of the dower, which invalidates the specified dower in marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man marries a woman and specifies as dower 'a cloth' (thawb) without further description, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The dower is valid and the wife gets a medium cloth.
B) The dower is invalid and mahr al-mithl is required because cloths are multiple genera.
C) The husband can choose any cloth.
D) The dower is valid only if the cloth is described as fine.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the specified dower is valid only when the genus (jins) is known; ignorance of genus invalidates it and mahr al-mithl becomes wajib.
