Mahr When Garment Type is Unspecified: Hanafi Ruling
Ruling on mahr when garment type/quality is unknown, with proof and inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr when the garment's type is unknown, distinguish between jahalah fahishah and jahalah khafifah, and explain why the Hanafi school uses istihsan over qiyas.

Core Idea
In nikah, ignorance of type invalidates the named mahr; ignorance of quality does not.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the Hanafi position on mahr when a garment is mentioned without specifying its type or quality. The Hanafi school distinguishes between gross ignorance (jahalah fahishah) which relates to the type (jins) and slight ignorance (jahalah khafifah) which relates to the quality (sifat). The ruling is based on the dual nature of marriage as both a property obligation and an exchange, using istihsan (juristic preference) to reject the analogy to sale. Understanding this ruling helps us appreciate the Hanafi methodology of balancing textual analogy with practical facilitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is specifying a garment as mahr. If the type is unspecified, the tassmiyah is invalid and mahr al-mithl is due; if type is specified but quality is not, the tassmiyah is valid and the husband has the option (takhyir) between average quality and price.
2
Locate the dalil
The Hanafi proof is based on the nature of nikah as both iltizam mal (property obligation) and mu'awadah (exchange). As an obligation, it tolerates slight jahalah, unlike sale which is pure exchange.
The text uses the example of diyah (blood money) where unspecified camels are accepted.
3
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes marriage to sale, requiring both type and quality to be specified. The Hanafi response uses istihsan, arguing that sale is based on strictness (diq) and marriage on leniency (samahah).
4
Apply the ruling to different types of mahr
For cloth (not dhawat al-amthal), even exaggerated description gives the husband choice because cloth is valued by price, not like. For measurable/weighable items (makilat/mawzunat), if both type and quality are specified, the husband must give the named item.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is that in the Hanafi school, a marriage contract with an unspecified quality is valid with a husband's choice, while in the Shafi'i school such a contract would require mahr al-mithl due to invalid tassmiyah.
Both schools agree the marriage itself is valid.

Source Text

کسی عوض کے مال لازم کرتا ہے اور التزام مال اصل جہالت سے بھی فاسد نہیں ہوتا ۔ جیسے دیت میں شریعت نے سو اونٹ غیر موصوف مقرر کئے ہیں اور کسی نے کسی کیلئے اقرار کر لیا کسی چیز کا تو یہ اقرار درست ہے۔ اور ہم نے یہ شرط لگائی کہ مسمی مال معلوم الوسط ہوتا کہ زوجین میں سے دونوں کی رعایت ہو سکے۔ اور سمی معلوم الوسط اسی وقت ہو سکتا ہے جبکہ جنس یعنی نوع بیان کر دی گئی ہو کیونکہ جنس یعنی نوع جید ، دی اور متوسط پر مشتمل ہوتی ہے اور متوسط کا تعلق دونوں طرف سے ہے اسلئے کہ وسط جید کے اعتبار سے ردی ہے اور ردی کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے جید ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ نکاح ابتداء تو التزام مال ہے اور انتہاء معاوضہ ہے۔ التزام مال کا تقاضا تو یہ ہے کہ اصل جہالت سے بھی نکاح فاسد نہ ہو جیسے اقرار التزام مال ہے اصل جہالت کو بھی برداشت کر لیتا ہے اور معاوضہ کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ نکاح مطلقاً جہالت کو برداشت نہ کرے نہ جہالت فاحشہ کو اور نہ جہالت میرہ کو جیسے بیچ بالکل جہالت کی متحمل نہیں ہے۔ پس ہم نے دونوں مشابہتوں کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ نکاح جہالت فاحشہ یعنی اصل جہالت کو تو برداشت نہیں کرے گا۔ البتہ جہالت بیرہ اور خفیفہ کو برداشت کر لے گا۔ اسلئے احناف نے کہا کہ بیان جنس ضروری ہے البتہ بیان وصف ضروری نہیں ہے اور بیان جنس اسلئے بھی ضروری ہے کہ اگر جنس مجہول ہے تو وسط کا علم بھی نہیں ہو سکے گا کیونکہ جنس کا وسط ہی نہیں ہوتا۔ معانی اجناس کے مختلف ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ ایک صاحب نے کسی سے پوچھا کہ عقل بڑی ہے یا بھینس، تو جواب ملا کہ سوال ہی غلط ہے کیونکہ چھوٹا بڑا تو اتحاد جنس کے وقت ہوتا ہے اختلاف جنس کی صورت میں نہیں ہوتا۔
بخلاف البیع سے امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ نکاح کو بیچ پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہے اسلئے بیع کی بنیاد ہے تنگی پر اور نکاح کی بنیاد ہے نرمی پر اور مسائلت پر۔
و انما يتخير لان الوسط سے صاحب ہدایہ نے اشکال کا جواب دیا ہے۔ اشکال یہ ہے کہ اوسط درجہ کا گھوڑایا اوسط درجہ کا گدھا مہر سمی ہے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ مہر سمی کا ادا کرنا اگر ممکن ہو تو دوسری چیز ادا نہیں کی جائے گی پھر شوہر کو یہ اختیار کیوں دیا ہے کہ وہ اوسط درجہ کا جاتور دے دے یا اس کی قیمت۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ اوسط کا علم قیمت سے ہوگا کیونکہ جس کی قیمت بہت زیادہ ہے وہ جید ہے اور جس کی قیمت بہت کم ہے وہ ردی ہے اور جس کی نہ زیادہ ہے اور نہ کم وہ وسط ہے۔ پس ادا کے حق میں قیمت اصل ہوگی اور عبد اصل ہے تسمیہ کیونکہ تسمیہ اس پر واقع ہوا ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ ایک اعتبار سے قیمت اصل ہے اور ایک اعتبار سے مسمیٰ اصل ہے۔ لہذا شو ہر کو اختیار ہو گا جو چاہے دے دے۔
ہدایہ کے اس نسخہ میں ولعبد اصل تسمیہ ہے۔ اس نسخہ کے اعتبار سے یوں کہیں گے کہ متن میں حیوان غیر موصوف کومبر بنایا تھا یہاں اس کی ایک مثال عبد کا ذکر کر دیا گیا اور بعض نسخوں میں ہے لفظ والعین اصل یہ نسخہ زیادہ واضح ہے کیونکہ اس وقت مطلب ہو گا کہ مین شی یعنی مہر سمن اصل ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
ایسے کپڑے پر نکاح کیا جس کا وصف بیان نہیں کیا تو مہر مثل لازم ہے
وان تزوجها على ثوب غير موصوف فلها مهر المثل ومعناه انه ذكر الثوب ولم يزيد عليه ووجهه ان هذه جهالة الجنس لان الثياب اجناس ولوسمي جنسا بان قال هروى تصح التسمية ويخير الزوج لما بينا
وكذا اذا بالغ فى وصف الثوب فى ظاهر الروية لانها ليست من ذوات الامثال وكذا اداسمى مكيلا اوموزوناو سمی جنسه دون صفته وان سمی جنسه و صفته لا يخيرلان الموصوف منها يثبت في الذمة ثبوتا صحيحا
ترجمہ اور اگر نکاح کیا عورت سے ایسے کپڑے پر جس کا وصف بیان نہیں کیا گیا تو عورت کیلئے مہر مثل ہے اور مراد اس کی یہ ہے کہ ثوب کا ذکر تو کیا اور اس پر اضافہ نہیں کیا اور وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ یہ جہالت جنس ہے۔ کیونکہ کپڑے مختلف اجناس کے ہوتے ہیں اور اگر جنس بیان کی بایں طور کہ کہا ہروی ہے تو تسمیہ صحیح ہے اور شوہر کو اختیار دیا جائے گا اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ۔ اور ایسے ہی جب مبالغہ کیا کپڑے کے وصف میں ظاہر الروایۃ میں ۔ کیونکہ کپڑا ذوات الامثال میں سے نہیں ہے اور ایسے ہی جب ذکر کیا ملیلی یا موزونی چیز کا اور اس کی جنس بیان کی نہ کہ صفت اور اگر ذکر کیا اس کی جنس اور صفت کو تو شوہر کو اختیار نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ اسلئے کہ موصوف ان میں سے ثابت ہوتا ہے ذمہ میں ثبوت صحیح کے طور پر ۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نکاح میں کپڑے کو مہر بنایا لیکن کپڑے کا وصف ذکر نہیں کیا مثلاً یہ تو کہہ دیا کہ مہر میں کپڑا دوں گا۔ لیکن اس کی نوع بیان نہیں کی تو ایسی صورت میں ائمہ اربعہ کے نزدیک مہر مثل واجب ہوگا۔ وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں نوع مجہول ہے اسلئے کہ کپڑوں کی بہت سی انواع ہیں۔ مثلاً روئی کا، کستان کا ، ریشم کا۔ پس جہالت مسمی کی وجہ سے مہر مثل واجب ہوگا۔ اور اگر کپڑے کی نوع بیان کر دی مثلاً کہا کہ وہ ہر وی سوتی تھان کا ہوگا تو اب تسمیہ صحیح ہے اور شوہر کو قیمت اور اوسط درجہ کے ہروی کپڑے کے درمیان اختیار ہو گا۔ دلیل ماقبل میں گذر چکی اور اگر کپڑے کا وصف بیان کرنے میں مبالغہ کیا یعنی نوع بھی بیان کی گئی اور اس کا طول، عرض، موٹائی اور سانچہ بھی متعین کر دیا گیا تو اس صورت میں بھی شوہر کو وسط ثوب اور اس کی قیمت کے درمیان اختیار ہوگا۔ کیونکہ کپڑ اذوات الامثال میں سے نہیں ہے بلکہ ذوات القیم میں سے ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ کپڑا اگر ہلاک ہو گیا تو مضمون بالقیمہ ہو گا مضمون بالمثل نہیں ۔ اور اگر مہر کسی مکیلی چیز کو بنایا یا موزونی چیز کو اور اس کی نوع بیان کردی مثلاً ایک کر گندم یا ایک من زعفران کو مہر بنایا لیکن اس کی صفت بیان نہیں کی گئی تو اب بھی شوہر کو اوسط درجہ کے سمی اور اس کی قیمت کے درمیان اختیار ہوگا۔ اور اگر نوع اور وصف دونوں بیان کر دیئے گئے تو اب شوہر پر مسمی واجب ہو گا۔ قیمت اور مسمی کے درمیان اختیار نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ مکیلات اور موزونات میں سے جس کا وصف بیان کر دیا گیا تو وہ ذمہ میں علی الاطلاق ثابت ہوتی ہے بیع سلم میں بھی اور اس کے علاوہ میں بھی اس کے برخلاف ثوب موصوف کہ وہ صرف بیع سلم میں ذمہ میں خلاف قیاس ثابت ہوتا ہے۔
It makes a property obligation, and the obligation of property is not invalidated even by original ignorance. Just as in diyah, the Shariah appointed one hundred un-described camels, and if anyone acknowledges something for someone, that acknowledgment is valid. And we set the condition that the named property (musamma) is of known middle status so that both spouses can be considered. And the named middle is only possible when the type (jins) is stated, because the type includes good, bad, and middle, and the middle is related to both sides, because the middle is bad in relation to good and good in relation to bad. The conclusion is that marriage is initially an obligation of property and ultimately an exchange. The requirement of property obligation is that even original ignorance does not invalidate marriage, like acknowledgment which bears original ignorance, and the requirement of exchange is that marriage absolutely does not bear ignorance—neither gross ignorance nor mild ignorance—like sale which does not bear ignorance at all. So we, considering both similarities, said that marriage will not bear gross ignorance, i.e., original ignorance, but it will bear mild and slight ignorance. Therefore the Hanafis said that stating the type is necessary, but stating the quality is not necessary. And stating the type is also necessary because if the type is unknown, knowledge of the middle is not possible, because a type has no middle due to the differences in meanings of types. A person asked someone: "Is intelligence bigger or a buffalo?" The answer was: "The question itself is wrong, because bigger and smaller only occur when there is unity of type, not in case of difference of types."
Contrary to sale (bay') is the refutation of Imam Shafi'i's proof. The summary of this refutation is that it is not correct to analogize marriage to sale, because sale is based on strictness and marriage is based on leniency and facilitation.
"And he has choice because the middle"—the author of Hidayah gave an answer to an objection. The objection is: a middle grade horse or a middle grade donkey is named as mahr, and the rule is that if the named mahr can be given, another thing is not given. Then why is the husband given the choice to give the middle quality or its price? The answer is that knowledge of the middle will be through the price, because that which is very high in price is good, that which is very low is bad, and that which is neither high nor low is middle. So in terms of payment, price is the origin, and the named item is the origin of the naming because the naming occurred on it. The conclusion is that in one aspect price is the origin, and in another aspect the named is the origin. Therefore the husband has a choice to give whichever he wishes.
In this copy of Hidayah, the wording is "and the servant is the origin of the naming" (wa al-abd asl al-tasmiyah). According to this copy, they will say: in the text, the un-described animal was made as an example, here one example of a servant is mentioned. In some copies, the phrase is "wa al-ayn asl" (and the thing itself is the origin). This copy is clearer because then the meaning is that the named thing (mu'ayyan shay') is the origin of the dower. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Ruling on marriage with an un-described garment: If one marries her for an un-described garment, she gets mahr al-mithl. Its meaning is that he mentioned the garment and did not add to it. The reason is that this is ignorance of the type, because garments are of different types. If he specified the type by saying, for example, "Harawi" (a type of cloth), the naming is valid and the husband has a choice as we have explained.
Similarly, if he exaggerated in describing the garment in the apparent narration, because it is not among things with like equivalents. Also if he named a measurable or weighable item and specified its type without its quality. And if he specified its type and quality, he does not have a choice, because the described item from among these is established in the dhimma (liability) with a valid establishment.
Translation: And if a man marries a woman on an un-described garment, she is entitled to mahr al-mithl. Its meaning is that he mentioned the garment and did not add to it. The reason is that this is ignorance of the type, because garments are of different types. And if he stated the type by saying, for example, "Harawi," the naming is valid and the husband will be given a choice due to the reason we have mentioned. Similarly, when he exaggerated in describing the garment in the apparent narration, because a garment is not among things with like equivalents. And similarly, when he mentioned a measurable or weighable item and specified its type but not its quality. And if he specified its type and quality, the husband will not be given a choice because the described item from among these is established in the dhimma with a valid establishment.
Explanation: The issue is that if one makes a garment as mahr in marriage but does not mention its description, e.g., he says "I will give a garment as mahr" but does not specify its type, in such a case according to the four imams, mahr al-mithl is obligatory. The reason is that the type is unknown because there are many types of garments, e.g., cotton, silk, etc. So due to ignorance of the named item, mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. If he did specify the type, e.g., said "it will be of Harawi cotton cloth," then the naming is valid and the husband has a choice between the price and the average grade Harawi garment. The proof has passed earlier. If he exaggerated in describing the garment, i.e., stated the type and also specified its length, width, thickness, and pattern, even then the husband has a choice between the middle garment and its price, because a garment is not among things with like equivalents but among things with value. This is why if the garment is destroyed, it is guaranteed by value (madhmun bi al-qimah), not by like. If the mahr is made a measurable or weighable item and its type is specified, e.g., one khirr (a measure) of wheat or one mann (a weight) of saffron, but its quality is not specified, then also the husband has a choice between the average-grade named item and its price. If both type and quality are specified, then the husband is obliged to give the named item, and he has no choice between price and the named item, because measurable and weighable items whose quality is described are established in the dhimma absolutely, both in salam sale and otherwise, unlike a described garment which is established in the dhimma only in salam sale as an exception to analogy.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (hukm + dalil) from the Hanafi school regarding the validity of mahr (dower) when the type (jins) or quality (sifat) is unspecified. The author, Al-Marghinani in Hidayah, establishes a nuanced position that distinguishes marriage (nikah) from sale (bay'), rejecting the analogy proposed by Imam al-Shafi'i. The core principle is that marriage partakes of both property obligation (iltizam mal) and exchange (mu'awadah). As an obligation, it tolerates some ignorance (jahalah), like an acknowledgment (iqrar) of an unspecified debt. As an exchange, it cannot tolerate gross ignorance (jahalah fahishah), i.e., ignorance of the type (jins). Therefore, specifying the type is necessary for a valid tassmiyah (naming of mahr), but specifying the quality (sifat) is not required. If only the type is mentioned, the husband has the option (takhyir) to give either the average quality (wasat) of that type or its market value. If both type and quality are specified, the husband must give the exact described item and has no option. For items like cloth (which are not dhawat al-amthal, things with exact like equivalents), even exaggerated description does not remove the husband's choice because the obligation is ultimately in value. For measurable (makilat) and weighable (mawzunat) items, the ruling is different: if type and quality are specified, the husband must give the exact item, as they can be established in the dhimma (liability) absolutely, unlike cloth which only in salam sale. The passage also refutes Imam Shafi'i's qiyas to sale, arguing that sale is based on strictness (diq) while marriage is based on leniency (samahah) and facilitation (musa'alah). This is a classic Hanafi usul al-fiqh argument using istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah, as the ruling is from the matn of Hidayah (a core text) and the commentary is from Ashraf al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
جہالت (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty in the subject matter of a contract. Here classified as jahalah fahishah (gross - ignorance of type) and jahalah khafifah (slight - ignorance of quality).
مہر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower equivalent to that which is customary for women of similar status in the family.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi marriage contract, the husband says 'I give you this garment as mahr' without specifying its type (cotton, silk, etc.). What is the ruling on the mahr?
A) The marriage is invalid because mahr is unspecified.
B) The husband must give the average quality of that garment's type.
C) The wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl because the type is unknown.
D) The husband can choose any garment arbitrarily.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi nikah, only ignorance of the type of mahr invalidates the naming; ignorance of quality gives the husband a choice, based on the distinction between marriage and sale.

Ruling on Marriage with Wine or Pork as Mahr
Ruling on validity of marriage when mahr is wine or pork for a Muslim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a marriage where the mahr is wine or pork, and explain why the marriage remains valid while the condition is void, using the distinction between marriage and sale.

Core Idea
A void condition in marriage does not invalidate the contract; only the condition is nullified, and mahr al-mithl becomes due.

In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario: a Muslim man marries a woman and stipulates that her mahr (dower) is wine or pork—items that are not property (mal) for a Muslim. The Hanafi school rules that the marriage itself is valid, but the condition is void (fasid), and the wife is entitled to the mahr of her peers (mahr al-mithl). This ruling highlights a key principle: marriage is a robust contract that tolerates void conditions, unlike sale (bay') which is invalidated by them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? (marriage) What is the hukm? (valid/sahih)
The marriage is the primary contract; the condition is secondary.
2
Identify the condition
What condition is attached to the mahr? (accepting wine or pork as mahr)
The condition is part of the marriage contract specification.
3
Classify the condition
Is the condition valid or invalid? (fasid because wine/pork are not mal for a Muslim)
Fasid conditions are those that conflict with Islamic law.
4
Analyze the effect on the contract
Does the void condition invalidate the marriage? (No, because marriage is a strong contract; the condition is canceled)
Contrast with sale where void conditions invalidate the contract.
5
Determine the dower
What mahr is due? (mahr al-mithl, because the specified mahr is invalid)
The tassmiyah (naming of mahr) is not valid, so default mahr applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان تزوج مسلم على خمر او خنزير فالنکاح جائزو لها مهر مثلها لان شرط قبول الخمر شرط فاسد فيصح النكاح ويلغو الشرط بخلاف البيع لانه يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة لكن لم تصح التسمية لما ان المسمى ليس بمال في حق المسلم فوجب مهر المثل
ترجمہ . پس اگر نکاح کیا مسلمان نے شراب یا خنزیر پر تو نکاح جائز ہے اور عورت کیلئے اس کا ہر مشکل ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہ قبول خمر کی شرط ، شرط فاسد ہے تو نکاح صحیح ہے اور شرط لغو ہے بخلاف بیع کہ وہ شرط فاسد سے باطل ہو جاتی ہے لیکن تسمیہ صحیح نہیں ہوئی اسلئے کہ مسمی مسلمان کے حق میں مال نہیں ہے تو مہر مثل واجب ہوا۔
If a Muslim marries on [the condition of] wine or a pig, the marriage is valid and she gets her mahr al-mithl, because the condition of accepting wine is a void condition, so the marriage is valid and the condition is canceled, contrary to sale, because it is invalidated by void conditions. But the naming (tassmiyah) is not valid because the named item is not property (mal) with respect to a Muslim, so mahr al-mithl is due.
Translation: So if a Muslim married on wine or a pig, the marriage is valid and the woman is entitled to her mahr al-mithl. Because the condition of accepting wine is a void condition, so the marriage is valid and the condition is canceled, unlike sale which becomes invalid by void conditions. But the naming (tassmiyah) is not valid because the named item is not property in the right of a Muslim, so mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of Hidayah, followed by a brief commentary. The passage deals with the scenario where a Muslim husband stipulates wine or pork as the mahr (dower). The ruling is clear: the marriage is valid (jā'iz), but the condition is void (fasid), and the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the dower of her peers). The reasoning is twofold. First, the condition of accepting wine or pork is a void condition (shart fasid) because these items are not property (mal) for a Muslim—wine and pork are impure and forbidden to consume, so they cannot be considered valuable property in Islamic law. In contracts of exchange like sale (bay'), a void condition invalidates the entire contract, but marriage (nikah) is different: it is a strong contract ('aqd qawi) that is not easily invalidated by void conditions. Instead, the marriage remains valid and the condition is canceled (laghw). Second, because the named mahr is not valid property, the tassmiyah (specification of dower) is not valid, so the default mahr al-mithl applies. This ruling illustrates a key Hanafi principle: marriage is more resistant to invalidity than sale, aligning with the earlier discussion about marriage being based on leniency (samahah) versus sale's strictness. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah, as the text is directly from the matn of Hidayah.

Key Terms
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): A condition that is legally invalid but does not invalidate the primary contract in marriage; it is canceled (laghw) and the contract remains valid.
تسمیہ (tassmiyah): The act of naming or specifying the mahr (dower) in the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A Muslim man marries a woman with the condition that her mahr is a bottle of wine. According to the Hanafi school, the marriage is:
A) Invalid (batil) because wine is not permissible as property.
B) Valid but the condition is void, and the wife gets mahr al-mithl.
C) Valid only if she agrees to accept wine as mahr.
D) Considered a sale (bay') and thus invalid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a marriage contracted with a void condition regarding the dower remains valid; the condition is nullified and the wife receives mahr al-mithl, illustrating the strength of the marriage contract over void stipulations.

Ruling on Specifying a Garment or Measured/Weighed Item as Mahr
Ruling on dower specification with description levels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a garment is specified as mahr without description, with type only, and with detailed description, and differentiate between garments and fungible items in terms of the husband's option.

Core Idea
A garment as mahr gives the husband an option even with full description; fungible items require exact delivery if described.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi rulings on specifying a garment or a measured/weighed item as dower (mahr) in a marriage contract. The key distinction lies in whether the item is from the category of fungible goods (mithli) or unique goods (qimi). We will see how the husband's obligation changes based on the level of description provided, and why garments are treated differently from wheat or saffron.

Guided Path
1
Identify the item type and description level
Is the mahr a garment (qimi) or a measured/weighed item (mithli)? How much description is given: no type, type only, or type and description?
2
Apply the classification rule
For garments, even with full description, the husband has an option between the medium-quality garment and its value because garments are qimi. For mithli items, if only type is given, husband has option; if both type and description are given, husband must deliver exactly that item.
3
State the ruling for each scenario
For garment with no type: mahr al-mithl. For garment with type: valid tasmiya, husband has takhyir. For exaggerated description: same takhyir. For mithli with type only: husband has option. For mithli with type and description: no option, must give specified item.
4
Understand the ratio legis (illah)
The distinction is based on whether the item is from dhawaat al-amthal (fungibles) or dhawaat al-qiyam (unique items). Garments are qimi, so exact replacement is not possible; hence option. Described mithli items can be exactly specified, so no option.
5
Note the exceptional case
The passage notes that a described garment is only established in the dhimma in salam contracts (khilaf al-qiyas), not in marriage.

Source Text

كتاب النكاح
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم وكذا اذا بالغ فى وصف الثوب فى ظاهر الروية لانها ليست من ذوات الامثال وكذا اداسمى مكيلا اوموزوناو سمی جنسه دون صفته وان سمی جنسه و صفته لا يخيرلان الموصوف منها يثبت في الذمة
ثبوتا صحيحا
ترجمہ اور اگر نکاح کیا عورت سے ایسے کپڑے پر جس کا وصف بیان نہیں کیا گیا تو عورت کیلئے مہر مثل ہے اور مراد اس کی یہ ہے کہ ثوب کا ذکر تو کیا اور اس پر اضافہ نہیں کیا اور وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ یہ جہالت جنس ہے۔ کیونکہ کپڑے مختلف اجناس کے ہوتے ہیں اور اگر جنس بیان کی بایں طور کہ کہا ہروی ہے تو تسمیہ صحیح ہے اور شوہر کو اختیار دیا جائے گا اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ۔ اور ایسے ہی جب مبالغہ کیا کپڑے کے وصف میں ظاہر الروایۃ میں ۔ کیونکہ کپڑ ا ذوات الامثال میں سے نہیں ہے اور ایسے ہی جب ذکر کیا مکیلی یا موزونی چیز کا اور اس کی جنس بیان کی نہ کہ صفت اور اگر ذکر کیا اس کی جنس اور صفت کو تو شوہر کو اختیار نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ اسلئے کہ موصوف ان میں سے ثابت ہوتا ہے ذمہ میں ثبوت صحیح کے طور پر ۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نکاح میں کپڑے کو مہر بنایا لیکن کپڑے کا وصف ذکر نہیں کیا مثلاً یہ تو کہہ دیا کہ مہر میں کپڑا دوں گا۔ لیکن اس کی نوع بیان نہیں کی تو ایسی صورت میں ائمہ اربعہ کے نزدیک مہر مثل واجب ہوگا۔ وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں نوع مجہول ہے اسلئے کہ کپڑوں کی بہت سی انواع ہیں۔ مثلاً روئی کا، کستان کا ، ریشم کا۔ پس جہالت مسمی کی وجہ سے مہر مثل واجب ہوگا۔ اور اگر کپڑے کی نوع بیان کر دی مثلاً کہا کہ وہ ہر وی سوتی تھان کا ہوگا تو اب تسمیہ صحیح ہے اور شوہر کو قیمت اور اوسط درجہ کے ہروی کپڑے کے درمیان اختیار ہو گا۔ دلیل ماقبل میں گذر چکی اور اگر کپڑے کا وصف بیان کرنے میں مبالغہ کیا یعنی نوع بھی بیان کی گئی اور اس کا طول، عرض، موٹائی اور سانچہ بھی متعین کر دیا گیا تو اس صورت میں بھی شوہر کو وسط ثوب اور اس کی قیمت کے درمیان اختیار ہوگا۔ کیونکہ کپڑ اذوات الامثال میں سے نہیں ہے بلکہ ذوات القیم میں سے ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ کپڑا اگر ہلاک ہو گیا تو مضمون بالقیمہ ہو گا مضمون بالمثل نہیں ۔ اور اگر مہر کسی مکیلی چیز کو بنایا یا موزونی چیز کو اور اس کی نوع بیان کردی مثلاً ایک کر گندم یا ایک من زعفران کو مہر بنایا لیکن اس کی صفت بیان نہیں کی گئی تو اب بھی شوہر کو اوسط درجہ کے مسمی اور اس کی قیمت کے درمیان اختیار ہوگا۔ اور اگر نوع اور وصف دونوں بیان کر دیئے گئے تو اب شوہر پر مسمی واجب ہو گا۔ قیمت اور مسمی کے درمیان اختیار نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ مکیلات اور موزونات میں سے جس کا وصف بیان کر دیا گیا تو وہ ذمہ میں علی الاطلاق ثابت ہوتی ہے بیع سلم میں بھی اور اس کے علاوہ میں بھی اس کے برخلاف ثوب موصوف کہ وہ صرف بیع سلم میں ذمہ میں خلاف قیاس ثابت ہوتا ہے۔
Book of Marriage. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya Volume 4. And likewise if he exaggerated in describing the garment in Zahir al-Riwayah, because it is not from the category of items with counterparts (dhawaat al-amthal). And likewise if he named a measured or weighed item and specified its genus without its description. And if he specified its genus and description, he does not have the option (of choosing between the item and its value), because the described item from these becomes established in the dhimma with sound establishment. Translation: If marriage was contracted with a woman upon a garment whose description was not mentioned, the woman is entitled to mahr al-mithl. The meaning is that the garment was mentioned but nothing additional (like type) was specified. The reason is that this is ignorance of the genus, because garments are of different types. If the genus was mentioned, e.g., he said it is a Herati cloth, then the specification is valid, and the husband is given the option due to the proof we mentioned. Similarly, if he exaggerated in describing the garment in Zahir al-Riwayah, because the garment is not from dhawaat al-amthal. And similarly if he mentioned a measured or weighed item and specified its genus without its description. And if he mentioned its genus and description, then the husband is not given an option, because the described item from these is established in the dhimma with sound establishment. Commentary: The issue is that in marriage a garment is made as dower but its description is not mentioned, e.g., he said 'I will give a garment as dower' but did not specify its type. In this case, according to the four Imams, mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. The reason is that the type is unknown because there are many types of garments, e.g., cotton, [؟], silk. So due to ignorance of the named item, mahr al-mithl is obligatory. If he specified the type, e.g., he said it is a Herati cotton cloth, then the specification is valid, and the husband has the option between the value and the medium-quality Herati cloth. The proof has passed earlier. If he exaggerated in describing the garment, i.e., both the type and its length, width, thickness, and pattern were specified, then also the husband has the option between the medium garment and its value, because the garment is not from dhawaat al-amthal but from dhawaat al-qiyam. This is why if the garment is destroyed, it is guaranteed by value (damn bi'l-qima) not by replacement (damn bi'l-mithl). If the dower is made a measured item or a weighed item and its type is specified, e.g., one kurr of wheat or one mann of saffron, but its description is not mentioned, then also the husband has the option between the medium-grade named item and its value. If both type and description are mentioned, then the husband is obliged to give the named item; he does not have the option between value and the named item, because among measured and weighed items, once described, they are established in the dhimma unconditionally, in salam sale and otherwise. This is contrary to the described garment, which is established in the dhimma only in salam sale, contrary to analogy.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the ruling on specifying a garment or a measured/weighed item as dower (mahr) in marriage, with or without description. The author first presents the ruling: if the garment is mentioned without specifying its type (jins), the wife gets mahr al-mithl (the appropriate dower for her status) because the type is unknown (jahala fi al-jins). If the type is specified (e.g., Herati cloth), the specification is valid but the husband has the option to give either the specified item (of average quality) or its value, because garments are not fungible goods (dhawaat al-amthal). Even if the garment’s description is detailed (exaggerated) in Zahir al-Riwayah, the husband still has the option because a garment is valued by price (dhawaat al-qiyam), unlike wheat or other fungibles. For measured or weighed items (makilat/muzunat), if only the type is mentioned (e.g., wheat) without quality, again the husband has the option. But if both type and description are specified (e.g., high quality wheat), then the husband must deliver exactly that item; no option for value, because such items when described are established in the dhimma (legal liability) in all transactions, including salam. The passage contrasts this with a described garment, which is only established in the dhimma in salam sales, not in marriage, because that is an exception to the general rule (khilaf al-qiyas). The commentary elaborates with examples and reasons, confirming the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
ذوات الامثال (dhawaat al-amthal): Items that have counterparts or equivalents (mithliyat) – fungible goods that can be replaced by similar items in case of destruction.
مھر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The appropriate dower for the wife based on her social standing, family, beauty, etc., used when the specified dower is invalid.
تسمیہ (tasmiya): The act of naming or specifying the dower amount or item in the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Mahr al-mithl
C) The garment of his choice
D) No mahr

Key Takeaway
The key distinction is whether the item is fungible (mithli) or unique (qimi); this determines the husband's option to give the medium-quality item or its value.

Nikah — Marriage

Marriage with Invalid Dower: Hanafi vs. Maliki
Ruling on validity of marriage with wine or pig as dower; inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that a marriage with wine or pig as dower is valid, compare it with the Maliki position, and apply the distinction from sale.

Core Idea
A marriage with an invalid dower remains valid; only the dower condition fails.

What happens if a Muslim marries a woman and agrees to give her wine or a pig as her dower (mahr)? Does the marriage itself become invalid, or is only the dower affected? The Hanafi school, along with the Shafi'i and Hanbali schools, rules that the marriage is valid and the wife receives the appropriate dower (mahr al-mithl), while the condition to deliver wine or pig is void. The Maliki school, however, analogizes marriage to sale and deems the marriage void. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind the Hanafi position and its rebuttal of the Maliki analogy.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Begin by clearly stating the Hanafi ruling: the marriage contract is valid (sahih), the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl, and the condition to deliver wine or pig is void (batil).
Remember: 'sahih' means the contract produces all its legal effects; 'batil' means the condition produces no effect.
2
Identify the Maliki position and its proof
The Maliki school holds that the marriage is void (fasid), basing this on qiyas with sale. In sale, if the price is wine or pig, the sale is void; similarly, if the dower is such, the marriage should be void. Identify this argument.
The Hanafi response will challenge the analogy (qiyas) on the basis of a difference in the nature of the contract.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal to the Maliki qiyas
The Hanafi response distinguishes marriage from sale on two grounds: (1) In sale, void conditions involving riba are explicitly prohibited by the Quran, but no such prohibition applies to marriage; (2) Omission of dower does not invalidate marriage, so a fortiori a void condition does not invalidate it. Understand this refutation.
The principle 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' is not directly invoked, but the underlying idea is that marriage is not a pure exchange contract.
4
Understand the effect of invalid dower specification
The Hanafis argue that specifying wine or pig as dower is invalid because these items are not mal mutaqawwim for a Muslim. Therefore, it is as if no dower was specified, and mahr al-mithl becomes wajib. This is the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical outcome differs between the schools.
Mahr al-mithl is determined by the dower given to women similar to the wife in status.
5
Evaluate the tarjih and authority
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi and supported by the majority (Hanafi, Shafi'i, Hanbali). It comes from Zahir al-Riwayah. The Maliki position, though legitimate, is considered marjuh (weaker) in this context.
Knowing the authority weight helps in ifta: when giving fatwa, the mufti follows the mufta bihi position.

Source Text

رہی یہ بات کہ بیع شروط فاسدہ سے فاسد ہو جاتی ہے نکاح فاسد نہیں ہوتا تو ان دونوں میں وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ شرط فاسد بیع میں ربط ہے اور ربوا نص کتاب سے حرام ہے اور نکاح میں ربط ہی نہیں ہے لہذا شرط رکن عقد میں مؤثر نہیں ہوگی۔ پس رکن عقد درست رہے گا اور شرط لغو ہو جائے گی۔
If a Muslim marries upon wine or pig, the marriage is valid and she has mahr al-mithl, because the condition of accepting wine is a void condition; thus the marriage is valid and the condition is void, contrary to sale, because sale is invalidated by void conditions. However, the specification (tasmiya) is not valid because the named item is not property (mal) in the right of a Muslim, so mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. Translation: So if a Muslim married upon wine or pig, the marriage is valid and the woman gets mahr al-mithl. Because the condition of accepting wine is a void condition. Thus the marriage is valid and the condition is void, contrary to sale, because sale is invalidated by void conditions, but the specification is not valid because the named item is not property for a Muslim, so mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. Commentary: A Muslim man married a woman and fixed wine or pig as dower; according to Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Shafi'i, Imam Ahmad, the marriage is valid and mahr al-mithl is obligatory. According to Malik, the marriage is void. Malik likens marriage to sale: just as sale is void if wine or pig is made the price, similarly marriage becomes void if wine or pig is made dower. The proof of the three Imams is that when the husband said 'I married you upon wine', he imposed a condition of accepting wine, which is a void condition. It has already passed that marriage is not invalidated by void conditions; rather, the conditions themselves become void. Because a void condition is not worse than omitting specification altogether, and since omission of specification does not invalidate marriage, a void condition a fortiori does not invalidate marriage. At most, we can say that specification of wine and pig is not valid because they are not valuable property for a Muslim; and when specification is not valid, mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. Therefore in this case also mahr al-mithl is obligatory. The answer to Malik's analogy is that the condition for validity of specification is that the named item be property; when it is not, specification is void, and it is as if no dower was mentioned; and omission of dower does not invalidate marriage. In sale, the same reasoning applies: since wine and pig are not valuable property, specification is invalid, so it is as if no price was mentioned, and sale without a price is void. As for the difference that sale is invalidated by void conditions while marriage is not, the reason is that a void condition in sale involves riba which is explicitly forbidden by the Quran, whereas in marriage there is no such prohibited linkage; thus the condition does not affect the marriage contract; the pillar remains valid and the condition becomes void.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of marriage when wine (khamr) or pig (khinzir) is specified as dower (mahr). The Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Hanbali positions (the three Imams) state that the marriage is valid and the wife receives mahr al-mithl (the appropriate dower). The Maliki school holds that the marriage is void (fasid) because they analogize marriage to sale, where such conditions render the contract void. The passage explains the Hanafi reasoning: the condition to accept wine is a false condition (shart fasid), but marriage is not invalidated by false conditions; only the condition is void. The specification (tasmiya) fails because wine and pig are not valuable property (mal mutaqawwim) for a Muslim. Since no valid dower is specified, mahr al-mithl is due. The passage then distinguishes marriage from sale: in sale, a void condition (like involving riba) makes the sale void, but in marriage the condition does not affect the essence of the contract. This distinction is based on the different nature of the contracts. The commentary refutes Malik's qiyas by explaining that the absence of a valid dower does not invalidate marriage, just as omitting dower altogether does not invalidate it.

Key Terms
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): A condition that is invalid in Islamic law, such as a condition that is not in accordance with the objectives of the contract.
مال متقوم (mal mutaqawwim): Property that is legally valuable and permissible to transact, according to Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Marriage is valid and wife gets mahr al-mithl
C) Marriage is valid but the husband must give wine
D) Marriage is valid but must be renewed

Key Takeaway
When an invalid item is named as dower, the Hanafi school upholds the marriage while delivering the appropriate dower (mahr al-mithl), distinguishing marriage from sale where similar conditions would void the contract.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Dower on a Pointed Item That Turns Out Different
Dispute among three major Hanafi jurists on dower when the pointed item differs from the named item.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding dower when the designated specific item (by ishara) is found to be different, and explain the reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
When a pointed dower item turns out to be non-property, Abu Hanifa gives mahr al-mithl; Sahibayn give its like or value depending on genus.

Marriage is valid even if the dower specified by pointing turns out to be something else. But what dower is owed? This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani on whether the wife receives mahr al-mithl, the value of the intended item, or an equivalent of the intended item. The dispute hinges on whether the indication (ishara) or the verbal naming (tasmiya) determines the subject of the contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
There are two cases: (1) a jar of vinegar is indicated but turns out to be wine; (2) a slave is indicated but turns out to be free. Both involve a specific item designated by pointing (ishara) that is not as described.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifa rules mahr al-mithl in both cases. He argues that the indication (ishara) is stronger for identification, so the contract attaches to the actual pointed item (wine or free person), which cannot be valid dower, hence mahr al-mithl.
Ishara overrides tasmiya.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position and reasoning
Abu Yusuf gives the value of the intended property (or its like if fungible). He analogizes to destruction of the specified dower before delivery: the husband made her anticipate property and failed to deliver, so she gets its value.
In vinegar case, like weight of vinegar; in slave case, value of a slave.
4
State Muhammad's position and reasoning
Muhammad distinguishes by genus. If the named item (musamma) and indicated item (mushar ilayh) are the same genus (e.g., vinegar in a jar), the contract attaches to the indicated item, so she gets its like. If different genus (e.g., named a slave but found free), the contract attaches to the named item, which is not property, so mahr al-mithl.
Thus in vinegar case same genus → like weight; in slave case different genus → mahr al-mithl.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: In the vinegar case, Abu Hanifa gives mahr al-mithl; Sahibayn give equivalent weight of vinegar. In the slave case, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad give mahr al-mithl; Abu Yusuf gives the value of the slave.
The dispute shows how principles of identification affect the dower obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عورت سے ایک سرکے کے دن پر نکاح کیا، وہ اچانک شراب نکلا اور اگر غلام پر نکاح کیا وہ اچانک آزاد نکلا تو مہر مثل لازم ہے... اقوال فقہاء
فان تزوج امرأة على هذا الدن من الخل فاذا هو خمر فلها مهر مثلها عند ابي حنيفة وقالا لها مثل وزنه خلاوان تزوجها على هذا العبد فاذاهو حريجب مهر المثل عند ابي حنيفة و محمد وقال ابويوسف تجب القيمة لابي يوسف انه اطمعها مالا و عجز عن تسليمه فتجب قيمته او مثله ان كان من ذوات الامثال كما اذاهلک العبد المسمى قبل التسليم وابو حنيفة يقول اجتمعت الاشارة والتسمية فتعتبر الاشارة لكونها ابلغ في المقصود وهو التعريف فكانه تزوج على خمر اوحر ومحمد يقول الاصل ان المسمى اذا كان من جنس المشار اليه يتعلق العقد بالمشار اليه لان المسمى موجود في المشار ذاتا والوصف يتبعه وانكان من خلاف جنسه يتعلق بالمسمى لان المسمى مثل للمشاراليه وليس بتابع له والتسمية ابلغ في التعريف
We married a woman upon this jar of vinegar, and suddenly it turns out to be wine; then she gets mahr al-mithl according to Abu Hanifa, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said she gets the equivalent of its weight in vinegar. And if he married her upon this slave, and suddenly he is free, then mahr al-mithl is obligatory according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; and Abu Yusuf said the value (of the slave) becomes obligatory. Because Abu Yusuf says: he made her anticipate property and then was unable to deliver it, so its value or its like (if fungible) becomes obligatory, as when the specified slave dies before delivery. Abu Hanifa says: the indication (ishara) and the specification (tasmiya) are combined, so the indication is considered because it is more effective in the purpose (identification); thus it is as if he married upon wine or a free person. Muhammad says: The principle is that if the named item (musamma) is of the same genus as the indicated item (mushar ilayh), the contract is attached to the indicated item, because the named item exists in the indicated item in essence, and the description follows it. If it is of a different genus, then it is attached to the named item, because the named item is like a representation of the indicated item, not a follower, and the specification is more effective in identification.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a case where a specific object is designated as dower, but it turns out to be different from what was intended. Two scenarios: (1) A jar of vinegar turns out to be wine; (2) A slave turns out to be free. Abu Hanifa rules mahr al-mithl in both cases because the indication (ishara) points to the actual item, which is non-property (wine) or non-enslavable (free person), so the specification fails. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad initially say in the first case she gets the equivalent weight of vinegar (i.e., the intended item is vinegar, so she gets its like), but in the second case they differ: Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa that mahr al-mithl is due, because the named item (free person) is not property; meanwhile Abu Yusuf says she gets the value of the slave (had he been a slave). Abu Yusuf's reasoning: the husband made the wife anticipate property (by indicating the slave) and then failed to deliver, so she is entitled to the value of the object he indicated, similar to destruction of the specified item before delivery. Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the indication and specification together are considered, but the indication is stronger for identification; thus the contract is effectively for wine or a free person, which are not valid dower, so mahr al-mithl. Muhammad distinguishes: if the named item (musamma) and the indicated item (mushar ilayh) are of the same genus (e.g., vinegar in a jar), the contract attaches to the indicated item; if different genus (e.g., named a slave but found free), the contract attaches to the named item, which is not property, so mahr al-mithl. The passage highlights the principles of ishara (pointing) and tasmiya (naming) in determining the subject of a contract.

Key Terms
اشارہ (ishara): The act of pointing to a specific object to identify it as the subject of a contract, e.g., 'this jar'.
مسمی (musamma): The named or specified item, e.g., a slave that is verbally described or named.
مشار الیہ (mushar ilayh): The physical object pointed to, e.g., the jar or the actual person present.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a man marries a woman on a jar of vinegar that turns out to be wine, what is the wife entitled to?
A) Mahr al-mithl
B) The value of vinegar
C) The value of wine
D) The jar (as is)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when the indicated dower item differs from the named item, the indication may prevail, leading to mahr al-mithl if the indicated item is non-property; but the Sahibayn give value or like depending on the circumstance.
